Q1. Physical quantities are
    (A) quantities such as length, mass and time.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) quantities such as kilos, pounds and gallons.
    (C) quantities such as pounds, dollars and rupees.
    (D) quantities such as degrees, radians and steradians.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A physical quantity is a physical property of a phenomenon, body, or substance, that can be quantified by measurement. A physical quantity can be expressed as the combination of a magnitude expressed by a number ‚Äì usually a real number ‚Äì and a unit. All these given above can be expressed as explained so these are physical quantities.

Q2. Measurement of a physical quantity is essentially the
    (A) process of observing the physical quantity
    (B) process of comparing with a standard using an instrument   <-- CORRECT
    (C) process of taking readings on an instrument
    (D) process of subdividing the physical quantity
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The Measurement of a given quantity is essentially an act or result of comparison between a quantity whose magnitude (amount) is unknown, with a similar quantity whose magnitude (amount) is known, the latter quantity being called a Standard.

Q3. Fundamental or base quantities are arbitrary. In SI system these are ______, mass, time, electric current, thermodynamic temperature, amount of substance, and luminous intensity.
    (A) acceleration
    (B) force
    (C) length   <-- CORRECT
    (D) velocity
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A base quantity is chosen and arbitrarily defined, rather than being derived from a combination of other physical quantities. The 7 base quantities are:
 PHYSICAL QUANTITY
 BASE SI UNIT
 Mass (m)
 Kilogram (Kg)
 Length (ll)
 Metre (m)
 Time (t)
 Second (s)
 Current (II)
 Ampere (A)
 Temperature (T)
 Kelvin (K)
 Amount of sub. (n)
 Molar (mol)
 Luminous Intensity (L)
 Candela (cd

Q4. Unit for a fundamental physical quantity is
    (A) defined as average various reference standards
    (B) the smallest measurable value of the physical quantity
    (C) defined as best of various reference standards
    (D) reference standard for the given physical quantity   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Unit is the reference used as the standard measurement of a physical quantity. The unit in which the fundamental quantities are measured are called fundamental unit and the units used to measure derived quantities are called derived units.

Q5. In SI system the fundamental units are
    (A) meter, kilogram, second, coulomb, Kelvin, mole, candela and horse power
    (B) meter, kilogram, second, ampere, Kelvin, mole and candela   <-- CORRECT
    (C) meter, Newton, second, ampere, Kelvin, mole and candela
    (D) meter, kilogram, second, ampere, Kelvin, mole and watt
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The SI base units and their physical quantities are the metre for measurement of length, the kilogram for mass, the second for time, the ampere for electric current, the kelvin for temperature, the candela for luminous intensity, and the mole for amount of substance.

Q6. _________ are units of physical quantity that can be expressed as a combination of fundamental physical quantities.
    (A) Basic units
    (B) Derived units   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Simple units
    (D) Complex units
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Derived units are units which may be expressed in terms of base units by means of mathematical symbols of multiplication and division.

Q7. Joule is the SI unit of
    (A) acceleration
    (B) force
    (C) power
    (D) energy   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The joule (symbol J), is a derived unit of energy in the International System of Units. It is equal to the energy transferred to (or work done on) an object when a force of one newton acts on that object in the direction of its motion through a distance of one metre (1 newton metre or N‚ãÖm).

Q8. Newton is the SI unit of
    (A) work
    (B) force   <-- CORRECT
    (C) acceleration
    (D) power
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The newton is the SI unit for force; it is equal to the amount of net force required to accelerate a mass of one kilogram at a rate of one meter per second squared.

Q9. The least count of any measuring equipment is
    (A) the smallest quantity that can be measured using that instrument.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the smallest reading on the instrument.
    (C) the smallest effect in any instrument.
    (D) the smallest range in any instrument.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The smallest value that can be measured by the measuring instrument is called its least count. Measured values are good only up to this value. The least count error is the error associated with the resolution of the instrument.

Q10. Resolution is
    (A) a measure of the bias in the instrument
    (B) a measure of the functional errors
    (C) the smallest amount of input signal change that the instrument can detect reliably   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a measure of the systematic errors
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Resolution is the smallest amount of input signal change that the instrument can detect reliably.

Q11. If $\theta $ is the parallax angle of a planet at a distance 'D', when observed from two different positions on the Earth, separated by distance 'b', the expression for 'D' is
    (A) $\frac{\theta}{b}$
    (B) $\frac{2b}{\theta }$
    (C) $\frac{b}{\theta }$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{\theta}{2b}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Parallax Method of Measurement: Astronomers use an effect called parallax to measure distances to nearby stars. Parallax is the apparent displacement of an object because of a change in the observer's point of view.
To measure the distance D of a far away planet S by the parallax method, We observe it from two different positions (observatories) A and B on the Earth, separated by distance AB = b at the same time as shown in the given figure.
We measure the angle between the two directions along which the planet is viewed at these two points. The $\angle$ASB in the figure represented by symbol Œ∏ is called the parallax angle or parallactic angle.
As the planet is very far away, bD<<1 and therefore, Œ∏ is very small. Then we approximately take AB as an arc of length b of a circle with center at S and the distance D as the radius AS = BS so that AB = b = DŒ∏ where Œ∏ is in radians.
D = $\frac{b}{\theta} $

Q12. Absolute error of the measurement is
    (A) the difference between two individual measurements and their mean.
    (B) the difference between the individual measurement and the true value of the quantity.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the difference between the individual measurement and the true value of the quantity squared.
    (D) the difference between the individual measurement and the true value of the quantity cubed.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Absolute error is defined as the magnitude of difference between the actual and the individual values of any quantity in question.
Say we measure any given quantity for n number of times and a_1, a_2, a_3 ‚Ä¶.. a_ _n are the individual values, then arithmetic mean is given by:
a_ _ m =( [a_ 1+a_2+a_ 3+ ‚Ä¶.. + a_ n]/n)
Now absolute error formula as per definition will be:

Q13. The arithmetic mean of all the absolute errors $\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}$ is given by
    (A) $\Delta \mathrm{a}_{\text {mean }}=\frac{\left(\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_1\right|+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_2\right|+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_3\right|+\ldots+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_{\mathrm{n}}\right|\right)}{\mathrm{n}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $2 \Delta \mathrm{a}_{\text {mean }}=\frac{\left(\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_1\right|+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_2\right|+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_3\right|+\ldots+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_{\mathrm{n}}\right|\right)}{\mathrm{n}}$
    (C) $\Delta \mathrm{a}_{\text {mean }}=\frac{2\left(\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_1\right|+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_2\right|+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_3\right|+\ldots+\left|\Delta \mathrm{a}_{\mathrm{n}}\right|\right)}{\mathrm{n}}$
    (D) $\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}} = {\rm{ }}\left( {\left| {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{\rm{1}}}} \right| + \left| {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{\rm{2}}}} \right| + \left| {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{\rm{3}}}} \right| + ... + {\rm{ }}|\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{\rm{n}}}|} \right)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We know that mean is the average of all numbers. So mean of all the absolute errors $=\frac{\text { sum of all absolute errors }}{\text { number of errors }}$

Q14. The relative error is given by
    (A) Relative error = $\frac{\Delta a_{\text {mean }}}{1.2 a_{\text {mean }}}$
    (B) Relative error = $\frac{\Delta a_{\text {mean }}}{a_{\text {mean }}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Relative error = $\frac{\Delta a_{\text {mean }}}{2 a_{\text {mean }}}$
    (D) Relative error = $\frac{2 \Delta a_{\text {mean }}}{a_{\text {mean }}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Relative Error or fractional error: It is defined as the ration of mean absolute error to the mean value of the measured quantity.
$\delta a=\frac{\text { mean absolute value }}{\text { mean value }}$
Relative error = $\frac{\Delta a_{\text {mean }}}{a_{\text {mean }}}$

Q15. Percentage error Œ¥a is given by
    (A) $\delta {\rm{a }} = {\rm{ }}\left( {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}/{{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}} \right)$70$\% $
    (B) $\delta {\rm{a }} = {\rm{ }}\left( {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}/{{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}} \right)$ 80$\% $
    (C) $\delta {\rm{a }} = {\rm{ }}\left( {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}/{{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}} \right)$100$\% $   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\delta {\rm{a }} = {\rm{ }}\left( {\Delta {{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}/{{\rm{a}}_{{\rm{mean}}}}} \right)$ 200$\% $
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Percentage Error: It is the relative error measured in percentage.
So Percentage Error $\delta a ={ mean \ absolute\ value\over mean\ value} \times 100$%
$\delta a ={ Œîa_{mean}\over a_{mean}}\times 100$%

Q1. When two quantities are added or subtracted, the absolute error in the final result is
    (A) absolute value of the sum of errors of individual quantities
    (B) absolute value of the difference of errors of individual quantities
    (C) absolute value of the sum of individual quantities
    (D) the sum of the absolute errors in the individual quantities   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When two quantities are added or subtracted, the absolute error in the final result is the sum of the absolute errors in the individual quantities.
For e.g: error $‚àÜx$ in the sum x = a + b is $‚àÜx = \pm (‚àÜa+‚àÜb)$
Maximum value of error, $‚àÜx$ = $(‚àÜa+‚àÜb)$

Q2. When two quantities are multiplied or divided, the relative error in the result is
    (A) the sum of the absolute errors in the multipliers
    (B) the difference of the absolute errors in the multipliers
    (C) the difference of the relative errors in the multipliers
    (D) the sum of the relative errors in the multipliers   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When two quantities are multiplied or divided, the relative error in the result is the sum of the relative errors in the multipliers.
e.g x = a x b
Maximum possible error is: ${‚àÜx\over x} = \pm ({{‚àÜa\over a} + {‚àÜb\over b}})$
Similarly, for error in quotient: x = $a\over b$
Maximum possible error is: ${‚àÜx\over x} = \pm ({{‚àÜa\over a} + {‚àÜb\over b}}) $

Q3. The relative error in a physical quantity raised to the power k is
    (A) (k ‚Äì 1) times the relative error in the individual quantity
    (B) k times the absolute error in the individual quantity
    (C) k times the relative error in the individual quantity.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (k ‚Äì 1) times the absolute error in the individual quantity
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The relative error in a physical quantity raised to a power k is the k times the relative error in the individual quantity.
for e.g. $x = {a^n\over b^m}$
Maximun relative error, ${‚àÜx\over x} = \pm ({n{‚àÜa\over a}+m{‚àÜb\over b}})$

Q4. The significant figures of a number are those digits that
    (A) carry meaning contributing to its measurement resolution.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) are all non zero digits.
    (C) are at even positions after decimal.
    (D) are at odd positions after decimal.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The significant figures of a number are digits that carry meaning contributing to its measurement resolution. This includes all digits except:
 All leading zeros;
 Trailing zeros when they are merely placeholders to indicate the scale of the number (exact rules are explained at identifying significant figures); and
 Spurious digits introduced, for example, by calculations carried out to greater precision than that of the original data, or measurements reported to a greater precision than the equipment supports.

Q5. The power (or exponent) to which the base quantities are raised to represent that quantity is called
    (A) dimension.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) combination.
    (C) conversion.
    (D) measurement.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The dimension of the units of a derived physical quantity may be defined as the number of times the fundamental units of mass, length and time appear in the physical quantity.

Q6. According to the principle of homogeneity of dimensions, we can add or subtract
    (A) similar physical quantities.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) any physical quantities.
    (C) different physical quantities.
    (D) chemical physical quantities.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: It would be more exact to say that "Quantities with the same units can be added and subtracted with no problem." Quantities with the same dimensions can often be added and subtracted as long as the units are correctly converted.

Q7. In an equation, the dimensions of the LHS and RHS of the equation are the same. The equation is
    (A) dimensionally inconsistent.
    (B) dimensionally consistent.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) none of these.
    (D) not possible.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Principle of homogenity of dimensions states that ‚ÄúFor an equation to be dimansionally correct, the dimensions of each term on LHS must be equal to the dimensions of each term on RHS.‚Äù

Q8. The dimensional formula for Planck‚Äôs constant is
    (A) [MLT]
    (B) [ML^2T^-1]   <-- CORRECT
    (C) [M^2L^2T^-1]
    (D) [ML^1T^-1]
    Answer: B
    Explanation: [ML^2T^-1] (Hint use E = hŒΩ)

Q9. A dimensionally consistent equation
    (A) is always correct.
    (B) is necessarily correct.
    (C) is nearly correct.
    (D) is not necessarily correct.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If an equation fails this consistency test, it is proved wrong, but if it passes, it is not proved right. Thus, a dimensionally correct equation need not be actually an exact (correct) equation, but a dimensionally wrong (incorrect) or inconsistent equation is definitely wrong.

Q10. Electric charge is expressed in SI units as
    (A) Real unit
    (B) a base unit
    (C) derived unit   <-- CORRECT
    (D) complex unit
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The SI derived unit of electric charge is the coulomb (C). The symbol Q often denotes charge.

Q11. The units of pressure are the same as the units of _______.
    (A) elasticity
    (B) strain
    (C) plasticity
    (D) stress   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Pressure is not the same physical thing as stress, but they do use the same definition and thus produce the same units, so the same calculation can be used for both. They both measure force per unit area. The SI unit of both pressure and stress is Pascal.

Q12. The volume of a cube of side 2 cm is equal (in ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{3}}}$) to
    (A) 0.008
    (B) 0.0008
    (C) $8.0 \times {10^{ - 6}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.08
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Side of cube (a) = 2 cm = $2\times 10^{-2}m$
Volume of cube (V) = $a^3 = (2\times 10^{-2})^3$ = $8.0 \times 10^{-6}m^3$

Q13. The surface area of a solid cylinder of radius 2.0 cm and height 10.0 cm (in ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$) is equal to
    (A) 15
    (B) 150
    (C) $1.5 \times {10^4}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1500
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Radius of cylinder r = 2 cm = 20 mm
Height of cylinder h = 10 cm = 100 mm
Surface area of cylinder = $2\pi r(r+h)$
= $2\times 3.14 \times 20 (20+100)$ 
= $2\times 3.14 \times 20 \times 120 $
= 15072 mm^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 $\approx 1.5\times 10^4 mm^2$

Q14. How many meters does a vehicle moving with a speed of 18 km ${{\rm{h}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ covers in 1 s
    (A) 4.5
    (B) 5.0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6
    (D) 4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Speed of vehicle = 18 km h^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã-1
Mean it cover 18 km in 1 hour {3600 seconds)
Distance covered in 3600 sec = 18km = 18000 m
Distance covered in 1 sec = ${18000\over 3600 }= 5m$

Q15. The relative density of lead is 11.3. Its density in g ${\rm{c}}{{\rm{m}}^{ - {\rm{3}}}}$ is
    (A) 113
    (B) 11.3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.13
    (D) 1130
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Relative density means how much times a substance is denser than water.
Now relative density of lead = 11.3 means lead is 11.3 times denser than water.
Now water has a density 1 g cm^‚Äì3 in cgs units
Thus lead will have a density = 11.3 x 1 g cm^‚Äì3 = 11.3 g cm^‚Äì3

Q1. How many g ${\rm{c}}{{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ does 1 kg ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ equal?
    (A) ${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{7}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{8}}}$
    (C) ${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{5}}}$
    (D) ${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{3}}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We know 1 kg = 10^3 g
1 m^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 = 10^4 cm^2
1 s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã-2 = 1s^-2
Multiply all these quantities we get
$\Rightarrow$ 1 kg m^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã-2 = $10^3\times 10^4 gcm^2s^{-2}$
$\Rightarrow 1kgm^2s^{-2}= 10^7 gcm^2s^{-2}$

Q2. Approximately how many light years is a meter?
    (A) ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{1}}0}}$
    (B) ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{1}}2}}$
    (C) ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{16}}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{1}}1}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A light-year is a unit of distance. It is the distance that light can travel in one year. Light moves at a velocity of about 300,000 kilometers (km) each second. So in one year, it can travel about 10 trillion km. More precisely, one light-year is equal to $9.5\times 10^{15}m$.
$\Rightarrow$ 1 Light Year = $9.5\times 10^{15}m $
$\Rightarrow$ 1 m = ${1\over 9.5\times 10^{15} } Light\ year $
$\Rightarrow 1 m \approx 10^{-16}Light \ year $

Q3. Approximately how many km ${{\rm{h}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ is 3 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ ?
    (A) 3.5$ \times $${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{4}}}$
    (B) 3.9$ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{3}}}$
    (C) 3.9 $ \times $${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{4}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3.6$ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{\rm{4}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 1 km h^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã-2 = ${1000m\over 3600\times 3600 \;s^2} = {1\over 360\times 36}ms^{-2}$
$\Rightarrow$ $1ms^{-2} = 360\times 36 km\ h^{-2}$
$\Rightarrow$ $3ms^{-2} =3\times 360\times 36 km\ h^{-2}$
$\Rightarrow$ $3ms^{-2}= 38880km\ h^{-2} $
$\Rightarrow 3ms^{-2} \approx 3.9\times 10^4 km \ h^{-2}$

Q4. The value of G is = 6.67 √ó ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{11}}}}$ N ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}{\left( {{\rm{kg}}} \right)^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$. The value of G in ${\left( {{\rm{cm}}} \right)^{\rm{3}}}{{\rm{s}}^{-{\rm{2}}}}{{\rm{g}}^{-{\rm{1}}}}$ is
    (A) 6.67 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{8}}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 6.67 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{12}}}}$
    (C) 6.67 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{10}}}}$
    (D) 6.67 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{ - {\rm{9}}}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: In MKS units G = $6.67\times 10^{-11} Nm^2/kg^2$
1 N = $kgm/s^2$ =$1000g\times 100cm/s^2$= $10^5 gcm/s^2$
$1m^2=10^4 cm^2$
 $1kg^2=10^6g^2 $
$\therefore$G = $6.67\times 10^{-11}\times 10^5\times 10^4\over 10^6$ = $6.67\times 10^{-8}$

Q5. A new unit of length is chosen such that the speed of light in vacuum is unity. What is the distance between the Sun and the Earth in terms of the new unit if light takes 8 min and 20 s to cover this distance?
    (A) 500   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 600
    (C) 550
    (D) 450
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Distance between the Sun and the Earth $=$ Speed of light $\times$ Time taken by light to cover the distance
It is given that in the new unit system, speed of light = 1 unit.
Time taken, t = 8 min 20 s = 500 s
Theref‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äãore, Distance between the Sun and the Earth = 1 x 500 = 500 new units of length

Q6. Which of the following is the most precise device for measuring length?
    (A) A vernier callipers with 20 divisions on the sliding scale.
    (B) A screw gauge of pitch 1 mm and 100 divisions on the circular scale.
    (C) All instruments have same precision.
    (D) An optical instrument that can measure length to within a wavelength of light.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: An optical instrument that can measure length to within a wavelength of light.

Q7. A student measures the thickness of a human hair by looking at it through a microscope of magnification 100. He makes 20 observations and finds that the average width of the hair in the field of view of the microscope is 3.5 mm. What is the estimate on the thickness of hair ?
    (A) 0.035 mm   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.025 mm
    (C) 0.040 mm
    (D) 0.030 mm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Magnification of microscope = 100
Observed width of the hair = 3.5 mm
Estimate on the thickness of hair is given by
Magnification = $Observed \ width \over Real \ width $
Real width = $Observed\ width \over Magnification $= $3.5 \over 100$ = 0.035 mm

Q8. The photograph of a house occupies an area of 1.75 ${\rm{c}}{{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$ on a 35 mm slide. The slide is projected on to a screen, and the area of the house on the screen is 1.55 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$ . What is the linear magnification of the projector-screen arrangement?
    (A) 90.2
    (B) 88.4
    (C) 94.1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 84.1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Area of the house on the slide = 1.75 cm^‚Äã‚Äã2
Area of the image of the house formed on the screen = 1.55 m^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 = 1.55 √ó 10^4 cm^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Arial magnification, m_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äãa = $Area \ of \ image\over area \ of \ object $ = ${1.55\times 10^4\over 1.75}$= 8857
Linear magnification, m_$l$ = $\sqrt{a_m}= \sqrt{8857}$ = 94.1

Q9. The number of significant digits in 0.007 is
    (A) 2
    (B) 4
    (C) 3
    (D) 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There are three rules on determining how many significant figures are in a number: 
 Non-zero digits are always significant.
 Any zeros between two significant digits are significant.
 A final zero or trailing zeros in the decimal portion ONLY are significant.
So keeping these rules in mind, there are 1 significant digit.

    (D) 2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: There are three rules on determining how many significant figures are in a number:

So keeping these rules in mind, there are 3 significant digits.

 A final zero or trailing zeros in the decimal portion ONLY are significant.

Q14. The number of significant digits in 0.0006032 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$ is
    (A) 5
    (B) 3
    (C) 6
    (D) 4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: There are three rules on determining how many significant figures are in a number: 
 Non-zero digits are always significant.
 Any zeros between two significant digits are significant.
 A final zero or trailing zeros in the decimal portion ONLY are significant.
So keeping these rules in mind, there are 4 significant digits.

Q15. The mass of a box measured by a grocer's balance is 2.300 kg. Two gold pieces of masses 20.15 g and 20.17 g are added to the box. What is the total mass of the box and the difference in the masses of the pieces to correct significant figures?
    (A) 2.5 kg, 0.02 g
    (B) 2.5 kg, 0.05 g
    (C) 2.3 kg, 0.03 g
    (D) 2.3 kg, 0.02 g   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Total mass = 2.3 kg + 0.02015 kg + 0.02017 kg = 2.34032 kg = 2.3 kg
Difference of mass of the gold pieces = 20.17 g - 20.15 g = 0.02 g

Q1. The length, breadth and thickness of a rectangular sheet of metal are 4.234 m, 1.005 m, and 2.01 cm respectively. Give the area of the sheet to correct significant figures.
    (A) 8.8 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$
    (B) 8.7221 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$
    (C) 8.722 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$
    (D) 8.72 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Length of sheet is given by, l = 4.234 m
Breadth of sheet is given by, b = 1.005 m
Thickness of sheet is given by, t = 2.01 cm = 2.01 √ó 10^-2 m
Area of the sheet = 2 (l √ó b + b √ó t + t √ó l) = 2 (4.234 √ó 1.005 + 1.005 √ó 0.0201 + 0.0201 √ó 4.234) = 2 (4.3604739) = 8.7209478 m^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 
As area can contain a maximum of three significant digits, therefore, on rounding off, we get area = 8.72 m^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2

Q2. The length, breadth and thickness of a rectangular sheet of metal are 4.234 m, 1.005 m, and 2.01 cm respectively. Give the volume of the sheet to correct significant figures.
    (A) 0.1855 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{3}}}$
    (B) 0.08552 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{3}}}$
    (C) 0.0755 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{3}}}$
    (D) 0.0855 ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{3}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: length of sheet, l = 4.234 m
breadth of sheet, b = 1.005 m
thickness of sheet, t = 2.01 cm = 2.01 √ó 10^-2 m
volume = l √ó b √ó t
$\Rightarrow$ V = 4.234 √ó 1.005 √ó 0.0201 = 0.0855289 = 0.0855 m^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã3 (This number has only 3 significant figures i.e., 8, 5, and 5)

Q3. A physical quantity P is related to four observables a, b, c and d as follows : $P = \frac{a^3 b^2}{\sqrt{c} d}$. The percentage errors of measurement in a, b, c and d are 1$\% $, 3$\% $, 4$\% $ and 2$\% $, respectively. What is the percentage error in the quantity P?
    (A) 13$\% $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 12$\% $
    (C) 15$\% $
    (D) 11$\% $
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Given that, P = $\frac {a^3b^2}{ \sqrt c \ d}$
Maximum fractional error in P is given by 
$\frac{\Delta P}{P}= \pm\left(3 \frac{\Delta a}{a}+2 \frac{\Delta b}{b}+\frac{1}{2} \frac{\Delta c}{c}+\frac{\Delta d}{d}\right)$
$\Rightarrow \frac{\Delta P}{P}= \pm\left(3 \frac{1}{100}+2 \frac{3}{100}+\frac{1}{2} \frac{4}{100}+\frac{2}{100}\right)$ $\Rightarrow \frac{\Delta P}{P}= \pm 0.13$
Percentage error in P is given by= $\frac{\Delta P}{P} \times 100=0.13 \times 100$ = 13%

Q4. A physical quantity P is related to four observables a, b, c and d as follows: $P=\frac{a^3 b^2}{\sqrt{c} d}$. The percentage errors of measurement in a, b, c and d are 1$\% $, 3$\% $, 4$\% $ and 2$\% $, respectively. If the value of P calculated using the above relation turns out to be 3.763, to what value should you round off the result?
    (A) 3.76
    (B) 4.0
    (C) 3.71
    (D) 3.8   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Value of P is given as 3.763.
By rounding off the given value to the first decimal place, we get
P = 3.8

Q5. A book with many printing errors contains four different formulas for the displacement y of a particle undergoing a certain periodic motion. Choose the correct formula
    (A) y = (a/T) sin t/a
    (B) y = a sin 2$\pi $t
    (C) y = a sin vt
    (D) y = a sin $\frac{2\pi t}{T}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Dimension of y is given by = M^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã0 L^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1 T^0
Dimension of a is given by = M^0L^‚Äã‚Äã1T^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã0 
Dimension of $sin\frac{2\pi t}{T}$= $M^0L^0T^0$
Dimension of L.H.S = Dimension of R.H.S. Hence, the given formula is dimensionally correct.

Q6. The unit of length convenient on the atomic scale is known as an angstrom and is denoted by ${\mathop A\limits^0}:{\rm{ 1 }}{\mathop A\limits^0}{\rm{ }} = {\rm{ 1}}{0^{ - {\rm{1}}0}}$ m. The size of a hydrogen atom is about $0.{\rm{5 }}{\mathop A\limits^0}$ . What is the total atomic volume in ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{3}}}$ of a mole of hydrogen atoms ?
    (A) $ \cong 3.2 \times {10^{ - 6}}{m^3}$
    (B) $ \cong 3 \times {10^{ - 7}}{m^3}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $ \cong 3.3 \times {10^{ - 7}}{m^3}$
    (D) $ \cong 2.9 \times {10^{ - 6}}{m^3}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Radius of hydrogen atom, r = 0.5 √Ö = 0.5 √ó 10^-10 m
Volume of hydrogen atom is given by = (4/3) $\pi$ r^3
= (4/3) √ó (22/7) √ó (0.5 √ó 10^-10)^3
= 0.524 √ó 10^-30 m^3
1 mole of hydrogen contains 6.023 √ó 10^23 hydrogen atoms.
‚à¥ Volume of 1 mole of hydrogen atoms is given by = 6.023 √ó 10^23 √ó 0.524 √ó 10^‚Äì30
= 3.16 √ó 10^‚Äì7 m^3
$\approx 3\times 10^{-7} m^3$

Q7. One mole of an ideal gas at standard temperature and pressure occupies 22.4 L (molar volume). What is the ratio of molar volume to the atomic volume of a mole of hydrogen? (Take the size of hydrogen molecule to be about 1 √Ö).
    (A) $ \cong {10^4}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $ \cong {10^2}$
    (C) $ \cong {10^3}$
    (D) $ \cong {10^5}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Radius of hydrogen atom, r = 0.5 = 0.5 √ó 10^‚Äì10 m
Volume of hydrogen atom = ${4\over 3} \times {22\over 7} \times (0.5\times 10^{-10})^3$
= $0.524\times 10^{-30}m^3$
Now, 1 mole of hydrogen contains 6.023 √ó 10^23 hydrogen atoms.
Volume of 1 mole of hydrogen atoms, V_a = 6.023 √ó 10^23 √ó 0.524 √ó 10^‚Äì30
= 3.16 √ó 10^‚Äì7 m^3
Molar volume of 1 mole of hydrogen atoms at STP,
V_m = 22.4 L = 22.4 √ó 10^‚Äì3 m^3
$\Rightarrow$ ${V_m\over V_a}= {22.4\times 10^{-3}\over 3.16\times 10^{-7}}$= 7.08 $\times 10^{4}$
= $\cong 10^{4}$

Q8. Which of the following systems of units is not based on units of mass, length and time alone?
    (A) CGS
    (B) FPS
    (C) SI   <-- CORRECT
    (D) MKS

    Explanation: SI

Q9. The magnetic moment has the dimensions of
    (A) [LA]
    (B) [L^2T^-1A]
    (C) [LT^-1A]
    (D) [L^2A]   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The SI unit of magnetic moment is Am^2. Therefore, its dimensions are [L^2 A]

Q10. Surface tension has the same dimensions as that of:
    (A) Momentum
    (B) Cofficient of viscosity
    (C) Spring constant   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Impulse
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Surface tension = $\frac{Force}{Length}$
= $\frac{[MLT^{-2}]}{[L]}$ = [ML^0T^-2]
Spring constant = $\frac{Force}{Length}$
= $\frac{[MLT^{-2}]}{[L]}$ = [ML^0 T^-2]

Q11. When the planet Jupiter is at a distance of 824.7 million kilometers from the Earth, its angular diameter is measured to be 35.72‚Äù of arc. Calculate the diameter of Jupiter.
    (A) $1.429 \times {10^5}km$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $1.321 \times {10^7}km$
    (C) $2.523 \times {10^5}km$
    (D) $3.632 \times {10^5}km$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Distance of Jupiter from the Earth, D = 824.7 √ó 10^6 km
Angular diameter = 35.72‚Äú = 35.72 √ó 4.874 √ó 10^-6 rad
Diameter of Jupiter = d
Using the relation, Œ∏ = $d\over D$
d = Œ∏$\times$ D = 824.7 √ó 10^6 √ó 35.72 √ó 4.872 √ó 10^-6 $\cong 1.429\times 10^5 km$

Q12. The dimensions of impulse are equal to that of
    (A) angular momentum
    (B) force
    (C) linear momentum   <-- CORRECT
    (D) pressure
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Same dimensions as linear momentum.

Q13. Horse power is unit of
    (A) Time
    (B) Power   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Distance
    (D) Current
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The horsepower (hp) is a unit in the foot-pound-second ( fps ) or English system. A power level of 1 hp is approximately equivalent to 746 watt.

Q14. Which of the following quantities measured from different inertial reference frames are same?
    (A) Displacement
    (B) Force
    (C) Kinetic energy   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Velocity
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In an inertial frame, an object or body accelerates only when a physical force is applied and in the absence of a net force, a body at rest will remain at rest and a body in motion will continue to more uniformly. Kinetic energy measured from different inertial frame gives the same value, while the other three being vector quantities their values vary.

Q15. The significant digits in 0.000532 are
    (A) 2, 3
    (B) 5, 3, 2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0,5,3,2
    (D) 5, 3
    Answer: B
    Explanation: There are three rules on determining how many significant figures are in a number: 
 Non-zero digits are always significant.
 Any zeros between two significant digits are significant.
 A final zero or trailing zeros in the decimal portion ONLY are significant.
Keeping these rules in mind, we can say that only 5,3,2 are significant digits.

Q10. Population of a town is reported as 157,900. Which of the following statements is correct?
    (A) the population is 157900$ \pm $25
    (B) the population is 157900$ \pm $20
    (C) the population is 157900$ \pm $50   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the population is 157900$ \pm $100
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 157900 implies that the population is believed to be within the range of about 157850 to about 157950. In other words, the population is 157900¬±50. The ‚Äúplus-or-minus 50‚Äù appended to this number means that we consider the absolute uncertainty of the population measurement to be 50 ‚Äì (‚Äì50) = 100. We can also say that the relative uncertainty is 100/157900, which we can also express as 1 part in 1579, or 1/1579 = 0.000633, or about 0.06 percent.

Q11. Population of a town is reported as 158000. Which of the following statements is correct?
    (A) the population is 158000$ \pm $250
    (B) the population is 158000$ \pm $300
    (C) the population is 158000$ \pm $400
    (D) the population is 158000$ \pm $500   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The value 158000 implies that the population is likely between about 157500 and 158500, or 158000¬±500. The absolute uncertainty of 1000 translates into a relative uncertainty of $1000\over 158000$ or 1 part in 158, or about 0.6 percent.

Q12. The surface tension of a liquid is 70 dyne/cm. In MKS system its value is?
    (A) 7 ‚úï 10^2 N/m
    (B) 70 N/m
    (C) 7 ‚úï 10^3 N/m
    (D) 7 ‚úï 10^-2 N/m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $1 dyne = 10^{-5}\;N$
$1 cm =10^{-2}\;m$ hence its value in MKS is given by :-
$70 dyne/cm= 70 \times \large\frac{10^{-5}}{10^{-2}}$ = 7 ‚úï 10^-2 N/m

Q13. The result of rounding off 34.216 to 3 digits is
    (A) 342
    (B) 34.22
    (C) 34.2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3.42
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The rules for rounding off are following. 
 If the first non-significant digit is less than 5, then the least significant digit remains unchanged.
 If the first non-significant digit is greater than 5, the least significant digit is incremented by 1.
 If the first non-significant digit is 5, the least significant digit can either be incremented or left unchanged.
 All non-significant digits are removed.
So rounding off 34.216 upto 4 digits is 34.22 and upto 3 digits is 34.2

Q14. Dimensional analysis can be used to
    (A) deducing relations among the physical quantities.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) check the order of an equation.
    (C) check the validity of an equation.
    (D) to check integration of the equation.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Dimensional analysis is also used to deduce the relation between two or more physical quantities. If we know the degree of dependence of a physical quantity on another, that is the degree to which one quantity changes with the change in another, we can use the principle of consistency of two expressions to find the equation relating these two quantities.

Q15. An object has a length of 0.42 cm. Which of the following statements is correct?
    (A) the uncertainty in the length is 0.05
    (B) the uncertainty in the length is $ \pm $0.01
    (C) the uncertainty in the length is about 4$\% $
    (D) the uncertainty in the length is 0.01   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Suppose, you are simply told that an object has a measured length with no indication of its precision as in the question.
In this case, all you have to go on is the number of digits contained in the data. Thus the quantity ‚Äú0.42 cm‚Äù is specified to 0.01.
So the uncertainty in the length is 0.01.

# Motion in A Straight Line  (5 tests)

Motion in a Straight Line Test 01  (id 537) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Physics > Motion in A Straight Line

Q1. The position of an object moving in a straight line can be specified with reference to
    (A) a triangle
    (B) an arbitrary star
    (C) another straight line
    (D) a conveniently chosen origin   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: To describe motion along a straight line, we can choose an axis, say X-axis, so that it coincides with the path of the object. We then measure the position of the object with reference to a conveniently chosen origin, say O. Positions to the right of O are taken as positive and to the left of O, as negative.

Q2. For motion in a straight line
    (A) motion towards origin is positive
    (B) position to the left of the origin is taken as positive and to the right as negative.
    (C) motion away from origin is positive
    (D) position to the right of the origin is taken as positive and to the left as negative.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: To describe motion along a straight line, we can choose any axis, let us consider X-axis, so that it coincides with the path of the object. We then measure the position of the object with reference to a origin, say O. Positions to the right of O are taken as positive and to the left of O, as negative.

Q3. Path length is defined as
    (A) distance from origin to origin.
    (B) the distance from origin to maximum point.
    (C) the total length of the path traversed by an object.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the distance from origin to minimum point.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The path length is defined as the total length of the path traversed by an object. Unlike displacement, which is the shortest distance between two points, the path length is the total distance travelled, regardless of where it travelled.

Q4. Path length is a________________.
    (A) tensor
    (B) derived unit
    (C) scalar   <-- CORRECT
    (D) vector
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Path length has no particular direction and it depends upon the path chosen to reach the destination, so it is scaler.

Q5. In Kinematics we study ways to
    (A) describe motion without going into the causes of motion.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) find jerk without going into the causes of motion.
    (C) find acceleration without going into the causes of motion.
    (D) find velocity without going into the causes of motion.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Kinematics is a branch of classical mechanics that describes the motion of points, bodies (objects), and systems of bodies (groups of objects) without considering the mass of each or the forces that caused the motion.

Q6. For motion in 3 dimensions we need
    (A) frame of reference consisting of a clock and a Cartesian system having two mutually $\perp$ axes (X and Y)
    (B) frame of reference consisting of a clock and a Cartesian system having three mutually $\perp$ axes, (X,Y, and Z)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) No frame of reference is required a single point will do.
    (D) No frame of reference is required ; a set of 3 points will do.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Motion is a change in position of an object with time. In order to specify the position, we need to use a reference point and a set of axes. It is convenient to choose a rectangular coordinate system consisting of three mutually perpendicular axes, labelled X-, Y-, and Z- axes.
The point of intersection of these three axes is called origin (O) and serves as the reference point. The coordinates (x, y. z) of an object describe the position of the object with respect to this coordinate system.
To measure time, we position a clock in this system. This coordinate system along with a clock constitutes a frame of reference.

Q7. For one-dimensional motion displacement is the change in position and is given by
    (A) $\Delta {\rm{x }} = {\rm{ }}{{\rm{x}}_{\rm{2}}} - {\rm{ }}{{\rm{x}}_{\rm{1}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\Delta {\rm{x }} = {\rm{ }}{{\rm{x}}_{\rm{2}}} + {\rm{ }}{{\rm{x}}_{\rm{1}}}$
    (C) $\Delta {\rm{x }} = \left( {{\rm{ }}{{\rm{x}}_{\rm{2}}} + {\rm{ }}{{\rm{x}}_{\rm{1}}}} \right)/{\rm{2}}$
    (D) $‚àÜx = 2(x_2+x_1)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Displacement is defined to be the change in position of an object. It can be defined mathematically with the following equation:
$Displacement = ‚àÜx = x_2-x_1$
where $x_2$ refers to the value of the final position, $x_1 \ \ $refers to the value of the initial position and $‚àÜx$ is the symbol used to represent displacement.

Q8. Displacement is a
    (A) Vector   <-- CORRECT
    (B) tensor
    (C) scalar
    (D) Hector
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Displacement vector is a vector which gives the position of a point with reference to a point other than the origin of the coordinate system.

Q9. An object is said to be in uniform motion in a straight line if its displacement
    (A) is equal in equal intervals of time.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) is increasing in equal intervals of time.
    (C) is equal in not equal intervals of time.
    (D) is decreasing in equal intervals of time.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Uniform motion is the kind of motion in which a body covers equal displacement in equal intervals of time. It does
not matter how small the time intervals are, as long as the displacements covered are equal. If a body is involved in rectilinear motion and the motion is uniform, then the acceleration of the body must be zero.

Q10. The change in position or displacement ($\Delta {\rm{x}}$) divided by the time intervals ($\Delta {\rm{t}}$), in which the displacement occurs is known as
    (A) average acceleration
    (B) acceleration
    (C) average velocity   <-- CORRECT
    (D) speed
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Average velocity is the displacement of an object, divided by the time it took to cover that distance.
$V_{average}= {‚àÜx\over ‚àÜt}$
Displacement is the straight line distance between the starting point and ending point of an object's motion.
Velocity is referred to as a vector quantity because it has both magnitude and direction.

Q11. Average speed is defined as the total path length travelled divided by the total time interval during which
    (A) maximum motion has taken place.
    (B) uniform motion has taken place.
    (C) the motion has taken place.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) minimum motion has taken place.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The average speed is the ratio of distance traveled to the time spent. Average speed is defined as the total path length travelled divided by the total time interval during which the motion has taken place.

Q12. Average speed is
    (A) always negative
    (B) never positive
    (C) always zero
    (D) always positive   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Average speed is the total distance traveled divided by the elapsed time. Average speed is the absolute value of the average velocity or the magnitude of the velocity. Therefore, average Speed is always positive.

Q13. Instantaneous velocity or simply velocity v at an instant t equals
    (A) $\mathop {\lim }\limits_{{\rm{t}} \to 0} \frac{{\Delta x}}{{2\Delta t}}$
    (B) $\mathop {\lim }\limits_{{\rm{t}} \to 1} \frac{{\Delta x}}{{\Delta t}}$
    (C) $\mathop {\lim }\limits_{{\rm{t}} \to \infty } \frac{{\Delta x}}{ {\Delta t}}$
    (D) $\mathop {\lim }\limits_{{\rm{t}} \to 0} \frac{{\Delta x}}{{\Delta t}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Instantaneous velocity is the velocity of an object in motion at a specific point in time. This is determined similarly to average velocity, but we narrow the period of time so that it approaches zero. The formula for instantaneous velocity is the limit as t approaches zero of the change in position over the change in t. Mathematically,
$\mathop {\lim }\limits_{{\rm{t}} \to 0} \frac{{\Delta x}}{{\Delta t}}$
The Instantaneous Velocity is expressed in m/s.

Q14. While determining velocity from the position-time graph, velocity at any time is the slope of the _______ to the point on the graph at that instant.
    (A) line from origin
    (B) perpendicular
    (C) tangent   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Unit vector
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Velocity is defined as the rate of change of position with respect to time, which may also be referred to as the instantaneous velocity to emphasize the distinction from the average velocity. In terms of a displacement-time (x vs. t) graph, the instantaneous velocity (or, simply, velocity) can be thought of as the slope of the tangent line to the curve at any point.

Q15. If the position- time graph is a straight line then
    (A) the velocity is increasing.
    (B) the velocity is constant.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the velocity is decreasing.
    (D) the velocity is zero.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The principle is that the slope of the line on a position-time graph reveals useful information about the velocity of the object. If the velocity is constant, then the slope is constant (i.e., a straight line).

Q1. If the position- time graph is a straight line parallel to the time axis
    (A) the velocity is increasing.
    (B) the velocity is decreasing.
    (C) the velocity is constant but non zero.
    (D) the velocity is zero.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Position-time graph of horizontal straight line parallel to time axis represents that the position of the body does not changes with the passage of time. So it represents the rest state of motion.
It means velocity of object is zero.

Q2. The average acceleration 'a' over a time interval is defined as
    (A) average speed divided by the time interval.
    (B) the change in velocity divided by the time interval.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) average velocity divided by the time interval.
    (D) average displacement divided by the time interval.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Acceleration is the rate of change of velocity with time. It is a vector quantity. Average acceleration is the change in velocity per unit time over an interval of time.Let initial velocity at time interval t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1 is v_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1 and final velocity at time interval t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 is v_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2, then
$\vec a_{avg}={‚àÜ\vec v\over ‚àÜt}={\vec v_2-\vec v_1\over t_2-t_1}$

Q3. Instantaneous acceleration is defined as
    (A) $\frac{v}{t}$
    (B) $\frac{{d^2}v} {{d{t^2}}}$
    (C) $\mathop {\lim }\limits_{{\rm{t}} \to 0} \frac{\Delta v}{{\Delta t}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{dx}{{dt}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Instantaneous acceleration is measured over a "short" time interval. The word short in this context means infinitely small or infinitesimal ‚Äî having no duration or extent whatsoever. It's a mathematical ideal that can can only be realized as a limit. The limit of a rate as the denominator approaches zero is called a derivative.
Instantaneous acceleration is then the limit of average acceleration as the time interval approaches zero ‚Äî or alternatively, acceleration is the derivative of velocity.
$a=\lim _\limits{\mathrm{t} \rightarrow 0} \frac{\Delta v}{\Delta t}=\frac{d v}{d t}$

Q4. For uniformly accelerated motion velocity at time t is given by
    (A) $v = t{v_0} + 2a$
    (B) $v = {v_0} + 2at$
    (C) $v = {v_0} + at$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $v = t{v_0} + a$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Consider a particle moving along a straight line with uniform acceleration 'a'. At t = 0, let the particle be at A and $v_o$ be its initial velocity and when t = t, v be its final velocity.
Acceleration = $Change\ in\ velocity \over time\ taken$ 
$\Rightarrow a ={v-v_o\over t-0}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $at= v-v_o$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $v= v_o+at$

Q5. A car moving at 60 km/h comes to a stop in 4.0 s. What was its deceleration?
    (A) -6.1227 m/s^2
    (B) 4.023 m/s^2
    (C) ‚àí4.1667 m/s^2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -5.2 m/s^2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: initial velocity u = 60 km/h = 60 $\times$1000/(60 $\times$ 60) = 16.667m/s
As it stop final velocity v = 0
Time taken t = 4 s
We know,
a = $ {v-u\over t }$
$= {0-16.667\over 4}$ = ‚àí4.1667m/s^2
A negative sign shows it is a decelaration.

Q6. A car is traveling due west at 20.0 m/s. Find the velocity of the car after 37.00 s if its constant acceleration is 1.0 m/s^2 due east. Assume the acceleration remains constant.
    (A) 23.0 m/s east
    (B) 17.0 m/s west
    (C) 23.0 m/s west
    (D) 17.0 m/s east   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Assume west direction as +ve. Initial velocity, u = + 20.0 m/s
Final velocity = ?
Acceleration a = - 1.0 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Time taken t = 37.0 s
We know, v = u + at
$v = 20.0 - 37.0\times 1$
v = -17.0
The negative sign shows direction of velocity is opposite. So velocity is 17.0 m/s due east.

Q7. For motion with uniform acceleration, x-t graph is
    (A) a hyperbola
    (B) a straight line
    (C) a cubic
    (D) a parabola   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: We know that , s = ut + 0.5at^2
The slope of the x-t graph will give you velocity. So, if u=0, the slope of the graph at t=0 is 0. For u>0, the initial slope is +ve and for negative u, the initial slope is negative. Hence you will get parabolic shapes.

Q8. For motion with uniform acceleration, v-t graph is
    (A) a straight line perpendicular to the time axis.
    (B) a straight line inclined to the time axis.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) an ellipse.
    (D) a straight line parallel to the time axis.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When velocity - time graph is plotted for an object moving with uniform acceleration, the slope of the graph is a straight line. 
_(Velocity - time graph of an object moving with uniform acceleration)

Q9. The area under the velocity-time curve between times ${{\rm{t}}_{\rm{1}}}$ and ${{\rm{t}}_{\rm{2}}}$ is equal to the
    (A) path length of the object during that interval of time.
    (B) velocity of the object during that interval of time.
    (C) displacement of the object during that interval of time.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) average velocity of the object during that interval of time.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The area under the velocity-time curve between times t_ 1 and t_ 2 is equal to the displacement of the object during that interval of time.

Q10. If the velocities of two particles A and B are respectively ${{\rm{v}}_{\rm{A}}}$ and ${{\rm{v}}_{\rm{B}}}$. Then the velocity of object B relative to object A is
    (A) ${{\rm{v}}_{{\rm{BA}}}} = {\rm{ }} - {{\rm{v}}_{\rm{B}}} + {\rm{ }}{{\rm{v}}_{\rm{A}}}$
    (B) ${{\rm{v}}_{{\rm{BA}}}} = {\rm{ }}{{\rm{v}}_{\rm{B}}} + {\rm{ }}{{\rm{v}}_{\rm{A}}}$
    (C) ${{\rm{v}}_{{\rm{BA}}}} = {\rm{ }}{{\rm{v}}_{\rm{B}}} - {\rm{ }}{{\rm{v}}_{\rm{A}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${{\rm{v}}_{{\rm{BA}}}} = {\rm{ }} - {{\rm{v}}_{\rm{B}}} - {\rm{ }}{{\rm{v}}_{\rm{A}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Relative velocity of a body A with respect to another body B, when both are in motion, is the velocity with which A appears to move to B.
In general,
$V_{BA} = V_{B}-{V}_{A} $

Q11. In which of the following examples of motion, can the body be considered approximately a point object?
    (A) a spinning top moving on a curved path
    (B) a tumbling beaker that has slipped off the edge of a table
    (C) a spinning cricket ball that turns sharply on hitting the ground
    (D) a railway carriage moving without jerks   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Point object is used in kinematics branch of physics. It is an object whose dimensions are ignored or neglected while considering its motion.
The size of a carriage is very small as compared to the distance between two stations. Thus, the carriage can be treated as a point sized object.

Q12. Domestic power supply in India is
    (A) 110 V, 60 Hz
    (B) 416 V, 60 Hz
    (C) 220 V, 50 Hz   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 24 V DC
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The voltage in India is 220 volts, alternating at 50 cycles per second (Hertz). This is the same as, or similar to, most countries in the world including Australia, Europe and the UK.

Q13. The distance(s) in metres travelled by a particle is related to time(t) in seconds by the equation of motion:
S = 10t + 4t^2. What is the initial velocity of the body?
    (A) 6 m/s
    (B) 4 m/s
    (C) 14 m/s
    (D) 10 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Velocity is given by:
v = $ds\over dt$= $d(10t+4t^2)\over dt$= 10 + 8t
Velocity at t = 0, v_0 = 10 + 8 $\times$ 0 = 10 m/s

Q14. SI unit of acceleration is
    (A) $m/h^2$
    (B) $mm/h^2$
    (C) $cm/s^2$
    (D) $m/s^2$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Acceleration is the rate of change of velocity of an object with respect to time.
a = $change \ in \ velocity \over time \ taken $
SI unit of velocity = m/s
SI unit of time = s
So SI unit of acceleration = ${m\over s\times s}= m/s^2$

Q15. Name the instrument used to measure instantaneous speed of a vehicle.
    (A) speedometer   <-- CORRECT
    (B) accelerator
    (C) ammeter
    (D) multimeter
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The device used to measure the instantaneous speed of the vehicle is the speedometer.

Q1. A truck is coming towards you from a distance of 1000m on a straight road at time t=0. At time t=10 seconds it is at a distance of 900 m. The average velocity in m/sec is
    (A) 14
    (B) 12
    (C) 10   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 17
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Initial distance x_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1 = 1000 m
Initial time t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1= 0 sec
Final distance, x_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 = 900 m
Final time t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 = 10 sec
Average velocity, $v_{avg}={distance \ covered \over time \ taken}$ = ${1000-900\over 10-0}={100\over 10}= 10\ m/s$

Q2. A truck is coming towards you from a distance of 1000 m on a straight road, at time t = 0. It reaches you in 100 seconds. The average speed in m/s is:
    (A) 14
    (B) 12
    (C) 10   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 17
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Total distance covered s = 1000 m
Total time taken t = 100 - 0 = 100 s
Average speed, $v_{avg}={total \ distance \ covered\over total \ time \ taken}$ $= {1000\over 100}$ = 10 m/s

Q3. A truck is coming towards you from a distance of 1000m on a straight road, at time t=0. The driver stops for a second near a poster. He reaches you in 100 sec. The average speed in m/s is
    (A) 14
    (B) 10   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 17
    (D) 12
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Total distance covered s = 1000 m
Total time taken t = 100 - 0 = 100 s
Average speed, $v_{avg}={total \ distance \ covered\over total \ time \ taken}$ $= {1000\over 100}= 10 \ m/s$

Q4. A truck is coming towards you from a distance of 1000 m on a straight road. At time t=0 it starts from rest. At time t=10 seconds its velocity is 20m/s. What is the average acceleration in m/ ${\rm{se}}{{\rm{c}}^{\rm{2}}}$?
    (A) 5.2
    (B) 2.5
    (C) 1.5
    (D) 2.0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Average acceleration is the change in velocity divided by an elapsed time.
Initial velocity, u = 0 m/s
Final velocity, v = 20 m/s
Time elapsed = 10-0 = 10 s
Average acceleration, $a_{avg} = {change \ in \ veloctiy \over time \ elapsed}$ $= {20-0\over 10}= 2\ m/s^2$

Q5. With reference to the figure which shows a particle moving along a straight line, y axis represents the position and x axis represents time. If x_1 = 18m, the average velocity at if x_1 in m/s is
    (A) 180
    (B) 18.0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 20
    (D) 1.8
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Average velocity can be defined as the displacement divided by the time.
Total displacement, d = 18 m
Time taken t = 1 s
average velocity, $v_{avg}={Total \ displacement \over time \ taken }$
$= {18\over 1} = 18 \ m/s$

Q6. A bus starts from rest with an acceleration of 1 m/sec^2. A man who is 48 meter behind the bus with a uniform velocity of 10 m/sec. Then the minimum time after which the man will catch the bus is
    (A) 10 sec
    (B) 8 sec   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 14 sec
    (D) 4 sec
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the distance traveled by the bus when man catches the bus be S meter. Distance traveled by the man when he catch the bus, S' = S+48 meter
Given: Initial velocity of bus u = 0
Initial velocity of man, u' = 10m/sec
Acceleration of Bus = 1 m/s^2 
Acceleration of Man = 0
We will use the formula for displacement i.e.,
$S = ut+{1\over 2}at^2$
Displacement of Bus, $S= {1\over 2}t^2 \ ......(1)$
Displacement of Man, $S+48=10t \ ....... (2)$
By substituting the value of S from eq(1) in eq(2) we get
${1\over 2}t^2+48=10 t $
$\Rightarrow t^2-20t+96=0$
$\Rightarrow t^2-12t-8t+96=0$
$\Rightarrow (t-8)(t-12)=0$
 $\Rightarrow$ t = 8, 12
Taking minimum value we have t = 8 sec.

Q7. A stone thrown from the top of a building is given an initial velocity of 20.0 m/s straight upward. Determine the time in seconds at which the stone reaches its maximum height. (Take g = 9.8 m/${\rm{se}}{{\rm{c}}^{\rm{2}}}$)
    (A) 1.67
    (B) 2.7
    (C) 2.8
    (D) 2.04   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial velocity is given by , u = 20.0 m/s
At maximum height it will stop, so final velocity is given by , v = 0 m/s
Acceleration due to gravity g = 9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Time taken to reach maximum height is = t
We know that, v = u + at
$\Rightarrow$ $0 = 20 +(-9.8)t$
$\Rightarrow$$‚Äã‚Äã t = {-20\over -9.8}=2.04\ s$ [g is taken as negative because it is in the opposite direction of motion]

Q8. With reference to the figure below which shows a particle moving along a straight line, the y-axis represents the position and x-axis represents time. If ${{\rm{x}}_{\rm{2}}}$ = 270m, the instantaneous velocity at ${{\rm{x}}_{\rm{2}}}$ in m/s is

Q9. Motion along a straight line is called __________.
    (A) parabolic motion
    (B) oscillatory motion
    (C) circular motion
    (D) rectilinear motion   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Rectilinear motion is another name for straight-line motion. This type of motion describes the movement of a particle or a body. A body is said to experience rectilinear motion if any two particles of the body travel the same distance along two parallel straight lines.

Q10. A jet lands on an aircraft carrier at 60 m/s. What is its acceleration if it stops in 2.0 s?
    (A) -10 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (B) -30 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -20 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (D) 30 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 60 m/s
As it stops then final velocity, v = 0 m/s
Time taken t = 2.0 s
We know, v - u = at
$\Rightarrow$ 0 - 60 = 2a
$\Rightarrow$ a = ${-60\over 2}= -30 \ m/s^2$
-ve sign shows velocity is decreasing.

Q11. A jet lands on an aircraft carrier at 30 m/s. What is its acceleration if it stops in 2.0 s?
    (A) 20 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (B) -10 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (C) -20 ${\rm{m}}{{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$

Q12. A jet lands on an aircraft carrier at 60 m/s. It stops in 2.0 s. What is the displacement of the plane when it stops?
    (A) 35
    (B) 45
    (C) 60.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 50
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 60 m/s
As it stops so final velocity, v = 0 m/s
Time taken t = 2 seconds
We know, v - u = at
$\Rightarrow a = {v-u\over t}\ \ .....(1)$
Also, $s = ut+{1\over 2}at^2$
From (1), we have
$s = ut+{1\over 2}({v-u\over t})t^2$
$\Rightarrow s = ut+{1\over 2}({v-u})t$
After putting given values, we have 
$\Rightarrow s = (60\times 2)+{1\over 2}(0-60)\times 2$
$\Rightarrow$ s = 120-60 = 60 m

Q13. A jet lands on an aircraft carrier at 30 m/s. It stops in 2.0 s. What is the displacement of the plane when it stops?

    (B) 45
    (C) 35
    (D) 40

    Explanation: Initial velocity u, = 30 m/s

Time t = 2 s
Distance covered = s
we know that ,v= u +at
0= 30 + a(2)
a= - 15m/s^2
We know, s = $ut+{1\over 2}at^2$
$\Rightarrow s = 30\times 2+{1\over 2}(-15)\times2^2$
$\Rightarrow$ s = 30 m

Q15. A truck has a velocity of 2 m/s at time t=0. It accelerates at 2 m / ${{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$ on seeing police. What is its velocity in m/s at a time of 2 sec?

Q1. A truck has a velocity of 3 m/s at time t = 0. It accelerates at 3 m/${{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$ on seeing police. What is its velocity in m/s at a time of 2 sec?
    (A) 7
    (B) 9   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 12
    (D) 8
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 3 m/s
Acceleration, a = 3 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Initial time, t_1 = 0 s
Final time, t_2 = 2s
Time taken t = 2 - 0 = 2 s 
Final velocity, v =?
We know, v = u + at
$\Rightarrow v = 3+2\times 3$
$\Rightarrow $ v = 3 + 6 = 9 m/s^2

Q2. A stone thrown from the top of a building is given an initial velocity of 20.0 m/s straight upward. Determine the time in seconds at which the stone reaches its maximum height. (Take g = 9.8 m/${\rm{se}}{{\rm{c}}^{\rm{2}}}$)
    (A) 2.8
    (B) 2.7
    (C) 1.67
    (D) 2.04   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial velocity is given by , u = 20.0 m/s
At maximum height it will stop, so final velocity is given by , v = 0 m/s
Acceleration due to gravity g = 9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Time taken to reach maximum height is = t
We know that, v = u + at
$\Rightarrow$ $0 = 20 +(-9.8)t$
$\Rightarrow$$‚Äã‚Äã t = {-20\over -9.8}=2.04\ s$ [g is taken as negative because it is in the opposite direction of motion]

Q3. A stone thrown from the top of a building is given an initial velocity of 20.0 m/s straight upward. Determine the maximum height it travels in meters. (Take g = 9.8 m/${\rm{se}}{{\rm{c}}^{\rm{2}}}$)
    (A) 25.4
    (B) 30.4
    (C) 15.4
    (D) 20.4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 20.0 m/s
At maximum height stone will be stopped, So final velocity, v = 0 m/s
Acceleration due to gravity, a = g = -9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 (-ve sign show the opposite direction of motion)
Let maximum height = s
We know, $v^2-u^2=2as$
$\Rightarrow$ $0^2-(20)^2= 2\times(- 9.8)s$
$\Rightarrow -400= -19.6s$
$\Rightarrow s = {-400\over -19.6}= 20.4\ m$

Q4. A stone thrown from the top of a building is given an initial velocity of 20.0 m/s straight upward. Determine the time in seconds at which the stone returns to the height from which it was thrown. g = 9.8 m/sec^2.
    (A) 5.32
    (B) 3.45
    (C) 4.08   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4.44
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Initial velocity u = 20.0 m/s
At maximum height stone will be stopped, 
So final velocity v = 0 m/s
Acceleration due to gravity a = g = -9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 (-ve Because it is in opposite direction of motion)
Let maximum height = s
We know,
v^2 ‚àí u^2 = 2as
$\Rightarrow$ 0^2 ‚àí (20)^2 = 2 $\times$ ( ‚àí 9.8)s
$\Rightarrow$ ‚àí 400 = ‚àí 19.6s
$\Rightarrow s = {-400\over -19.6}$ = 20.4 m
Time to cover this distance upward is given by 
$\Rightarrow$ v ‚àí u = at
$\Rightarrow$ 0-20 = (-9.8)t
$\Rightarrow$ t = ${-20\over -9.8}$ = 2.04 sec 
Again to reach the same level from where it has been thrown it has to cover the same distance downward.
For this initial velocity u = 0 
s = 20.4 m
a = 9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 (+ve because motion is in same direction).
So,
$\Rightarrow$ 20.4 = 0 $\times$ t + $1\over 2$ $\times$ 9.8t^2
$\Rightarrow t^2 = {20.4\over 4.9}= 4.16$ 
$\Rightarrow t =\sqrt {4.16}$ = 2.04 
Total time = 2.04 + 2.04 = 4.08 s

Q5. A stone thrown from the top of a 50 m tall building is given an initial velocity of 20.0 m/s straight upward. Determine the velocity in m/sec when the stone returns to the height from which it was thrown. g = 9.8 m/sec^2.
    (A) -30.0
    (B) -15.0
    (C) -25.0
    (D) -20.0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: t_A = 0
y_A = 50m
v_A = 20$\frac{m}{s}$
a = -g = -9.80$\frac{m}{s^2}$ 
(v_C)^2 ‚àí (vA)^2 = 2a(y_C‚àí y_A) 
With y_C = y_A we get
(VC)^2 = (v_A)^2
$\Rightarrow$ v_C = $\pm$v_A
As the motion of the stone is downward, and the‚Äù+‚Äùsign was assigned for the upward motion,
we get for v_ C = ‚àív_A= ‚àí20 m/s.

Q6. A stone thrown from the top of a building is given an initial velocity of 20.0 m/s straight upward. The height of the building is 50.0 m. Determine the velocity in m/sec when the stone hits the ground. (g =9.8 m/${\rm{se}}{{\rm{c}}^{\rm{2}}}$)
    (A) -39.7
    (B) -37.1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -33.8
    (D) -27.4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Initial velocity is given by u = 20 m/s
Final velocity before hitting ground is given by = v
Distance covered is, s = 50 m
Acceleration due to gravity, a = 9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
We know that, $v^2-u^2= 2as$
$\Rightarrow v^2-(-20)^2= 2\times 9.8\times 50$
$\Rightarrow v^2-400= 980$
$\Rightarrow v^2= 1380$
$\Rightarrow v= \sqrt {1380}= \pm 37.1$
As this velocity is in the opposite direction, so v = - 37.1 m/s

Q7. Two parallel rail tracks run north-south. Train A moves north with a speed of 54 km/ hr, and train B moves south with a speed of 90 km/ hr. What is the velocity of B with respect to A in m/sec? Choose the positive direction of x-axis to be from south to north.
    (A) -30.0
    (B) -40.0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -45.0
    (D) -55.0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Velocity of A is given by , $v_A = +54\ km h^{‚Äì1} = + 15\ ms^{‚Äì1 }$
Velocity of B is given by , $v_B = ~‚Äì 90\ km h^{‚Äì1} =\ ‚Äì 25\ m s^{‚Äì1 }$
Relative velocity of B with respect to A, $v_{BA}= v_B ‚Äì v_A $$=-25-15 =\ ‚Äì 40\ m s^{‚Äì1 }$
i.e. the train B appears to A to move with a speed of 40 ms^‚Äì1 from north to south.

Q8. Two parallel rail tracks run north-south. Train A moves north with a speed of 27 km/ hr, and train B moves south with a speed of 45 km/ hr. What is the velocity of B with respect to A in m/s? Choose the positive direction of the x-axis to be from the south to north:
    (A) -18
    (B) -20   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -28
    (D) -15
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The velocity of A is given by, v_A = +27 kmh^‚Äì1 = +7.5 ms^‚Äì1
The velocity of B is given by , v_B = -45 kmh^‚Äì1 = -12.5 ms^‚Äì1
The relative velocity of B with respect to A is given by, v_BA = v_B ‚Äì v_A = ‚àí7.5‚àí12.5 = ‚Äì20 ms^‚Äì1
i.e. the train B appears to A to move with a speed of 20 ms^‚Äì1 from north to south.

Q9. Two parallel rail tracks run north-south. Train A moves north with a speed of 54 km/ hr, and train B moves south with a speed of 90 km/ hr. What is the velocity of ground with respect to B in m/s? Choose the positive direction of the x-axis to be from the south to the north.
    (A) 30 m/s
    (B) 28 m/s
    (C) 25.0m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 22 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Choose the positive direction of the x-axis to be from the south to the north. 
Then, v_A = +54 km h^‚Äì1= +15 ms^‚Äì1
v_B= ‚Äì90 km h^‚Äì1= ‚Äì25 ms^‚Äì1
The relative velocity of B with respect to A = v_B ‚Äì v_A = -25 ‚àí (15) = -40 ms^‚Äì1, i.e. the train B appears to A to move with a speed of 40 ms^‚Äì1 from north to south.
The relative velocity of ground with respect to B = 0 ‚Äì v_B = 0 ‚àí (‚àí25) = 25ms^‚Äì1.

Q10. Two parallel rail tracks run north-south. Train A moves north with a speed of 54 km/ hr, and train B moves south with a speed of 90 km/ hr. What is the velocity of a monkey running on the roof of the train A against its motion (with a velocity of 18 km/hr with respect to the train A) as observed by a man standing on the ground? Choose the positive direction of x-axis to be from the south to north.
    (A) 12 ms^-1
    (B) 10.0ms^-1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8 ms^-1
    (D) 14 ms^-1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the velocity of the monkey with respect to the ground be v_M. The relative velocity of the monkey with respect to A,
$v_{M A}=v_{M}-v_{A}=-18 k m h^{-1}=-5 m s^{-1}$
Therefore velocity of monkey will be given by , $v_{M}=(15-5) m s^{-1}=10 m s^{-1}$ [$\because v_{A}=+54 k m h^{-1}=15 m s^{-1}$]

Q11. Two parallel rail tracks run north-south. Train A moves north with a speed of 54 km/ hr, and train B moves south with a speed of 90 km/ hr. What is the velocity of a monkey running on the roof of the train A against its motion (with a velocity of 18 km/hr with respect to the train A) as observed by a man standing on the ground in m/s ? Choose the positive direction of x-axis to be from south to north
    (A) 11
    (B) 8
    (C) 10.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Choose the positive direction of the x-axis to be from the south to the north. 
Then, v_A = +54 km h^-1 = +15 ms^-1
v_B = -90 km h^-1 = - 25 ms^-1
The relative velocity of B with respect to A
= v_B - v_A = (-25) -15= -40 ms^-1, i.e. the train B appears to A to move with a speed of 40 ms^-1 from north to south.
The relative velocity of ground with respect to B = 0 - v_B = 0 - (-25) = 25ms^-1
Now, let the velocity of the monkey with respect to the ground be v_M. 
The relative velocity of the monkey with respect to A,
v_MA = v_M - v_A = 18 -54 kmh^-1 = - 10ms^-1.

Q12. A jet lands on an aircraft carrier at 63 m/s. What is its acceleration in ${\rm{m}}/{{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$ if it stops in 2.0 s?
    (A) -33
    (B) -31.5   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -35
    (D) 34
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 63 m/s
As it stops, so final velocity, v = 0 m/s
Time t = 2.0 s
We know that, v - u = at
|$\Rightarrow$ $a = {v-u\over t}$
$\Rightarrow$ $ a = {0-63\over 2}$
$\Rightarrow$ $ a = -31.5\ m/s^2$

Q13. A jet lands on an aircraft carrier at 63 m/s. What is the displacement of the plane in m while it stopped in 2 s:
    (A) 60.0
    (B) 57.0
    (C) 68.0
    (D) 63.0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial velocity u = 63 m/s
At it stops final velocity v = 0 m/s
Time taken t = 2 s
v = u+ at
0 = 63 + 2a
a = -31.5 m/s^2
We know,
$s = ut +{1\over 2}at^2$
s = 63 $\times$2 + 1/2 $\times$ (-31.5)$\times$ 2^2
s = 63 m

Q14. A car traveling at a constant speed of 45.0 m/s passes a trooper hidden behind a billboard. One second after the speeding car passes the billboard; the trooper sets out from the billboard to catch it, accelerating at a constant rate of 3 m/s^2. How long does it take her to overtake the car?
    (A) 36.0 s
    (B) 33.0 s
    (C) 34.0 s
    (D) 31.0 s   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The initial speed of the car u = 45 m/s
Let t = 0 s when the car passes the trooper.
The trooper starts from rest 1 s after the car passes the billboard.
In this 1 s the car would have covered a distance of 45 m.
Let y be the time at which the trooper overtakes the car.
Distance covered by car at time y
S = 45 + uy = 45 + 45y......(1)
(The distance is measured from the billboard)
The same distance is covered by the trooper also.
S = 0 + $1\over 2$ $\times$ 3 $\times$(y)^2....(2)
(Initial speed of trooper = 0).
Equating (1) and (2)
45 + 45y = $3\over 2$(y)^2
$\Rightarrow$ 3y^2 - 90y - 90 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ y^2 - 30y - 30 = 0
Using quadratic formula, we get:
$\Rightarrow$ $ {30 ¬± \sqrt {900+120} \over 2}$ = ${30 \pm 31.93\over 2 }$ = 30.97 s $\approx$ 31 s 
neglected negative value of y.

Q15. Jules Verne in 1865 proposed sending people to the Moon by firing a space capsule from 220-m-long cannon with a final velocity of 10.97 km/s. What would have been the unrealistically large acceleration experienced by the space travelers during launch?
    (A) 2.74 $\times$ 10^3 m/s^2
    (B) 3.74 $\times$ 10^5 m/s^2
    (C) 2.74 $\times$ 10^5 m/s^2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2.74 $\times$ 10^6 m/s^2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We know the equation of motion
v^2 ‚àí u^2 = 2as 
Given: v = 10.97 km/s = 10.97 $\times$ 10^3 m/s
u = 0
S = 220 m
Acceleration $a = {v^2 - u^2 \over 2s}$ =$ (10.97 \times 10^3 )^2- (0)^2\over 2 \times 220 $ = $ (10.97 \times 10^3 )^2\over 440 $ 
= 2.74 $\times$ 10^5 m/s^2
