Q1. A golf ball is released from rest from the top of a very tall building. Calculate the position in m of the ball after 2.00 seconds.
    (A) 22.2
    (B) 20.9
    (C) 32.1
    (D) 19.6   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Ball is under free fall, acceleration will be due to gravity.
Thus ,Initial velocity u is= 0
Time = 2.0 seconds
Acceleration due to gravity, g is= 9.8 ms^-2
We know that, S = ut + ${1\over 2}gt^2$ = 0$\times t +{1\over 2}\times( 9.8)\times (2.0)^2$
hence, S= 19.6 m

Q2. A truck covers 40.0 m in 8.50 s while smoothly slowing down to a final speed of 2.80 m/s. Find its original speed in m/s:
    (A) 6.61   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 5.61
    (C) 8.61
    (D) 7.61
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let initial velocity is given by = u
Final velocity is given by v = 2.80 m/s
Distance covered is ,s = 40.0 m
Time taken is, t = 8.50 s
We know,
v = u + at 
$\Rightarrow$ v-u = at .....(1)
Also 
$s = ut+{1\over 2}at^2$ 
From (1) put value of at, we get
$\Rightarrow$ s = ut + ${1\over 2}t(v-u)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ s = ut + ${1\over 2}tv-{1\over 2}ut$ 
$\Rightarrow$ s = ${1\over 2} ut+{1\over 2}tv$ 
Put all the given values, we get
$\Rightarrow$ 40 = $ {1\over 2}\times u\times 8.5+ {1\over 2}\times 2.8 \times 8.5$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 80 - 23.8 = 8.5u 
$\Rightarrow$ 8.5u = 56.2 
$\Rightarrow$ u = 6.61 m/s

Q3. A truck covers 40.0 m in 8.50 s while smoothly slowing down to a final speed of 2.80 m/s. Find its original speed in m/s.
    (A) -0.3878
    (B) -0.368
    (C) 6.61   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4.756
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We know that, for a particle moves in a straight line with a constant acceleration a_x, its motion is described by the kinematic equation given by:
 $\Delta x=\frac{1}{2}\left(v_{x i}+v_{x f}\right) \Delta t $
Rearranging it, we have
$v_{i}=\frac{2 \Delta x}{\Delta t}-v_{f}$
$\text{Substituting the values of} ~\Delta x, \Delta t ~and ~v_{f}\text{ into this equation, we get}$
$v_{i}=\frac{2(40.0 \mathrm{m})}{8.50 \mathrm{s}}-(2.80 \mathrm{m} / \mathrm{s})=6.61 \mathrm{m} / \mathrm{s}$

Q4. A body moving with uniform acceleration has a velocity of 12.0 cm/s in the positive x-direction when its x coordinate is 3.00 cm. If its x coordinate 2.00 seconds later is -5.00 cm, what is the magnitude of its acceleration in ${\rm{cm}}/{{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$?
    (A) -12.0
    (B) -14.0
    (C) -16.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -18.0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Distance covered s = Final position - initial position = -5 - 3 = -8 cm
Initial velocity u = 12.0 cm/s
Time taken t = 2.0 s
We know 
 $s =ut+{1\over 2}at^2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ - 8 = 2 $\times$ 12.0 + ${1\over 2}a\times4$ 
$\Rightarrow$ -8 = 24 + 2a
$\Rightarrow$ a =$ {-8-24\over 2}$ = ‚àí16.0 cm/s^2 hence this is required result

Q5. A particle moves along the x-axis. Its position is given by the equation x = 2.00 + 3.00t ‚àí 4.00t^2 with x in meters and t in seconds. Determine its position in m at the instant it changes direction
    (A) 2.56 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2.22 m
    (C) 3.21 m
    (D) 1.97 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: it will change direction When the speed is zero.
Velocity v = ${dx\over dt}$ = 3 - 8t 
Put v = 0, we get
$\Rightarrow$ 3 ‚àí 8t = 0
$\Rightarrow$ t = ${3\over 8}$ 
It ll change direction at $t = {3\over 8}$ 
Position at this time.
 $x({3\over 8})= 2+3({3\over 8})-4({3\over 8})^2$ 
= $2+{9\over 8}-{9\over 16}$ 
= $32 \ + \ 18 \ - \ 9\over 16$ 
= $41\over16$ 
= 2.56 m

Q6. A particle moves along the x axis. Its position is given by the equation $x = 2.00 + 3.00t - 4.00{t^2}$ with x in meters and t in seconds. Determine its velocity in m/s when it returns to the position it had at t = 0.
    (A) -3.0m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -5.54m/s
    (C) -4.02m/s
    (D) -2.75m/s
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The given equation is $x = 2.00 + 3.00t - 4.00{t^2}$
At t = 0, we have x = 2,
$\therefore$ 2 = 2 + 3.0t - 4t^2
$t(3-4 t)=0\\ t=0~and ~t=\frac{3}{4}$
Now Velocity is given by , v = ${dx\over dt}= 3-8t$
= 3 - $8\times {3\over 4}$ = 3 - 6 = - 3 m/s
Negative sign shows direction of velocity is opposite.

Q7. A drag racer starts her car from rest and accelerates at 10.0 ${\rm{m}}/{{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$ for the entire distance of 400 m.How long did it take the race car to travel this distance in seconds?
    (A) 9.01
    (B) 8.33
    (C) 10.2
    (D) 8.94   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial velocity u = 0
Acceleration a = 10.0 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Distance covered s = 400 m
Time is taken, t = ?
We know
$s = ut+{1\over 2}at^2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $ 400= 0\times t+{1\over 2}\times 10\times t^2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 400 = 5t^2 
$\Rightarrow$ t^2 = 80 
$\Rightarrow$ t = $ \sqrt {80}$ = 8.94 s

Q8. A drag racer starts her car from rest and accelerates at 10.0 ${\rm{m}}/{{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$ for the entire distance of 400 m . What is the speed of the race car in m/s at the end of the run?
    (A) 87.2
    (B) 86.0
    (C) 89.4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 90.3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 0
Acceleration, a = 10.0 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Distance covered, s = 400 m
Final velocity, v = ?
We know that, $v^2-u^2 = 2as$
$\Rightarrow v^2-0= 2\times 10\times 400$
$\Rightarrow 8000= v^2$
$\Rightarrow v= \sqrt {8000}= 89.4\ m/s$

Q9. A jet plane lands with a speed of 100 m/s and can accelerate at a maximum rate of -5.00 ${\rm{m}}/{{\rm{s}}^{\rm{2}}}$ as it comes to rest. From the instant the plane touches the runway, what is the minimum time in seconds before it can come to rest?
    (A) 10.0
    (B) 25.0
    (C) 30.0
    (D) 20.0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 100 m/s
As it stops so final velocity, v = 0
Acceleration a = - 5 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
We know, v - u = at
$\Rightarrow$ $ t = {v-u\over a}$
$\Rightarrow$ $ t = {0-100\over -5}={-100\over -5}$
$\Rightarrow$ t = 20.0 s

Q10. A truck on a straight road starts from rest, accelerating at 2.00 m/s^2 until it reaches a speed of 20.0 m/s. Then the truck travels for 20.0 s at a constant speed until the brakes are applied, stopping the truck in a uniform manner in an additional 5.00 s. How long in seconds is the truck in motion?
    (A) 32.0
    (B) 35.0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 37.3
    (D) 23.0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: As start from rest,
So Initial velocity u = 0 m/s
Final velocity v = 20 m/s
Acceleration a = 2 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Let Time during this period = t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1
We know,
v-u = at
So, 20 ‚àí 0 = 2t_1
$t_1 = {20\over 2}$ = 10 s
Now travel with a constant speed of 20 m/s for time t_2 = 20 s
Time is taken to stop t_3 = 5s
Total time of motion t = 10 + 20 + 5 = 35 s

Q11. A truck on a straight road starts from rest, accelerating at 2.00 m/s^2 until it reaches a speed of 20.0 m/s. Then the truck travels for 20.0 s at a constant speed until the brakes are applied, stopping the truck in a uniform manner in an additional 5.00 s. What is the average velocity in m/s of the truck for the motion described?
    (A) 16.2
    (B) 154
    (C) 15.7   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 17.5
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As start from rest,
So Initial velocity u = 0 m/s
Final velocity v = 20 m/s
Acceleration a = 2 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Let Time during this period = t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1
Also let distance covered = s_1
We know,
v - u = at
So, 20 ‚àí 0 = 2t_1
$t_1 = {20\over 2}$ =10 s
Also,
v^2_ ‚àí u^2= 2as_1
$\Rightarrow$ 400 ‚àí 0 = 2 √ó 2 √ó s_1
$s_1 = {400\over 4}$ =100 m 
Now travel with constant speed of 20 m/s for time t_2 = 20 s
Distance covered 
s_2 = 20 $\times$ 20 = 400 m
Time taken to stop
t_3 = 5s
Before stopping it covers distance $= s_3$
$s_3={1\over 2}(20-0)5$ = 50 m
Total distance covered = 100 + 400 + 50 = 550 m
Total time of motion t = 10 + 20 + 5 = 35 s
Average velocity $v_{avg} = {total\ distance\over total \ time}$ 
$= {550\over 35}$ = 15.7 m/s

Q12. A ball starts from rest and accelerates at 0.500 m/s^2 while moving down an inclined plane 9.00 m long. When it reaches the bottom, the ball rolls up another plane, where, after moving 15.0 m, it comes to rest. What is the speed of the ball in m/s at the bottom of the first plane?

    (D) 4.00 m/s

Final velocity v =?

v^2 ‚àí u^2 = 2as
$\Rightarrow $ v^2 ‚àí 0 = 2 $\times$ 0.500 $\times$ 9.0
v^2 = 9
$\Rightarrow$ v = 3 m/s
This is the initial velocity for the second plane

Q13. A ball starts from rest and accelerates at 0.500 m/s^2 while moving down an inclined plane 9.00 m long. When it reaches the bottom, the ball rolls up another plane, where, after moving 15.0 m, it comes to rest. How many seconds does it take to roll down the first plane?

    (C) 2.0
    (D) 4.0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Initial velocity is given by ,u = 0
Acceleration a = 0.500 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2

Time taken t =?

s = ut + ${1\over 2}at^2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $ 9 = 0\times t+{1\over 2}\times (0.5)t^2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $t^2= {9\times 2\over 0.5} = 36$ 
$\Rightarrow$ t = 6 s

Q14. A ball starts from rest and accelerates at 0.500 m/s^2 while moving down an inclined plane 9.00 m long. When it reaches the bottom, the ball rolls up another plane, where, after moving 15.0 m, it comes to rest. What is the acceleration in m/s^2 along the second plane?

    (C) -0.321

v^2 ‚àí u^2 = 2as
$\Rightarrow$ v^2‚àí0 = 2 $\times$ 0.500 $\times$ 9.0
$\Rightarrow$ v^2 = 9
$\Rightarrow$ v = 3 m/s
This is initial velocity for second plane
For second plane

Final velocity v = 0 (as it stop)
Distance covered s = 15 m
Acceleration a = ?
$\Rightarrow$ 0 ‚àí 9 = 2 $\times$ a $\times$ 15
$\Rightarrow$ $a = {-9\over 30}$ = -0.3ms^-2

Q15. A ball starts from rest and accelerates at 0.500 m/s^2 while moving down an inclined plane 9.00 m long. When it reaches the bottom, the ball rolls up another plane, where, after moving 15.0 m, it comes to rest. What is the ball‚Äôs speed in m/s 8.00 m along the second plane?
    (A) 2.15 m/s
    (B) 2.05 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2.56 m/s
    (D) 2.23 m/s
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For First Plane
Initial velocity u = 0
Acceleration a = 0.500 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Distance covered s = 9.0 m
Final velocity v =?
We know
v^2 - u^2 = 2as
$\Rightarrow$ v^2 - 0 = 2 $\times$ 0.500 $\times$ 9.0
$\Rightarrow$ v^2 = 9
$\Rightarrow$ v = 3 m/s
This is initial velocity for second plane

Final velocity v = 0 (as it stop)
Distance covered s = 15 m

$\Rightarrow$ 0 - 9 = 2 $\times$ a $\times$ 15
$\Rightarrow$ a = - 9/30 = - 0.3 m/s^2

$\Rightarrow$ v^2 - 9 = 2 $\times$ (- 0.3) $\times$ 8.0
$\Rightarrow$ v^2 = -4.8 + 9 = 4.2
$\Rightarrow$ v = 2.05 m/s

========================================================================
Motion in a Plane Test 01  (id 542) [FREE]

Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The basic difference between a scalar and vector is one of
    (A) direction   <-- CORRECT
    (B) origin
    (C) magnitude
    (D) polar angle
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Scalar quantity gives you an idea about how much of an object there is, but vector quantity gives you an indication of how much of an object there is and that also in which direction. So, the main difference between these two quantities is associated with the direction, i.e. scalars do not have direction but vectors do.

Q2. The dimensions of Kinetic energy is same as that of
    (A) Pressure
    (B) Work   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Momentum
    (D) Force
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Work

Q3. The magnitude of displacement of a particle is
    (A) is less than the path length of the particle between two points.
    (B) is either less or equal to the path length of the particle between two points.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) is more than the path length of the particle between two points.
    (D) is equal to the path length of the particle between two points.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The maximum possible value for displacement is the distance travelled, so it cannot be of a greater value than distance (path length). The magnitude of the displacement is always less than or equal to the distance traveled. If two displacements in the same direction are added, then the magnitude of their sum will be equal to the distance traveled.

Q4. Two vectors are equal if
    (A) the direction is the same for both.
    (B) the magnitude is the same for both.
    (C) the two vectors have opposite directions.
    (D) the magnitude and direction are the same for both.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Equal vectors are vectors that have the same magnitude and the same direction. Equal vectors may start at different positions.

Q5. Multiplying a vector $\vec v$ by a positive real number $\lambda$
    (A) gives a vector $\overrightarrow {v'} $ = $\lambda \vec v$ in a direction opposite to $\vec v$
    (B) gives a scalar that is $\lambda $ times the polar angle of $\vec v$
    (C) gives a scalar that is $\lambda $ times the magnitude of $\vec v$
    (D) gives a vector $\overrightarrow {v'} $ = $\lambda \vec v$ in the same direction as $\vec v$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When a vector is multiplied by a positive number (for example 2, 3,5, 60 unit etc.) or a scalar only its magnitude is changed but its direction remains the same as that of the original vector.

Q6. Multiplying a vector $\vec v$ by a negative real number $\lambda$
    (A) gives a scalar that is $\lambda $ times the magnitude of $\vec v$
    (B) gives a scalar that is $\lambda $ times the polar angle of $\vec v$
    (C) gives a vector $\overrightarrow {v'} $ = $\lambda \vec v$ in the same direction as $\vec v$
    (D) gives a vector $\overrightarrow {v'} $ = $\lambda \vec v$ in a direction opposite to $\vec v$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If a vector is multiplied by a negative number (for example -2, -3, -5, -60 unit etc.) or a scalar not only its magnitude is changed but its direction also reversed.

Q7. To find the sum of vectors $\vec A$ and $\vec B$, we place vector $\vec B$ so that its
    (A) tail is at the head of the vector $\vec A$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) tail is at the tail of the vector $\vec A$
    (C) direction is the same as that of vector $\vec A$
    (D) head is at the head of the vector $\vec A$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Triangle law of vector addition states that when two vectors are represented as two sides of the triangle with the order of magnitude and direction, then the third side of the triangle represents the magnitude and direction of the resultant vector. Thus resultant vector is R= a+ b
Taken in same order mean tail of Vector B should be placed at the head of vector A as shown in image.

Q8. Vector addition is
    (A) non-commutative
    (B) commutative   <-- CORRECT
    (C) intransitive
    (D) asymmetric
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Vector addition is commutative, just like addition of real numbers. If you start from a point say P, you end up at the same spot no matter which displacement (a or b) you take first. The head-to-tail rule yields vector c for both a + b and b + a.

Q9. The addition of vectors and the multiplication of a vector by a scalar together gives rise to
    (A) intransitive law
    (B) distributive laws   <-- CORRECT
    (C) asymmetric laws
    (D) commutative law
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If a vector is multiplied by a scalar as in $p\vec A$ , then the magnitude of the resulting vector is equal to the product of p and the magnitude of $\vec A$, and its direction is the same as $\vec A$ if p is positive and opposite to $\vec A$ if p is negative.
Distributive law for scalar multiplication:
$p(\vec A+\vec B) = p\vec A+p\vec B$

Q10. Null vector or a zero vector has a magnitude
    (A) of complex nature
    (B) less than zero
    (C) greater than zero
    (D) equal to zero   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A null vector is a vector having a magnitude equal to zero. It is represented by $\vec 0$. A null vector has no direction or it may have any direction. Generally a null vector is either equal to resultant of two equal vectors acting in opposite directions or multiple vectors in different directions.
$\vec 0 = \vec A+(-\vec A)$

Q11. We can define the difference of two vectors A and B as the sum of two vectors A and B' such that B' is equal to B multiplied by
    (A) 1
    (B) -1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -2
    (D) 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Vector subtraction is defined in the following way.
 The difference of two vectors, A - B , is a vector C that is, C = A - B
 The addition of two vector such that C = A + (-B). B has been taken in opposite direction.
Thus vector subtraction can be represented as a vector addition.

Q12. An arbitrary vector $\vec v$ can be expressed as a sum of three mutually perpendicular unit vectors each multiplied by a
    (A) some scalar constant   <-- CORRECT
    (B) same scalar constant
    (C) scalar constant equal to -1
    (D) scalar constant equal to 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Any vector can be expressed as a sum of 3 perpendicular unit vectors, each multiplied by some number(the component of vector along that axis)
In the picture attached, the vector a has 3 different components along 3 perpendicular axes x.y.z and these components need not be equal all the times

Q13. A unit vector is a vector having a magnitude of 1 and points in
    (A) x-direction
    (B) z-direction
    (C) any chosen direction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) y-direction
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A unit vector is a vector that has a magnitude of 1 unit. A unit vector is also known as a direction vector. It is represented using a lowercase letter with a cap (‚Äò^‚Äô) symbol along with it. A vector can be represented in space using unit vectors. Any vector can become a unit vector by dividing it by the vector‚Äôs magnitude as follows:
$\text { Unit vector} =\frac{\text { vector }}{\text { magnitude of the vector }}$
$\hat i$ = a unit vector directed along the positive x-axis
$\hat j$ = a unit vector directed along the positive y-axis
$\hat k$ = a unit vector directed along the positive z-axis

Q14. An arbitrary vector $\vec A$ in a plane can be expressed in terms of its x and y components by the equation
    (A) ${\rm{}}\vec A = {A_x} - {A_y}$
    (B) ${\rm{}}\vec A = {A_x} + {A_y}$
    (C) $\vec A = {A_x}\hat i - {A_y}\hat j$
    (D) $\vec A = {A_x}\hat i + {A_y}\hat j$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In a two-dimensional coordinate system, any vector can be broken into x -component and y -component.
Vector $\vec A$ can be represented as 
$\vec A = A_x\hat i+ A_y\hat j$
Where $A_x$ is component in direction of x-axis and $\hat i$ is a unit vector in same direction of x-axis and $A_y$ is component in direction of y-axis and $\hat j$ is a unit vector in same direction of y-axis.

Q15. If ${A_x},{A_y}\ and\ {A_z}$ are x, y and z components of a vector then its magnitude is
    (A) $\sqrt {3A_x^2 + A_y^2 + A_z^2} $
    (B) $\sqrt {A_x^2 + A_y^2 + A_z^2} $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\sqrt {A_x^2 + A_y^2 + A_z^3} $
    (D) $\sqrt {A_x^2 + 2A_y^2 + A_z^2} $
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Rectangular components of a Vector: The projections of vector a along the x, y, and z directions are A_x, A_y, and A_z, respectively.
The magnitude of vector = $\sqrt {A_x^2 + A_y^2 + A_z^2} $

Q1. The speed of a projectile when it is at its greatest height is $\sqrt {\frac 2 5}$ times its speed at half the maximum height. What is the angle of projection?
    (A) $15^¬∞$
    (B) $90^¬∞$
    (C) $45^¬∞$
    (D) $60^¬∞$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Suppose the particle is projected with velocity u at an angle theta with the horizontal. Horizontal component of its velocity at all height will be u cos$\theta$.
At the greatest height, the vertical component of velocity is zero, so the resultant velocity is
$v_{1}=u \cos \theta$
At half the greatest height during upward motion,
y = $\frac {h}{2}$, a_y = -g, u_y = $u \sin \theta$
Using $v_{y}^{2}-u_{y}^{2}=2 a_{y} y$
We get, $v_{y}^{2}-u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta=2(-g) \frac{h}{2}$
or $v_{y}^{2}=u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta-g \times \frac{u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta}{2 g}=\frac{u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta}{2}$ $\left[\because h=\frac{u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta}{2 g}\right]$
or $v_{y}=\frac{u \sin \theta}{\sqrt{2}}$
Hence, resultant velocity at half of the greatest height is
$v_{2}=\left({\sqrt{{v_{1}^{2}}+\left(v_{y}^{2}\right)}}\right)$
$=\left(\sqrt{u^{2} \cos ^{2} \theta+\left(\frac{u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta}{2}\right)}\right)$
Given, $\frac{v_{1}}{v_{2}}=\left(\sqrt{\frac{2}{5}}\right)$
$\therefore \frac{v_{1}^{2}}{v_{2}^{2}}=\frac{u^{2} \cos ^{2} \theta}{u^{2} \cos ^{2} \theta+\left(\frac{u^{2} \sin ^{2} \theta}{2}\right)}=\frac{2}{5}$
or $\frac{1}{1+\frac{1}{2} \tan ^{2} \theta}=\frac{2}{5}$
or $2+\tan ^{2} \theta=5$ or $\tan ^{2} \theta=3$
or $\tan \theta=(\sqrt{3})$
$\therefore \theta=60^{\circ}$

Q2. A swimmer wishes to cross a 500 m wide river flowing at 5 km/hr. His speed with respect to water is 3 km/hr. If he heads in the direction making an angle $\theta $ with the flow, find the time he takes to cross the river?
    (A) $\frac{10}{sin \theta}$ minutes   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{10}{cos \theta}$ minutes
    (C) $\frac{10}{cos \theta}$ seconds
    (D) $\frac{10}{sin \theta} $ seconds
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The velocity of man w.r.t. water = 3 kmph. Thus the velocity of water is not necessary here because the velocity of man includes the contribution of the velocity of water because the given velocity of man is with respect to the flowing water which is the resultant velocity. The breadth of the river = 500 m = 0.5 km. Component of the velocity of man w.r.t. river along horizontal axis, v = 3sin($\theta$)
Now time is taken to cross the river, t = $\frac{\text { Distance }}{\text { velocity along horizontal axis }}=\frac{0.5}{3 \sin \theta}$ hrs 
$=\frac{0.5 \times 60}{3 \sin \theta}=\frac{10}{\sin \theta}$ minutes

Q3. A ball is dropped from a height. If it takes 0.2 s to cross the last 6.0 m before hitting the ground, find the height from which it was dropped. (Take g = 10m/s^2)
    (A) 57.05 m
    (B) 48.05 m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 32.35 m
    (D) 30.48 m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the initial velocity of the ball before the last 6m be = u
a = 10 m/s^2, s = 6.0m, t = 0.2 sec
$\Rightarrow$ $s = ut+{1\over 2}at^2$
$\Rightarrow 6 = 0.2u+{1\over 2}\times 10\times 0.04$
$\Rightarrow$ u = 29 m/s
Now consider the journey from rest to this height.
v = 29 m/s, u = 0 m/s,a = 10 m/s^2
v^2 ‚àí u^2 = 2as
$\Rightarrow$ 841 ‚àí 0 = 2 $\times $ 10 $\times $ s
$\Rightarrow$ s = 42.05 m
Therefore the total height = 42.05 + 6 = 48.05 m

Q4. An elevator is descending with uniform acceleration. A person in the elevator drops a marble at the moment the elevator starts to measure the acceleration of the elevator. The marble is 2 m above the floor when it is dropped. It takes 1.2 s to reach the floor of the elevator. What is the acceleration of the floor? Take g = 10 ms^-2.
    (A) 6.08 ms^‚àí2
    (B) 7.2 ms^‚àí2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6.58 ms^‚àí2
    (D) 8.18 ms^‚àí2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the acceleration of the elevator be ‚Äòa‚Äô downwards. As the elevator is going downwards the marble has to travel a distance more than 2 m in order to strike the floor.
Initial velocity, u = 0 for both the marble and the elevator. 
Distance travelled by elevator in 1.2 s = ${1\over 2}a\times (1.2)^2$ 
Distance travelled by marble in 1.2 s =${1\over2}g\times (1.2)^2$^$= {1\over 2}\times 10\times(1.2)^2 $
This distance should be equal to height of marble + distance covered by elevator.
So, ${1\over 2}\times 10\times(1.2)^2$ = $2+{1\over 2}\times a\times(1.2)^2$ 
On solving, we get, a = 7.2 ms^-2 downwards.

Q5. A body is projected with a velocity of 20ms^-1 at 50^¬∞ to the horizontal. Find Range of the projectile.
    (A) 40.2 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 45.2 m
    (C) 41.2 m
    (D) 39.2 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Initial Velocity v_o = 20 ms^-1 and $\theta = 50^¬∞$|
Horizontal Range, R =$v_o^2sin2\theta\over g$ $={400\sin\ 100^¬∞\over 9.8}$ = 40.2 m

Q6. A body is projected with a velocity of 20ms^-1 at 50^¬∞ to the horizontal. Find Maximum height reached.
    (A) $\approx 12 m$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\approx 22 m$
    (C) $\approx 15 m$
    (D) $\approx 20 m$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Initial Velocity, v_o = 20 ms^-1 and $\theta = 50^¬∞$
Maximum height reached, H = $v_o^2sin^2\theta\over 2g$ $= {400\sin^250^¬∞\over 2\times 9.8}$ = 11.97m $\approx 12 m$

Q7. A body is projected with a velocity of 20ms^-1 at 50^¬∞ to the horizontal. Find time of flight.
    (A) 3.5 s
    (B) 3.1 s   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 5.1 s
    (D) 4.2 s
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Initial Velocity, v_o = 20 ms^-1 and $\theta = 50^¬∞$
Time of flight = $2v_osin\theta\over g$ $= {2\times 20\times sin 50^¬∞\over 9.8}$ = 3.1 s

Q8. A man stands on the roof of a 15.0-m-tall building and throws a rock with a speed of 30.0 m/s at an angle of 33.0^o above the horizontal. You can ignore air resistance. Calculate the maximum height above the roof that the rock reaches.
    (A) 13.6 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 12.6 m
    (C) 14.2 m
    (D) 11.7 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let downward be the y-direction. Hence,
v_ox = v_o $\times$ cos$\theta$ = 30.0 $\times$cos33.0^o
= 25.2 m/s
v_oy = v_o $\times$ sin$\theta$ = 30.0 $\times$ sin33.0^o
= 16.3 m/s
At the maximum height, the velocity in the y direction v_y is zero:
hence , by Using 
(v_y)^2 = (v_oy)^2 + 2a_yh 
$\Rightarrow$ 0 = (16.3)^2 + 2(‚àí9.8)h
$h= {-(16.3\times 16.3)\over -2\times 9.8}$ = 13.6 m , thus height is 13.6 m

Q9. A man stands on the roof of a 15.0 m tall building and throws a rock with a velocity of magnitude 30.0 m/s at an angle of 33.0¬∞ above the horizontal. You can ignore air resistance. Calculate the magnitude of the velocity of the rock just before it strikes the ground.
    (A) 29.6 m/s
    (B) 30.6 m/s
    (C) 34.6 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 32.6 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let downward be the y-direction.
v_ox = v_o $\times$ cos$\theta$ = 30.0 $\times$ cos33.0^o
= 25.2 m/s
v_oy = v_o $\times$ sin$\theta$ = 30.0 $\times$ sin33.0^o
= 16.3 m/s
The velocity in the x direction is constant all the time,
At the ground, we have h = -15.0 m, 
We know,
(v_y)^2 = (v_oy)^2 + 2a_yh
$\Rightarrow$ $v_y=\sqrt {( v_{oy})^2+2a_yh}$ 
$v_y=\sqrt {( 16.3)^2+2(-9.8)(-15.0)} $
$\Rightarrow$ v_y = 23.7 m/s
The magnitude of the velocity of the rock just before it strikes the ground is
v = $\sqrt {(v_x)^2+(v_y)^2} $ 
$\Rightarrow$ v = $\sqrt{ (25.2)^2+(23.7)^2} $ = 34.6 m/s

Q10. Vectors are added by
    (A) adding the angles of the vectors
    (B) translating the two vectors
    (C) parallelogram law of addition   <-- CORRECT
    (D) adding the magnitudes of the vectors
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Parallelogram law of vector addition: It states that I\if two vectors are considered to be the adjacent sides of a parallelogram, then the resultant of two vectors is given by the vector which is a diagonal passing through the point of contact of two vectors.

Q11. Vectors can be added by:
    (A) Adding the magnitudes of the vectors
    (B) Adding the angles of the vectors
    (C) Vector addition   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Translating the two vectors
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Vector addition is the operation of adding two or more vectors together into a vector sum. The so-called parallelogram law gives the rule for vector addition of two or more vectors. For two vectors, the vector sum is obtained by placing them head to tail and drawing the vector from the free tail to the free head.

Q12. The vector addition is
    (A) associative   <-- CORRECT
    (B) intransitive
    (C) non-commutative
    (D) asymmetric
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Vector addition is the operation of adding two or more vectors together into a vector sum. Associative law of vector addition. The law states that the sum of vectors remains the same irrespective of their order or grouping in which they are arranged.
$ \vec A+(\vec B+\vec C) = (\vec A+\vec B)+\vec C $
This is known as the associative law of vector addition.

Q13. Which of the following physical quantities a vector?
    (A) Angular frequency
    (B) Number of moles
    (C) Acceleration   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Density
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Acceleration is a vector quantity because it has both magnitude and direction.
When an object has positive acceleration, the acceleration occurs in the same direction as the movement of the object.
When an object has a negative acceleration (it's slowing down), the acceleration occurs in the opposite direction as the movement of the object.

Q14. Which of the following physical quantities is a scalar?
    (A) current   <-- CORRECT
    (B) linear momentum
    (C) relative velocity
    (D) average velocity
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Electric current is a scalar quantity. It represents the direction of flow of positive charge but it is treated as a scalar quantity because current follows the laws of scalar addition and not the laws of vector addition, because the angle between the wires carrying current does not affect the total current in the circuit.

Q15. Which of the following physical quantities is a vector?
    (A) temperature
    (B) impulse   <-- CORRECT
    (C) gravitational potential
    (D) charge
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since force is a vector quantity, impulse is also a vector in the same direction. Impulse applied to an object produces an equivalent vector change in its linear momentum, also in the same direction. The SI unit of impulse is the newton second (Ns)

Q1. If ${A_x},{A_y}\ and\ {B_x},{B_y}$ are components of vectors $\vec A$ and $\vec B$ along the x and y-axis then the sum of the vectors $\vec A$ and $\vec B$ has a component in the x-direction equal to
    (A) ${A_x} - {B_x}$
    (B) $ - {A_x} - {B_x}$
    (C) ${A_x} + {B_x}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $ - {A_x} + {B_x}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The component method of addition can be summarized this way: 
 Using trigonometry, find the x-component and the y-component for each vector.
 Add up both x-components, (one from each vector), to get the x-component of the total.
 Add up both y-components, (one from each vector), to get the y-component of the total.
 Add the x-component of the total to the y-component of the total, and then use the Pythagorean theorem and trigonometry to get the size and direction of the total.
Using these points in mind, the sum of the vectors A and B has a component in the x direction $= A_x+B_x$

Q2. If $\vec r$ = $x\hat i + y\hat j$ is the position vector of a particle then the instantaneous velocity is given by
    (A) $v = \frac{dr} {2dt}$
    (B) $v = \frac{d(x+y)} {dt}$
    (C) $v = 2\frac{dr}{dt}$
    (D) $v = \frac{dr}{dt}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The exact measure of the velocity of a body at an instant or over a very-very short time interval ‚àÜt is known as instantaneous velocity. Mathematically instantaneous velocity of an object is the limiting value of average velocity as ‚àÜt tends towards 0.
Instantaneous velocity = $\displaystyle\lim_{\Delta t\to 0}\frac{\Delta x}{\Delta t} =\frac{dx}{ dt}$
So for given position vector, $\vec v$ = $\frac{dr}{dt}$

Q3. If $\vec r$ = $x\hat i + y\hat j$ is the position vector of a particle then the instantaneous acceleration is given by
    (A) $a = \frac{{d^3}r}{{d{t^3}}}$
    (B) $a = \frac{dr}{dt}$
    (C) $a = \frac{{d^2}r}{{d{t^2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $a = \frac{{d^4}r}{{d{t^2}}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The exact measure of the city of a body at an instant or over a very-very short time interval ‚àÜt is known as instantaneous velocity. Mathematically instantaneous velocity of an object is the limiting value of average velocity as ‚àÜt tends towards 0. Instantaneous velocity = $\displaystyle\lim_{\Delta t\to 0}\frac{\Delta x}{\Delta t} =\frac{dx}{ dt}$
So for given position vector, $\vec v$ = $\frac{dr}{dt}$
Instantaneous acceleration, $\vec a=$ $\frac{dv}{dt}= \frac{d^2r}{dt^2}$

Q4. Which is a constant for a freely falling object?
    (A) acceleration   <-- CORRECT
    (B) speed
    (C) displacement
    (D) velocity
    Answer: A
    Explanation: An object that falls through a vacuum is subjected to only one external force, the gravitational force, expressed as the weight of the object. An object that is moving only because of the action of gravity is said to be free falling and its motion is described by Newton's second law of motion. With algebra we can solve for the acceleration of a free falling object. The acceleration is constant and equal to the gravitational acceleration g which is 9.8 meters per square second at sea level on the Earth. The weight, size, and shape of the object are not a factor in describing a free fall.

Q5. For the case of uniformly accelerated motion in two dimensions it is possible to treat it as
    (A) Two separate simultaneous one-dimensional motions with varying acceleration along one direction and a non constant acceleration along perpendicular direction
    (B) Two separate simultaneous one-dimensional motions with constant acceleration along one direction and a non constant acceleration along perpendicular direction.
    (C) Two separate simultaneous one-dimensional motions with constant acceleration along two perpendicular directions.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Two separate simultaneous one-dimensional motions with constant acceleration along a single direction.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Consider a particle moving on x-y plane along a curved pat at time t, as shown in figure given below. Its displacement from origin is measured by vector $ \vec{r} $ its velocity is indicated by vector $‚Äã‚Äã\vec {v}$ (tangent to the path of the particle) and acceleration $\vec{a} $ as shown in the figure.
A Particle Moving in a xy Plane The vectors $ \vec{r}, \vec{v} \ and \ \vec{a}$ are interrelated and can be expressed in terms of their components, using unit vector notation as,
$\vec r= x\hat i+ y\hat j$ 
$v = {d\vec r\over dt}= {dx\over dt}\hat i + {dy\over dt}\hat j$ 
$= v_x\hat i + v_y\hat j$ 
And $\vec a= {dv\over dt}= {dv_x\over dt}\hat i+ {dv_y\over dt}\hat j$ 
$\vec a = a_x\hat i + a_y\hat j$ 
From the above relations we can say that two-dimensional motion is nothing but superimpose of two one dimension motions.
This is for the reason that in any two-dimensional motion, all the parameters can be resolved in two mutually perpendicular directions.

Q6. If particles A and B are moving with velocities $\vec v_A$ and $\vec v_B$ (each with respect to some common frame of reference, say ground.). Then, velocity of particle A relative to that of B is:
    (A) $\vec v_{BA}=$ $\vec v_B ~+‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã\vec v_A$
    (B) $\vec v_{BA}=$ $-\vec v_B ~_+‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã\vec v_A$
    (C) $\vec v_{BA}=$ $-\vec v_B ~-‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã\vec v_A$
    (D) $\vec v_{AB}=$ $\vec v_A ~-‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã\vec v_B$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The relative velocity of an object A with respect to another object B is the velocity that object A would appear to have to an observer situated on object B moving along with it. In simple words relative velocity of A with respect to B is the vector difference between the velocities of A and B. It is represented as 
$\vec v_{AB}=$ $\vec v_A ~-‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã\vec v_B$

Q7. The path of a projectile is
    (A) ellipse
    (B) hyperbola
    (C) straight line
    (D) parabola   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A particle with a vertical and horizontal velocity travelling in a gravitational field will trace out a parabola.

Q8. Centripetal acceleration of a particle moving in a circular path with constant velocity v is given by
    (A) ${{2}}{{{v}}^{{2}}}/{{R}}$, where R is the radius of the circle.
    (B) $\frac{v^2}{R}$, where R is the radius of the circle.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $v^2\times R$, where R is the radius of the circle.
    (D) ${{2}}{{{v}}^{{2}}}{{R}}$, where R is the radius of the circle.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A body that moves in a circular motion (of radius R) at constant speed ($\vec v$) is always being accelerated. The acceleration is at right angles to the direction of motion (towards the centre of the circle) and of magnitude $\frac{v^2}{R}$

Q9. The angle between $A = \hat i + \hat j$ and $B = \hat i - \hat j$ is
    (A) 45^o
    (B) 90^o   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 180^o
    (D) ^ - 45^o
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\cos (\theta)=\frac{\vec{A} \cdot \vec{B}}{|\vec{A}||\vec{B}|}=\frac{(\hat{i}+\hat{j}) \cdot(\hat{i}-\hat{j})}{|\sqrt{1^{2}+1^{2}}||\sqrt{1^{2}+(-1)^{2}}|}=\frac{1-1}{2}=0$
$\theta=\cos ^{-1}(0)=\frac{\pi}{2}~ or ~90^{0}$

Q10. The component of a vector $\vec r$ along X-axis will have maximum value if
    (A) $\vec r$ is along negative Y-axis
    (B) $\vec r$ is along positive X-axis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\vec r$ is along positive Y-axis
    (D) $\vec r$ make an angle of 45^o with the X-axis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let $\vec r$ makes an angle Œ∏ with the positive x-axis component of r along X-axis.
$ r_{x}=|r| \cos \theta$
$\left(r_{x}\right)_{\text {maximum }}=|r|(\cos \theta)_{\text {maximum }}$
$r_{x}=|r| \cos \theta$
$=|r| \cos 0^{\circ}=|r|\left(\therefore \cos \theta \text { is maximum } \mathrm{} \mathrm{} \text {of } \theta=0^{\circ}\right)$
$As~ \theta=0^{\circ}$
$\vec r$ is along positive x-axis

Q11. Which of the following algebraic operations on vectors is not permissible?
    (A) Multiplying any vector by any scalar
    (B) Adding a scalar component of the vector to the same vector   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Multiplying the sum of vectors A and B by a scalar
    (D) Adding any two vectors
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Although vectors and scalars represent different types of physical quantities, it is sometimes necessary for them to interact. While adding a scalar to a vector is impossible because of their different dimensions in space, it is possible to multiply a vector by a scalar.

Q12. Which of the following statement is false?
    (A) Three vectors not lying in a plane can never add up to give a null vector.
    (B) The average speed of a particle is either greater or equal to the magnitude of the average velocity of the particle over the same interval of time.
    (C) The total path length is always equal to the magnitude of the displacement vector of a particle.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The magnitude of a vector is always a scalar.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Displacement is a vector that is the shortest path length from the initial to the final position of the body. It is not always equal to path length. It can be zero and -ve also.

Q13. Given vectors a, b, c, d and a + b + c + d = 0,
 a, b, c and d must each be a null vector
 The magnitude of (a + c) equals the magnitude of ( b + d)
 The magnitude of a can never be greater than the sum of the magnitudes of b, c, and d
 b + c must lie in the plane of a and d if a and d are not collinear, and in the line of a and d, if they are collinear
which of the following statements not correct?
    (A) a, b, c and d must each be a null vector   <-- CORRECT
    (B) The magnitude of (a + c) equals the magnitude of ( b + d)
    (C) The magnitude of a can never be greater than the sum of the magnitudes of b, c, and d
    (D) b + c must lie in the plane of a and d if a and d are not collinear, and in the line of a and d, if they are collinear
    Answer: A
    Explanation: (a) Incorrect, In order to make vectors a + b + c + d = 0, it is not necessary to have all the four given vectors to be null vectors. There are many other combinations which can give the sum zero.
(b) Correct
We are given that ; a + b + c + d = 0
a + c = -(b + d)
Taking modulus on both sides, we get:
|a + c| = |-(b + d)| = |b + d|
Hence, the magnitude of (a + c) is the same as the magnitude of (b + d).
(c) Correct
We are given that , a + b + c + d = 0
a = ‚Äì (b + c + d)
Taking modulus on both sides, we get:
|a| = |b + c + d|; also
|a| $\leq$ |b| + |c| + |d| ...(i)
Equation (i) shows that the magnitude of a is equal to or less than the sum of the magnitudes of b, c, and d.
Hence, the magnitude of vector a can never be greater than the sum of the magnitudes of b, c, and d.
(d) Correct
From the given equation a + b + c + d = 0
a + (b + c) + d = 0
The resultant sum of the three vectors a, (b + c), and d can be zero only if (b + c) lie in a plane containing a and d, assuming that these three vectors are represented by the three sides of a triangle.
If a and d are collinear, then it implies that the vector (b + c) is in the line of a and d. This implication holds only then the vector sum of all the vectors will be zero.

Q14. Three girls skating on a circular ice ground of radius 200 m start from a point P on the edge of the ground and reach a point Q diametrically opposite to P following different paths as shown in figure. What is the magnitude of the displacement vector for each? For which girl is this equal to the actual length of path skate?
    (A) 200 m for each; B
    (B) 200 m for each; A
    (C) 300 m for each; C
    (D) 400 m for each; B   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: PQ = diameter = displacement for each girl = 2r = 2 $\times$ 200 = 400 m
 Since, displacement vector does not depend upon the actual path length and it is the shortest distance between initial and final position, so in the case of each girl the displacement is 400 m.
 This is equal to the actual length of the path skated by girl B.

Q15. A cyclist starts from the centre O of a circular park of radius 1 km, reaches the edge P of the park, then cycles along the circumference anticlockwise from P to Q, and returns to the centre along QO as shown in figure. If the round trip takes 10 min, what is the
 net displacement,
 average velocity, and
 average speed of the cyclist?
    (A) 0, 0, 15.4 km/hr
    (B) 0, 0, 27.4 km/hr
    (C) 0, 0, 21.4 km/hr   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0, 0, 11.4 km/hr
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Displacement is shortest distance b/w initial point and final point, as he returns back to origin after starting from origin, the displacement is zero. 
 Average velocity = $Displacement\over time\ taken $ 
 As displacement is zero, so average velocity is also eqaul to zero.
 Radius r = 1 km
 Distance covered = OP + PQ + QO
 $= r+{2\pi r\over 4}+r= 2r+{2\pi r\over 4}$ 
 = $2\times 1+{({2\over 4}\times {22\over 7}\times 1})$ 
 = $25\over 7$km
 Time taken = 10 minutes = $1\over 6$hour 
 Average speed $= {{25\over 7}\over {1\over 6}}= {25\times 6\over7}$= 21.4 km/h

Q1. A passenger arriving in a new town wishes to go from the station to a hotel located 10 km away on a straight road from the station. A dishonest cabman takes him along a circuitous path 23 km long and reaches the hotel in 28 min. What is
 the average speed of the taxi,
 the magnitude of average velocity?
    (A) 48.3 km/hr, 22.4 km/hr
    (B) 49.3 km/hr, 21.4 km/hr   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 46.3 km/hr, 24.4 km/hr
    (D) 47.3 km/hr, 23.4 km/hr
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Total distance travelled = 23 km
 Total time taken = 28 min = $28\over 60$ h
 $\therefore$ The average speed of the taxi = $Total\ distance \ travelled \over Total\ time\ taken$ 
 = $ {{23 \over 1}\over {28\over 60}} $ = 49.3 km/h
 Distance between the hotel and the station = 10 km = Displacement of the car
 $\therefore$ Average velocity = ${{10 \over 1}\over {28\over 60}} $ = 21.4 km/h

Q2. Rain is falling vertically with a speed of 30 m${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$. A woman rides a bicycle with a speed of 10 m${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ in the north to south direction. What is the direction in which she should hold her umbrella?
    (A) about ${\rm{28}}^\circ $ with the vertical, towards the south
    (B) about ${\rm{18}}^\circ $ with the vertical, towards the north
    (C) about ${\rm{28}}^\circ $ with the vertical, towards the north
    (D) about ${\rm{18}}^\circ $ with the vertical, towards the south   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The described situation is shown in the given figure.
Here,
v_c = Velocity of the cyclist
v_r = Velocity of falling rain
In order to protect herself from the rain, the woman must hold her umbrella in the direction of the relative velocity (v) of the rain with respect to the woman.
v = v_r + (-v_c) = 30 + (-10) = 20 m/s
tan $\theta $ = ${v_c \over v_r}= {10\over 30}$ 
$\theta $ = tan^-1 $1 \over 3$
$\theta $ $\approx$ 18^0
Hence, the woman must hold the umbrella toward the south, at an angle of nearly 18¬∞ with the vertical.

Q3. A man can swim with a speed of 4.0 km/h in still water. How long does he take to cross a river 1.0 km wide if the river flows steadily at 3.0 km/h and he makes his strokes normal to the river current? How far down the river does he go when he reaches the other bank?
    (A) 15 min, 750 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 16 min, 650 m
    (C) 19 min, 500 m
    (D) 13 min, 700 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Speed of the man, v_m = 4 km/h
Width of the river = 1 km
Time taken to cross the river = $Width \ of \ the \ river \over Speed \ of\ the\ man$ $={ 1\over 4} h = {1 √ó 60 \over 4 }= 15 \min$
Speed of the river, v_r = 3 km/h
Distance covered due to the flow of river = v_r √ó t
$= {3 √ó 1 \over 4} = {3 \over 4 }\ km = {3 √ó 1000 \over4}$ = 750 m

Q4. In a harbor, wind is blowing at the speed of 72 km/h and the flag on the mast of a boat anchored in the harbor flutters along the N-E direction. If the boat starts moving at a speed of 51 km/h to the north, what is the direction of the flag on the mast of the boat?
    (A) Approximately east   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Approximately north
    (C) Approximately south
    (D) Approximately north-east
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The flag is fluttering in the north-east direction. It shows that the wind is blowing toward the north-east direction. When the ship begins sailing toward the north, the flag will move along the direction of the relative velocity (v_wb) of the wind with respect to the boat.
The angle between v_w and (‚Äìv_b) = 90¬∞ + 45¬∞
tan $\beta$ = $51 ~Sin (90 + 45) \over 72 + 51~ Cos (90 + 45)$ 
Substituting and solving we get,
tan $\beta$ = ${51 \over 50.80} = 1.0038$ 
$\therefore$ $\beta$ = tan^-1(1.0038) = 45.110
Angle with respect to the east direction = 45.11¬∞ ‚Äì 45¬∞ = 0.11¬∞ with respect to east direction.
Hence, the flag will flutter approximately due east.

Q5. The ceiling of a long hall is 25 m high. What is the maximum horizontal distance that a ball thrown with a speed of 40 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ can go without hitting the ceiling of the hall?
    (A) 25 m
    (B) 120 m
    (C) 165 m
    (D) 150.5 m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Maximum height, h = 25 m
In projectile motion, the maximum height reached by a body projected at an angle Œ∏, is given by the relation:
h = $u^2 Sin^2Œ∏ \over 2g$
$\Rightarrow$ 25 = $ (40)^2 Sin^2Œ∏ \over 2 √ó 9.8$
= sin^2Œ∏ = 0.30625
sin Œ∏ = 0.5534
‚à¥ Œ∏ = sin^‚Äì1(0.5534) = 33.60¬∞
Horizontal range, R = $u^2 Sin 2Œ∏ \over g$
= $(40)^2 √ó Sin (2 √ó 33.600) \over 9.8$
= $1600 √ó Sin (67.2) \over 9.8$
= $1600 √ó 0.922 \over 9.8 $ = 150.5 m

Q6. A cricketer can throw a ball to a maximum horizontal distance of 100 m. How much high above the ground can the cricketer throw the same ball?
    (A) 60 m
    (B) 65 m
    (C) 76 m
    (D) 50 m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Maximum horizontal distance, R = 100 m
The cricketer will only be able to throw the ball to the maximum horizontal distance when the angle of projection is 45¬∞, i.e., Œ∏ = 45¬∞.
The horizontal range for a projection velocity v, is given by the relation:
R = $u^2 Sin~ 2\theta \over g$
100 = $u^2 Sin ~90¬∞ \over g$
$\Rightarrow$ $u^2 \over g $ = 100 ...‚Ä¶.(i)
The ball will achieve the maximum height when it is thrown vertically upward. For such motion, the final velocity $\vec v$ is zero at the maximum height H.
Acceleration, a = ‚Äì g
Using the third equation of motion, we get
v^2 ‚Äì u^2 = - 2gH
$H ={ u^2 \over 2g} = {100 \over 2 } = 50 m$ [By using (i)]

Q7. A stone tied to the end of a string 80 cm long is whirled in a horizontal circle with a constant speed. If the stone makes 14 revolutions in 25 s, what is the magnitude and direction of acceleration of the stone?
    (A) 9.9 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ , along the radius at every point away from the center
    (B) 10.2 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ , along the radius at every point towards the center
    (C) 9.9 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$, along the radius at every point towards the center   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 11.9 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ , along the radius at every point away from the center
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Length of the string, $l$ = 80 cm = 0.8 m
Number of revolutions = 14
Time taken = 25 s
Frequency, $\nu ={ Number \ of\ revolutions \over Time\ taken} = {14 \over 25} Hz$
Angular frequency, $\omega = 2\pi\nu$ = $2 √ó{ 22\over 7}√ó {14\over25} = {88 \over 25} \ rad \ s^{-1}$
Centripetal acceleration, a_c = œâ^2r = $ ({88\over 25})^2 √ó 0.8$ = 9.9 ms^-2
The direction of centripetal acceleration is always directed along the string, towards the centre, at all points.

Q8. An aircraft executes a horizontal loop of radius 1.00 km with a steady speed of 900 km/h. Compare its centripetal acceleration with the acceleration due to gravity.
    (A) 5 g
    (B) 23 g
    (C) 10 g
    (D) 6.4 g   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Radius of the loop, r = 1 km = 1000 m
Speed of the aircraft, v = 900 km/h
= $900\times {5\over 18}= 250\ m/s$
Centripetal acceleration, $a_c={v^2\over r}$ = ${(250)^2\over 1000}={62500\over 1000}=62.5\ m/s^2$
Acceleration due to gravity, g = 9.8 m/s‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
${a_c\over g}={62.5\over 9.8}$ = 6.4 g

Q9. Which of the following statements not true?
 The net acceleration of a particle in a circular motion is always along the radius of the circle towards the centre
 The acceleration vector of a particle in uniform circular motion averaged over one cycle is a null vector
 The net acceleration of a particle in uniform circular motion is always along the radius of the circle towards the centre
 The velocity vector of a particle at a point is always along the tangent to the path of the particle at that point.
    (A) (B)
    (B) (D)
    (C) (A)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (C)

Q10. The position of a particle is given by, $r = 3.0t\hat i - 2.0{t^2}\hat j + 4.0\hat k$. What is the velocity and acceleration of the particle?
    (A) $5.0\hat i - 4.0t\hat j$, $-3.0\hat j$
    (B) $4.0\hat i - 4.0t\hat j$, $-3.0\hat j$
    (C) $3.0\hat i - 4.0t\hat j$, $-4.0\hat j$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $2.0\hat i - 4.0t\hat j$, $-2.0\hat j$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Position vector, $\vec r = 3.0t\hat i-2.0t^2\hat j+4.0\hat k$
We know velocity is given by
$\vec v ={d\vec r\over dt}$
So, $\vec v = 3.0\hat i-4.0t\hat j$
Acceleration is given by 
$\vec a={d\vec v\over dt}$
So, $\vec a =-4.0\hat j$

Q11. The position of a particle is given by $\vec r = 3.0t\hat i + 2.0{t^2}\hat j + 4.0\hat k$. Find the magnitude and direction of the velocity of the particle at t = 2.0 s.
    (A) 7.54 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$, ${\rm{72}}^\circ $ with x-axis
    (B) 6.54 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$, ${\rm{74}}^\circ $ with x-axis
    (C) 8.84 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$, ${\rm{75}}^\circ $ with x-axis
    (D) 8.54 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$, ${\rm{7}}0^\circ $ with x-axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Position vector is given by, $\vec r= 3.0t\hat i+2.0t^2\hat j+4.0\hat k$
We know velocity is given by:-
$\vec v ={dr\over dt}$
So, $\vec v = 3.0\hat i+4t\hat j$
Velocity after 2 seconds is:
$\vec v= 3\hat i+8\hat j$
Magnitude of velocity = $\sqrt {(3)^2+(8)^2}$ = $\sqrt {73}$= 8.54 ms^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã-1
Direction is given by
$\theta = tan^{-1}({8\over 3})= 69.5\approx 70¬∞ $ with x-axis

Q12. A particle starts from the origin at t = 0 s with a velocity of 10.0 $\hat j$ m/s and moves in the x-y plane with a constant acceleration of (8.0$\hat i$ + 2.0$\hat j$) m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$. At what time is the x-coordinate of the particle 16 m? What is the y-coordinate of the particle at that time?
    (A) 1.5 s, 20 m
    (B) 2.2 s, 22 m
    (C) 1 s, 14 m
    (D) 2 s, 24 m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: u = u_x$\hat i$ + u_y$\hat j$ = 10$\hat j$, u_x = 0 and u_y = 10 m/s
a = a_x$\hat i$ + a_y$\hat j$ = 8i + 2j,
a_x = 8 and a_y = 2 m/s^2
x = u_xt +$1\over 2$a_xt^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 16 = $8 t^2\over 2$
$\Rightarrow$ t = 2 sec 
y = u_yt + $a_yt^2\over 2$ = 10 $\times$ 2 + $2\times 2^2\over 2$ = 24 m

Q13. An aircraft is flying at a height of 3400 m above the ground. If the angle subtended at a ground observation point by the aircraft positions 10.0 s apart is 30^o, what is the speed of the aircraft?
    (A) 193 m/s
    (B) 172 m/s
    (C) 182 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 192 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The positions of the observer and the aircraft are shown in the given figure.
Height of the aircraft from ground is given by, OR = 3400 m
Angle subtended between the positions is given by, $\angle$POQ = 30¬∞
Time = 10 s
In $\triangle$PRO, we have
tan 15^¬∞ = $PR \over OR$
PR = OR tan 15^¬∞ = $3400 \times tan 15¬∞$ 
$\triangle$PRO is similar to $\triangle$RQO.
$\therefore$ PR = RQ
PQ = PR + RQ = 2PR = 2 $\times$ 3400 tan 15^¬∞
= 6800 $\times$ 0.268 = 1822.4 m
$\therefore$ Speed of the aircraft is given by = $1822.4\over 10 $ 
= 182.24 m/s $\approx$ 182 m/s

Q14. A fighter plane flying horizontally at an altitude of 1.5 km with speed 720 km/h passes directly overhead an anti-aircraft gun. At what angle from the vertical should the gun be fired for the shell with muzzle speed 600 ms^‚àí1 to hit the plane? At what minimum altitude should the pilot fly the plane to avoid being hit? (Take g = 10 ms^‚àí2).
    (A) at an angle of 19.5^o with the vertical, 16 km   <-- CORRECT
    (B) at an angle of 21.5^o with the vertical, 15 km
    (C) at an angle of 23.5^o with the vertical, 17 km
    (D) at an angle of 20.5^o with the vertical, 12 km
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Height of the fighter plane = 1.5 km = 1500 m
Speed of the fighter plane, v = 720 km/h = 200 m/s
Let $\theta$ be the angle with the vertical so that the shell hits the plane. The situation is shown in the given figure.
Muzzle velocity of the gun, u = 600 m/s
Time taken by the shell to hit the plane = t
Horizontal distance travelled by the shell = u_xt
Distance travelled by the plane = vt
The shell hits the plane. Hence, these two distances must be equal.
u_xt = vt
u Sin $\theta$ = v
Sin $\theta$ = ${v \over u} = {200 \over 600} $ = 0.33
$\theta$ = Sin^-1(0.33) = 19.5^0
In order to avoid being hit by the shell, the pilot must fly the plane at an altitude (H) higher than the maximum height achieved by the shell.
$\therefore$ H = ${u^2sin^2 (90 ‚Äì Œ∏) \over 2g} ={ (600)^2 cos^2 Œ∏ \over 2g}$
= $360000 \times cos^2 (19.5)\over 2 \times 10$
= 16006.482 m
$\approx$ 16 km

Q15. A cyclist is riding with a speed of 27 km/h. As he approaches a circular turn on the road of radius 80 m, he applies brakes and reduces his speed at the constant rate of 0.50 m/s every second. What is the magnitude and direction of the net acceleration of the cyclist on the circular turn?
    (A) 0.84 ms^‚àí2, 58.5^o with the direction of the velocity
    (B) 0.86 ms^‚àí2, 54.5^o with the direction of the velocity.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.82 ms^‚àí2, 59.5^o with the direction of the velocity
    (D) 0.85 ms^‚àí2, 56.5^o with the direction of the velocity.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Speed of the cyclist, v = 27 km/h = 7.5 m/s
The radius of the circular turn, r = 80 m
Centripetal acceleration is given as:
a_c = ${v^2\over r} ={ (7.5)^2 \over 80 }=$ 0.7 ms^-2
The situation is shown in the given figure:
Suppose the cyclist begins cycling from point P and moves toward point Q. At point Q, he applies the breaks and decelerates the speed of the bicycle by 0.5 m/s^2.
This acceleration is along the tangent at Q and opposite to the direction of the motion of the cyclist.
Since the angle between a_c and a_T is 90^0, the resultant acceleration is given by:
a = $\sqrt {(a_c)^2 + (a_T)^2} $ = $\sqrt{ (0.7)^2 + (0.5)^2 }$
= $\sqrt {0.74}$ = 0.86 ms^-2
tan $\theta $ = $a_c \over a_T$
where $\theta $ is the angle of the resultant with the direction of velocity.
tan $\theta $ = $0.7 \over 0.5 $= 1.4
$\theta $ = tan^-1(1.4) = 54.46^o with the direction of velocity.

Q1. A ball is thrown upwards with an initial velocity of 10 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$. Determine the maximum height reached above the thrower‚Äôs hand.
    (A) 5.10 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 5.25 m
    (C) 5.23 m
    (D) 5.43 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Initial velocity is given by ,u = 10m/s
As at the maximum height ball will stop, so final velocity is given by v = 0 m/s
Only acceleration working on it is the acceleration due to gravity g = -9.8m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Let height = h
We know that, $v^2-u^2= 2as$
$\Rightarrow$ $(0)^2-(10)^2= 2\times (-9.8)h$
$\Rightarrow$ $h = {-100\over -19.6}$ = 5.10 m

Q2. A cricketer hits a cricket ball from the ground so that it goes directly upwards. If the ball takes, 10 s to return to the ground, determine its maximum height.
    (A) 132.5 m
    (B) 152.5 m
    (C) 112.5 m
    (D) 122.5 m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: We know that at the maximum height, the velocity of the ball is 0 m/s.
We also know that the ball takes the same time to reach its maximum height as it takes to travel from its maximum height to the initial position, due to time symmetry. The time taken is half the total time.
Therefore, we have the following information for the second (downward) part of the motion of the ball:
t = 5 seconds (half of the total time)
$v_{top} = 0 \ m/s$
g = 9.8 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2 downward
s = ?
We know that
s = ut+${1\over 2}gt^2$
Put all the given value, we get
$\Rightarrow$ s = $0\times 5+ {1\over 2}\times 9.8\times 25$
$\Rightarrow$ s = 122.5 m

Q3. As a ball rises, the vertical component of its velocity
    (A) Remains constant
    (B) Increase
    (C) Decrease   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Can't be determined
    Answer: C
    Explanation: If a ball is thrown upward at an angle, the ball has a vertical and a horizontal component of velocity. The force of gravity is acting on it and its acceleration is in the downward direction. The vertical component of velocity is therefore changing. As the motion and acceleration is in opposite direction so vertical component of velocity decrease.

Q4. The reason why cyclists bank when taking a sharp turn is:
    (A) cyclists enjoy turning to one side and so bank.
    (B) to supply the sidewise (centripetal) acceleration required to make the direction change.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) to decelerate at the turns as turns are dangerous.
    (D) to supply the acceleration required to move fast.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In order to make a safe turn, the cyclist has to bend a little from his vertical position. In this case, a component of the reaction provides the required centripetal force.
If $\theta$ is an angle made by the cyclist with the vertical then‚Äã
‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã
N cos$\theta$ = mg ....(1)
N sin$\theta$ = ${mv^2\over r} $.....(2)
Dividing (2) by (1), we get
$\tan\theta = {v^2\over rg}$ 
$\Rightarrow$‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã $\theta = tan^{-1}( {v^2\over rg})$
In actual practice, the value of $\theta$ is slightly less because the force of friction also contributes towards the centripetal force.

Q5. A motorcycle stunt rider rides off the edge of a cliff. Just at the edge his velocity is horizontal, with magnitude 9.0 m/s. Find the magnitude of the motorcycle‚Äôs position vector after 0.50s it leaves the edge of the cliff.
    (A) 4.3 m
    (B) 3.5 m
    (C) 4.7 m   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 5.2 m
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The motorcycle‚Äôs x- and y-coordinates at t=0.50 s are given by ;
x = v_ox t = $9.0 \times 0.50$ = 4.5 m
y = $-{1\over 2} gt^2$ = $- {1\over 2}\times 9.8\times (0.50)^2$= -1.2m
The negative value of y shows that the motorcycle is below its starting point.
The motorcycle‚Äôs distance from the origin is given by , r = $\sqrt {x^2+y^2}= \sqrt {(4.5)^2+(-1.2)^2}$ = 4.7 m

Q6. A motorcycle stunt rider rides off the edge of a cliff. Just at the edge, his velocity is horizontal, with a magnitude of 9.0 m/s. Find the magnitude of the motorcycle‚Äôs velocity vector, 0.50 s after it leaves the edge of the cliff.
    (A) 10.2 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 9.65 m/s
    (C) 8.98 m/s
    (D) 11.3 m/s
    Answer: A
    Explanation: the velocity components at t = 0.50 s are
v_x = v_ox = 9.0m/s 
v_y = ‚àígt = ‚àí9.8 $\times$ 0.50 = ‚àí4.9m/s 
The motorcycle has the same horizontal velocity v_x as when it left the cliff at t = 0, but in addition there is a downward (negative) vertical velocity v_y.
The velocity vector at t = 0.50 s is given by ,
$\vec v= v_x\hat i+v_y\hat j= 9.0\hat i+(-4.9)\hat j$ 
at t = 0.50 s the velocity has magnitude v is given by,
v = $\sqrt {(v_x)^2+(v_y)^2}=\sqrt {(9.0)^2+(-4.9)^2}$ 
Hence, velocity is v = 10.2 m/s

Q7. A batter hits a baseball so that it leaves the bat at speed ${{\rm{v}}_0}$= 37.0 m/s at an angle a = 53.1^o. Find the position of the ball and its velocity (magnitude and direction) at t = 2.00s.
    (A) 25.4 m/s at 23.2$^\circ $ above the horizontal
    (B) 26.4 m/s at 23.2$^\circ $ above the horizontal
    (C) 27.4 m/s at 21.2$^\circ $ above the horizontal
    (D) 24.4 m/s at 24.2$^\circ $ above the horizontal   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: We want to find x, y, v_x, and v_y at t = 2.00 s.
The initial velocity of the ball has components
v_ox = v_ o cos $\alpha_o$= $37.0 \times cos 53.1¬∞$ 
= 22.2 m/s 
v_oy = vo_ o sin $\alpha_o$= $37.0\times sin 53.1¬∞$ 
= 29.6 m/s
From above equations value of x and y at the = 2.0 s
x = v_ox t = $22.2 \times 2.0$ = 44.4 m
$y=v_{oy} t-{1\over 2} gt^2 $ ‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã
$=29.6 \times 2.0 -{1\over 2} \times 9.8\times (2.0) ^2$ 
= 39.6 m‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã
$v_x=v_{ox}=22.2 \ m/s $ ‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã
$v_y=v_{oy}-gt$ ‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã
$= 29.6 -9.8\times 2.0 =10.0 m/s$ 
The y-component of velocity is positive at t=2.0 s, so the ball is still moving upward the magnitude and direction of the velocity are
v = $\sqrt {(v_x)^2+(v_y)^2} $ 
= $\sqrt {(22.2)^2+(10)^2}=24.4 m/s$ ‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã
$\alpha = tan^{-1}({10.0 \over22.2 }) $ 
= $tan^{-1}0.45=24.2¬∞$ 
The ball is moving at 24.4 m/s in a direction 24.2¬∞ above the horizontal

Q8. A batter hits a baseball so that it leaves the bat at speed v_0 = 37.0 m/s at an angle a = 53.1^o. Find the time when the ball reaches the highest point of its flight, and its height h at this time?
    (A) 3.32 s, 41.7 m
    (B) 3.12 s, 43.7 m
    (C) 3.02 s, 44.7 m   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3.22 s, 42.7 m
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The initial velocity of the ball has components
v_ox = v_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äão cos $\alpha_o$= 37.0 $\times$ cos53.1^o
= 22.2 m/s
v_oy = v_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äão sin $\alpha_o$= 37.0 $\times$ sin 53.1^o
= 29.6 m/s
At the highest point, the vertical velocity v_y is zero. Call the time when this happens t_1; then
v_y = v_oy - gt_1 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ t_1 = $v_{oy}\over g$ = $29.6\over 9.8$ = 3.02 s
The height at the highest point is the value of y at time t_‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã1:
$h=v_{oy} t_1-{1\over2} g(t_1)^2 $
$=29.6\times 3.02 - {1\over 2}\times 9.8 \times (3.02 )^2$
= 44.7 m

Q9. A batter hits a baseball so that it leaves the bat at a speed ${{\rm{v}}_0}$ = 37.0 m/s at an angle a = 53.1^o. Find the horizontal range R-that is, the horizontal distance from the starting point to where the ball hits the ground?
    (A) 133 m
    (B) 134 m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 123 m
    (D) 213 m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The initial velocity of the ball has components
v_ox = v_o cos $\alpha_o$= 37.0 $\times$ cos53.1^o
= 22.2 m/s 
v_oy = v_o sin $\alpha_o$= 37.0 $\times$ sin 53.1^o
= 29.6 m/s
We‚Äôll find the horizontal range in two steps. First, we find the time t_2 when y = 0 (the ball is at ground level):
$y=0=v_{oy}t_2-{1\over 2} g(t_2)^2 $
$\Rightarrow t_2(v_{oy}-{1\over 2} gt_2)= 0$
This is a quadratic equation for t_2.
It has two roots:
t_2 = 0 and t_2 = $2v_{oy}\over g$ = ${2\times 29.6\over 9.80 }$ = 6.04 s
The ball is at y = 0 at both times. The ball leaves the ground at t_2 = 0, and it hits the ground at t_2 = 6.04 s.
The horizontal range R is the value of x when the ball returns to the ground at t_2 = 6.04 s:
R = vox $\times$ t_2 = 22.2 $\times$ 6.04 = 134 m

Q10. A sports car has a ‚Äúlateral acceleration‚Äù of 0.96g = 9.4 ms^-2. This is the maximum centripetal acceleration the car can sustain without skidding out of a curved path. If the car is travelling at a constant 40 m/s on level ground, what is the radius R of the tightest unbanked curve it can negotiate?
    (A) minimum radius = 175 m
    (B) minimum radius = 180 m
    (C) minimum radius = 160 m
    (D) minimum radius = 170 m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The car is in a uniform circular motion because it‚Äôs moving at a constant speed along a curve that is a segment of a circle. Hence we know
R =$v^2\over a_{rad}$ = $(40)^2\over 9.4 $ = 170 m
This is the minimum turning radius because a_rad is the maximum centripetal acceleration.

Q11. Passengers on a carnival ride move at constant speed in a horizontal circle of radius 5.0 m, making a complete circle in 4.0 s. What is their acceleration?
    (A) 12 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 15 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (C) 14 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (D) 16 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The speed is constant, so this is uniform circular motion. We are given the radius R = 5.0 m and the period T = 4.0 s, so we can calculate the acceleration directly using equation
$a_{rad}={4(\pi)^2 R\over T^2}$ = $4\times 22\times 22\times 5.0\over 7\times 7 \times 4.0\times 4.0$ = 12m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2

Q12. A projectile is fired a velocity of 150 meters per second at an angle of 30 degrees with the horizontal. What is the magnitude of the vertical component of the velocity at the time the projectile is fired?
    (A) 75 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 225 m/s
    (C) 150 m/s
    (D) 130 m/s
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Initial velocity, u = 150 m/s
Angle $\theta = 30^¬∞$
Vertical component is given by 
$v_y=usin\theta$ $= 150sin30^¬∞= 150\times {1\over 2}$
= 75 m/s

Q13. An airplane‚Äôs compass indicates that it is headed due north, and its airspeed indicator shows that it is moving through the air at 240 km/h. If there is a 100-kmh^-1 wind from west to east, what is the velocity of the airplane relative to the earth?
    (A) 260 km/h 23^o E of N   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 255 km/h 26^o E of N
    (C) 250 km/h 25^o E of N
    (D) 270 km/h 24^o E of N
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This problem involves velocities in two dimensions (northward and eastward), so it is a relative velocity problem using vectors. We are given the magnitude and direction of the velocity of the plane (P) relative to the air (A). We are also given the magnitude and direction of the wind velocity, which is the velocity of the air A with respect to the earth (E): 
$\vec v_{P/A}$= 240 km/h due north 
$\vec v_{A/E}$=100 km/h due east
The magnitude and direction of the velocity $\vec v_{P/E}$ of the plane relative to the earth ,is given by ;
$\vec v_{P/E}= \vec v_{P/A}+ \vec v_{A/E}$ 
The image above shows that the three relative velocities constitute a right-triangle vector addition; the unknowns are the speed $v_{P/E }$and the angle $\alpha $ , these values are calculated by:-
$v_{P/E}=\sqrt {(240)^2+(100)^2}$ = 260 km/h
$\alpha$ = $tan^{-1} ({100 \over 240})$= 23^o E of N

Q14. An airplane‚Äôs compass indicates that it is headed due north, and its airspeed indicator shows that it is moving through the air at 240 km/h. If there is a 100-km/h wind from west to east. In what direction should the pilot head to travel due north? What will be her velocity relative to the earth?
    (A) 23^o W of N, 260 km/h   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 28^o W of N, 260 km/h
    (C) 29^o W of N, 200 km/h
    (D) 35^o W of N, 198 km/h
    Answer: A
    Explanation: This is a relative velocity problem with vectors. The image given is a scale drawing of the situation. Again the vectors form a right triangle is given by:-
$\vec v_{P/E}= \vec v_{P/A}+ \vec v_{A/E}$ 
As shown in the image, The pilot points the nose of the airplane at an angle $\beta $ into the wind to compensate for the crosswind. This angle, which tells us the direction of the vector $\vec v_{P/A}$(the velocity of the airplane relative to the air), is one of our target variables. The other target variable is the speed of the airplane over the ground, which is the magnitude of the vector $\vec v_{P/E}$ (the velocity of the airplane relative to the earth). The known and unknown quantities are:$\vec v_{P/E} $ = is the magnitude unknown due to North
$\vec v_{P/A}$ = 240 km/h due to north 
$\vec v_{A/E}$ = 100 km/h due to east
We‚Äôll solve for the target variables by using image and trigonometry. thus,
$v_{P/E}=\sqrt {(240)^2+(100)^2}$ = 260km/h
$\beta =sin^{-1} ({100 \over 240})$= 23^¬∞ 
The pilot should point the airplane 23^o west of north, and his ground speed will be 260 km/h.

Q15. At a distance L = 400m from the traffic lights, the brakes are applied to a locomotive moving at a velocity v = 54km/hr. Determine the position of locomotive relative to the traffic lights 1 minute after the application of the brakes if its acceleration is -0.3m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2?
    (A) 40 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 30 m
    (C) 50 m
    (D) 15 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Initial velocity u = 54 km/h = 15 m/s
Let Final velocity v = 0
Acceleration a = -0.3 m/s^‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã‚Äã2
Time taken to stop = t
Using v = u + at
 $\Rightarrow$ 0 = 15 + (-0.3)t
$\Rightarrow$ t = 50 sec
It means it has been stopped before 1 minute.
So distance covered in 1 minute is given by 
s= ut +1/2 at^2
 = 15 $\times$ 60 + 1/2 $\times$ (-0.3) $\times$ (60)^2
 = 360 m
Position of locomotive relative to the traffic lights = 400 - 360 = 40 m
