Q1. Force is required:
    (A) only to keep an object moving
    (B) to start a stationary object and to stop a moving object   <-- CORRECT
    (C) only to start a stationary object moving
    (D) only to stop a moving object
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Force is required to start a stationary object and to stop a moving object due to inertia.

Q2. According to the first law of motion:
    (A) body acted on by no net force moves with increasing velocity and negative acceleration
    (B) body acted on by net force moves with constant velocity (which may be zero)
    (C) body acted on by zero net force moves with non zero acceleration
    (D) body acted on by no net force moves with constant velocity (which may be zero) and zero acceleration   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If net force act on a body then the acceleration of the body will also be zero. Hence velocity will not be changed i.e. it continues in its existing state of rest or uniform motion in a straight line.

Q3. Inertia refers to:
    (A) ease of motion
    (B) dullness
    (C) resistance to change   <-- CORRECT
    (D) slow motion
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Inertia is the resistance of any physical object to any change in its state of motion; this includes changes to its speed, direction, or state of rest. It is the tendency of objects to keep moving in a straight line at a constant velocity. Inertia is a property of matter by which it continues in its existing state of rest or uniform motion in a straight line unless that state is changed by an external force.

Q4. The momentum of a body is:
    (A) a vector equal in magnitude to the product of mass and average speed and direction being that of velocity
    (B) a scalar equal in magnitude to the product of mass and velocity
    (C) a vector equal in magnitude to the product of mass and acceleration and direction being that of velocity
    (D) a vector equal in magnitude to the product of mass and instantaneous velocity and direction being that of instantaneous velocity   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\vec p=m\vec v$

Q5. According to Newton's second law of motion:
    (A) The momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction opposite to the force
    (B) The integration of the momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction in which the force acts
    (C) The rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction in which the force acts   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction in which the force acts
    Answer: C
    Explanation: If the mass does not change then the acceleration of a particle is dependent on the forces acting upon the particle and the particle's mass. For a given particle, if the net force is increased, the acceleration is increased. For a given net force, the more mass a particle has, the less acceleration it has.
${\displaystyle \mathbf {F} =m\mathbf {a} =m{\frac {\mathrm {d} \mathbf {v} }{\mathrm {d} t}}={\frac {\mathrm {d} (m\mathbf {v} )}{\mathrm {d} t}}={\frac {\mathrm {d} \mathbf {p} }{\mathrm {d} t}}}.$
hence the rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force.

Q6. What is a force:
    (A) quantitative measure of the momentum between two bodies
    (B) quantitative measure of the interaction between two bodies   <-- CORRECT
    (C) qualitative measure of the momentum of two bodies
    (D) qualitative measure of the interaction between two bodies
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Newton's second law of motion gives the quantitative definition of force. The acceleration of an object as produced by a net force is directly proportional to the magnitude of the net force, in the same direction as the net force, and inversely proportional to the mass of the object.

Q7. The second law in terms of momentum p and mass m is:
    (A) $\vec{F}=k p \frac{\vec{d p}}{d t}$
    (B) F = kpp
    (C) $\vec{F}=k\frac{d\vec{p}}{dt}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) F = kp
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The applied force is directly proportional to the rate of change of momentum.

Q8. The second law of motion in terms of acceleration $\vec{a}$ and mass m of a body is:
    (A) $\vec{F}=m\vec{a}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\vec{F}=m\vec{a}\vec{a}$
    (C) $\vec{F}=m^2\vec{a}$
    (D) $\vec{F}=k\;m^{-1}\vec{a}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The second law states that the rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the force applied, and this change in momentum takes place in the direction of the applied force.
$\vec F = {{d\vec p} \over {dt}} = {{d\left( {m\vec v} \right)} \over {dt}}$
$\vec F = m{{d\vec v} \over {dt}} + \vec v{{dm} \over {dt}} $ 
if mass is constant, then
${{dm} \over {dt}} = 0$
$ \vec F = m{{d\vec v} \over {dt}}$
$ \vec F = m\vec a $

Q9. When several forces act on a body:
    (A) the effect on its motion is the same as when a single force, an algebraic sum only in the horizontal direction, acts on the body.
    (B) the effect on its motion is the same as when a single force, equal to the vector sum (resultant) of the forces, acts on the body.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the effect on its motion is the same as when a single force acts on the body.
    (D) the effect on its motion will be equal to a single force equal to the algebraic sum of the forces.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Force is a vector quantity. When several forces act on a body the effect on its motion is the same as when a single force, equal to the vector sum (resultant) of the forces, acts on the body
${{\vec F}_{net}} = {{\vec F}_1} + {{\vec F}_2} + {{\vec F}_3}.........$
${{\vec F}_{net}} = m{{\vec a}_1} + m{{\vec a}_2} + m{{\vec a}_3} + .........$ 
${{\vec F}_{net}} = m{{\vec a}_{net}} $

Q10. If a body is in equilibrium:
    (A) $\sum\vec{F}=0$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\mathop \sum \nolimits F$ > 0
    (C) $\mathop \sum \nolimits F$ < 0
    (D) $\mathop \sum \nolimits F$ depends on time
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The vector sum of all the forces acting on a body is zero.

Q11. The second law of motion is a vector law. It is equivalent to:
    (A) Three equations, one for each component of the vectors   <-- CORRECT
    (B) One equation, one for each component of the vectors
    (C) Two equations, one for each component of the vectors
    (D) Four equations, one for each component of the vectors and one for time
    Answer: A
    Explanation: F_x = ma_x, F_y = ma_y, F_z = ma_z

Q12. If Newton's second law is applied to a rigid body:
    (A) the acceleration is the average of all particles in the body
    (B) the acceleration is that of any particle in the body
    (C) the acceleration is that of the centre of mass   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the acceleration is the higher of all particles in the body
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A rigid body is characterized by the fact that the distances between any two particles that make up the body are constant in time. This means that instead of talking about the motion of each particle, we can talk about the motion of any one point in the body and of the body as a whole with reference to this one particle. The most convenient choice for this one point is the Centre of Mass
${{\vec a}_{cm}} = {{{m_1}{{\vec a}_1} + {m_2}{{\vec a}_2} + .....} \over M}$
$M{{\vec a}_{cm}} = \sum {m\vec a}$ 
$\vec F = \sum {m\vec a}$ , here F refers to the total external force

Q13. Force F at a point in space (location of the particle) at a certain instant of time t is:
    (A) related to acceleration a at previous point at that instant.
    (B) related to acceleration a at that point at previous instant.
    (C) related to acceleration a at that point at next instant.
    (D) related to acceleration a at that point and the same instant.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: According to Newton's second law of motion, the acceleration of a point mass as produced by a net force is directly proportional to the magnitude of the net force at that point in the same direction as the net force at that instant
F = ma

Q14. The force acting on a freely falling body in terms of mass m and acceleration due to gravity g is:
    (A) F = mg^2
    (B) F = mg   <-- CORRECT
    (C) F = m^2g
    (D) F = m^‚àí2g
    Answer: B
    Explanation: according to newton's second law of motion 
F = ma
here acceleration is due to gravity and is equal to g.
So that for a freely falling body
F = mg

Q15. Impulse is:
    (A) the difference of force over a short period
    (B) the integral of force over a short period   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the derivative of force over a short period
    (D) the average of force over a short period
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A resultant force causes acceleration and a change in the velocity of the body for as long as it acts. The change in momentum is equal to the product of the average force and duration. Conversely, a small force applied for a long time produces the same change in momentum, the same impulse, as a larger force applied for a short time interval.
Impulse J is
J = F_average(t_2‚àít_1)
The impulse is the integral of the resultant force (F) with respect to time
$J = \int\limits_{{t_1}}^{{t_2}} {F.dt} $

========================================================================
Laws of Motion Test 02  (id 548) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Physics > Laws of Motion
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Impulse is a
    (A) scalar and equals the change of mass
    (B) vector and equals the change of momentum   <-- CORRECT
    (C) vector and equals the change of mass
    (D) vector and equals the inertia of momentum
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since force is a vector quantity, the impulse is also a vector in the same direction.
Impulse J produced from time t_1 to t_2 is defined to be
${\ {J} =\int _{t_{1}}^{t_{2}}\ {F} \,\mathrm {d} t}$ 
where F is the resultant force applied from t_1 to t_2
force is related to momentum p by
F = $dp\over dt$
therefore, 
$\mathbf{J}=\int_{t_{1}}^{t_{2}} \frac{\mathrm{d} \mathbf{p}}{\mathrm{d} t} \mathrm{d} t$
$=\int_{p_{1}}^{p_{2}} \mathrm{d} \mathbf{p}$
$=\mathbf{p}_{2}-\mathbf{p}_{1}=\Delta \mathbf{p}$ 
where $\Delta p$ is the change in linear momentum from time t_1 to t_2.

Q2. Newton‚Äôs third law states that:
    (A) they exert forces on each other that at some instants are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction
    (B) they exert forces on each other that at some instants are equal in magnitude and same in direction
    (C) they exert forces on each other that at each instant are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) they exert forces on each other that at each instant are equal in magnitude and same in the direction
    Answer: C
    Explanation: When one body exerts a force on a second body, the second body simultaneously exerts a force equal in magnitude and opposite in direction on the first body. According to Newton's law for every action, there is always opposit and equal reaction or the mutual actions of two bodies upon each other are always equal and opposite in direction.

Q3. According to Newton's third law of motion, the action and reaction forces are:
    (A) not equal in magnitude and opposite in direction
    (B) not equal in magnitude and same in direction
    (C) equal in magnitude and opposite in direction   <-- CORRECT
    (D) equal in magnitude and same in direction
    Answer: C
    Explanation: When one body exerts a force on a second body, the second body simultaneously exerts a force equal in magnitude and opposite in direction on the first body. To every action, there is always opposed an equal reaction or the mutual actions of two bodies upon each other are always equal and opposite in direction.

Q4. According to the law of conservation of momentum:
    (A) the momentum of an interacting system of particles and fields is conserved
    (B) the momentum of an isolated system of interacting particles is conserved
    (C) the total momentum of an interacting system of particles and fields is conserved
    (D) the total momentum of an isolated system of interacting particles is conserved   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: when no external forces act on a system of several interacting particles, then the total momentum is conserved.

Q5. When bodies are in contact with each other then:
    (A) contact forces are not equal and in the same direction
    (B) contact forces are equal and opposite in direction   <-- CORRECT
    (C) contact forces are equal and in the same direction
    (D) contact forces are not equal and opposite in direction
    Answer: B
    Explanation: according to newton's third law of motion for every action, there is always equal and opposite reaction or the mutual actions of two bodies upon each other. Whenever two objects interact with each other, then the pair of forces acting on them are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction. Contact forces are mutual forces (action and reaction).

Q6. Friction is:
    (A) perpendicular to contact surface and opposes motion
    (B) parallel to contact surface and opposes the relative motion   <-- CORRECT
    (C) perpendicular to contact surface and aids motion
    (D) parallel to contact surface and aids motion
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Whenever a body of mass 'm' moves or tends to move over the surface of another body, then the opposite force acts parallel to the surface contact which opposes the relative motion.

Q7. Static friction force:
    (A) decreases before moving and increases later
    (B) is a strong interaction force
    (C) remains constant
    (D) increases until the body start to move   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It is the maximum friction, where a body just starts to move over the surface. 
for example. A large block of mass m is placed on a horizontal table. Apply a small force. the block does not move due to the friction force which balances the applied force. Now Gradually increase the applied force until it starts moving. This maximum applied force acting in the opposite direction is called Static Friction.

Q8. Rolling friction is:
    (A) greater than static friction
    (B) greater than or equal to static friction
    (C) equal to static friction
    (D) less than static friction   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As the area of contact is less in the case of rolling than in the case of sliding. In the rolling, the surfaces of contact do not rub each other. The velocity of the point of contact with respect to the surface remains zero all the time although the Centre of the mass of the wheel moves forward. Hence rolling friction is negligible in comparison to static friction.

Q9. The magnitude of the centripetal force is given by:
    (A) $F = m\frac{{v^2}}{{2R}}$
    (B) $F = 2m\frac{{v^2}}{R}$
    (C) $F = m\frac{{v^2}} {R}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $F = m\frac{8{v^2}}{R}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Centripetal force is a force that acts on a body moving in a circular path and is directed towards the Centre around which the body is moving. Any motion in a curved path represents accelerated motion and requires a force directed toward the center of curvature of the path. This force is called the centripetal force which means "center seeking" force.
The force has the magnitude $F = m\frac{{v^2}} {R}$.

Q10. The centripetal force required for the circular motion of a car such as taking a sharp turn is provided by:
    (A) friction   <-- CORRECT
    (B) contact force
    (C) rolling friction
    (D) gravitational force
    Answer: A
    Explanation: It is the force of friction that acts between tyres and road.

Q11. In which of the following cases is the net force non zero?
    (A) a kite skillfully held stationary in the sky
    (B) a coin falling under gravity   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a cork of mass 10 g floating on water
    (D) a drop of rain falling down with a constant speed
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The force acting on a coin is due to the gravitational force which causes an acceleration in a downward direction.

Q12. In which of the following cases is the net force zero:
    (A) a rocket just before liftoff
    (B) a feather falling under gravity
    (C) a coin falling under gravity
    (D) a high-speed electron in space far from all material objects, and free of electric and magnetic fields   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As no external fields like electric, magnetic and gravitational field acting on electron the net force is zero

Q13. A pebble of mass 0.05 kg is thrown vertically upwards. Give the direction and magnitude of the net force on the pebble, during its upward motion, Ignore air resistance
    (A) 0
    (B) 0.5 N vertically down   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.5 N vertically up
    (D) 0.05 N vertically down
    Answer: B
    Explanation: F = mg
= 0.05 $\times$ 10 = 0.5 N

Q14. A pebble of mass 0.05 kg is thrown vertically upwards. Give the direction and magnitude of the net force on the pebble, during its downward motion, Ignore air resistance.
    (A) 0.05 N vertically down
    (B) 0.5 N vertically up
    (C) 0.5 N vertically down   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: F = mg = 0.05 $\times$ 10 = 0.5 N downwards

Q15. A pebble of mass 0.05 kg is thrown vertically upwards. Give the direction and magnitude of the net force on the pebble, if the pebble was thrown at an angle of 45¬∞ with the horizontal direction, Ignore air resistance.
    (A) 0.5 N vertically down   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.5 N vertically up
    (C) 0
    (D) 0.05 N vertically down
    Answer: A
    Explanation: F = mg = 0.05 $\times$ 10 = 0.5 N. The horizontal component of the velocity remain constant.

Q1. Neglecting air resistance, in which of the following cases the net force acting on a stone of mass 0.1 kg is not acting downward?
    (A) just after it is dropped from the window of a train accelerating with 1 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$
    (B) just after it is dropped from the window of a train running at a constant velocity of 36 km/h
    (C) lying on the floor of a train which is accelerating with 1 m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{2}}}}$ , the stone being at rest relative to the train   <-- CORRECT
    (D) just after it is dropped from the window of a stationary train
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Weight of the stone is balanced by the reaction of the floor. The only acceleration is provided by the horizontal motion of the train
a = 1ms^-2
force in horizontal direction 
F = ma = 0.1 $\times$ 1 = 0.1N

Q2. Give the magnitude and direction of the net force acting on a stone of mass 0.1 kg lying on the floor of a train which is accelerating with 1 ms^‚àí2, the stone being at rest relative to the train. Neglect air resistance.
    (A) 0.2 opposite to the direction of motion
    (B) 0.1 N opposite to the direction of motion
    (C) 0.1 N along the direction of motion   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1.0 N in the direction of motion
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The weight of the stone is balanced by the reaction of the floor. The only acceleration is provided by the horizontal motion of the train.
a = 1ms^-2
force in the horizontal direction 
F = ma = 0.1 $\times
$ 1 = 0.1N

Q3. One end of a string of length l is connected to a particle of mass m and the other to a small peg on a smooth horizontal table. If the particle moves in a circle with speed v the net force on the particle (directed towards the centre) is
    (A) 0
    (B) T   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\mathrm{T}+\frac{\mathrm{mv^{2 }}}{1}$
    (D) $\mathrm{T}-\frac{\mathrm{mv}^2}{\mathrm{l}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: According to Newton's third law of motion, the net force on a rotating particle is equal to Tension in the String. As the action (ie force towards the centre) and reaction (tension in the string) are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction.

Q4. A constant retarding force of 50 N is applied to a body of mass 20 kg moving initially with a speed of 15 ms^‚àí1. How long does the body take to stop?
    (A) 4.0 s
    (B) 5.0 s
    (C) 6.0 s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 7.0 s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $F=m \frac{d v}{d t}$
$d t=m \frac{d v}{F}=20 \times \frac{15}{50}$ = 6 s

Q5. A constant force acting on a body of mass 3.0 kg changes its speed from 2.0 ms^‚àí1 to 3.5 ms^‚àí1 in 25 s. The direction of the motion of the body remains unchanged. What is the magnitude and direction of the force?
    (A) 0.08 ms^‚àí2, 0.14 N in the direction of motion
    (B) 0.18 N along the direction of motion   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.09 ms^‚àí2, 0.12 N in the direction of motion
    (D) 0.07 ms^‚àí2, 0.16 N in the direction of motion
    Answer: B
    Explanation: F = $m\frac{dv}{dt}=3(\frac{3.5-2}{25})$ = 0.18 N

Q6. A body of mass 5 kg is acted upon by two perpendicular forces 8 N and 6 N. Give the magnitude and direction of the net force acting on the body.
    (A) 14 N at an angle of 37^o to the 8 N force
    (B) 12 N at an angle of 38^o to the 8 N force
    (C) 10 N at an angle of 36^o52^o towards the 8 N force   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 16 N at an angle of 46^o to the 8 N force
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let F_1 = 8N & F_2 = 6 N. 
then the resultant force is $F=\sqrt{F_1^2+F_2^2}$ 
$\sqrt{8^2+6^2}$
= 10N
The direction is determined as $tan\theta=\frac{F_2}{F_1}$ 
= $6\over8$ 
therefore $\theta$ = 36^o52^'

Q7. The driver of a three-wheeler moving with a speed of 36 km/h sees a child standing in the middle of the road and brings his vehicle to rest in 4.0 s just in time to save the child. The mass of the three-wheeler is 400 kg and the mass of the driver is 65 kg. Find out the deceleration produced and the retarding force on the vehicle.
    (A) ‚Äì 2.2 ms^‚àí2, 900 N
    (B) - 2.5 ms^‚àí2, 1162.5 N   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ‚Äì 2.3 ms^‚àí2, 1000 N
    (D) - 2.4 ms^‚àí2, 1100 N
    Answer: B
    Explanation: V= final velocity = 0
V_0 = initial velocity = 36 km/h = 10 m/s
$a= \frac{v-v_0}{t} = \frac{0-10}{4} = -2.5 \frac{m}{s^2} $
F = ma = -465 $\times$ 2.5 = -1162.5N (negative sign indicates the retarding force)

Q8. A rocket with a lift-off mass of 20,000 kg is blasted upwards with an initial acceleration of 5.0 m s^-2. Calculate the initial thrust (force) of the blast.
    (A) 350000 N
    (B) 378000 N
    (C) 365000 N
    (D) 300000 N   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Initial thrust = upthrust required to impart acceleration + thrust to overcome gravity
= ma + mg = m(a + g) = 20000(5 + 10) = 300000N

Q9. A body of mass 0.40 kg moving initially with a constant speed of 10 m /s to the north is subject to a constant force of 8.0 N directed towards the south for 30 s. Take the instant the force is applied to be t = 0, the position of the body at that time to be x = 0, and predict its position at t = -5 s.
    (A) -60 m
    (B) -50 m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 50 m
    (D) -55 m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let $u=10\, ms^{-1}$, F = ‚àí8N, T = 30s and m = 0.4kg
$a=\frac{F}{m}$
$=\frac{-8}{0.4}$
= ‚àí20m/s^2
At t = -5 s, there is no force acting on the particle,
so,
x = ut = 10 $\times$ (-5) = ‚àí50m

Q10. A body of mass 0.40 kg moving initially with a constant speed of 10 ms^‚àí1 to the north is subject to a constant force of 8.0 N directed towards the south for 30 s. Take the instant the force is applied to be t = 0, the position of the body at that time to be x = 0, and predict its position at t = 25 s.
    (A) -6 km   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -7 km
    (C) -8.0 km
    (D) -7.5 km
    Answer: A
    Explanation: At t = 25s, the position of the particle will be
$x=u t+\frac{1}{2} a t^{2}$
$=10 \times 25-\frac{1}{2} \times 20 \times(25)^{2}$
= 250 - 6250
= -6 km

Q11. A body of mass 0.40 kg moving initially with a constant speed of 10 ms^‚àí1 to the north is subject to a constant force of 8.0 N directed towards the south for 30 s. Take the instant the force is applied to be t = 0, the position of the body at that time to be x = 0, and predict its position at t = -100 s
    (A) -60 km
    (B) -67 km
    (C) -50 km   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -55 km
    Answer: C
    Explanation: a = $ {F \over m} = {8 \over {0.4}} $ = 20ms^‚àí2 towards the south
position at t = 30 sec
s = ut + $\frac{1}{2} a t^{2}$
$s_{1}=(10 \times 30)-\frac{1}{2} \times 20 \times 30 \times 30 $ = -8700 m
velocity at t = 30 sec
v = u + at
v = 10 - (20 $\times$ 30) = ‚àí590m/sec
for motion between 30 sec to 100 sec (for 70 sec)
s_2 = (‚àí590 $\times $ 70) + 0 = ‚àí41300m
total distance 
s = s_1 + s_2 = -(8700 + 41300) = -50000m = -50Km

Q12. A truck starts from rest and accelerates uniformly at 2.0 ms^-2. At t = 10 s, a stone is dropped by a person standing on the top of the truck (6 m high from the ground). What is the magnitude of the velocity (in ms^-1) of the stone at t = 11s? (Neglect air resistance.)
    (A) 19.6 m/s
    (B) 21.0 m/s
    (C) 18.5 m/s
    (D) 22.4 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: During first 10 s , the horizontal component of the velocity is v_x = u + at = 0 + 2 $\times$ 10 = 20 m/s
 at t= 11s ,the horizontal component of velocity , in the absence of air resistance remains constant hence,
From 10 to 11 s, the vertical component of the velocity is v_y = u + gt = 0 + 10 $\times$ 1 = 10m/s
Relative velocity is,
$v=\sqrt{v_{x}^{2}+v_{y}^{2}}$
$=\sqrt{20^{2}+10^{2}}$
$=\sqrt{500} $
= 22.4 m/s

Q13. A truck starts from rest and accelerates uniformly at 2.0 ms^-2. At t = 10 s, a stone is dropped by a person standing on the top of the truck (6 m high from the ground). What is the magnitude of acceleration (in ms^-2) of the stone at t = 11s? (Neglect air resistance.)
    (A) 10 ms^-2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 14 ms^-2
    (C) 8 ms^-2
    (D) 12 ms^-2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When the stone is dropped from the truck, the horizontal force acting on it become zero after the stone is released. Stone continues to move under the influence of gravity only. So that acceleration of the stone is equal to the gravitational acceleration g.
a = g = 10ms^-2 acting vertically downward.

Q14. A bob of mass 0.1 kg hung from the ceiling of a room by a string 2 m long is set into oscillation. The speed of the bob at its mean position is 1 m s^‚àí1. What is the trajectory of the bob if the string is cut when the bob is at one of its extreme positions.
    (A) bob will go downwards at an angle
    (B) bob will go down in a parabolic path
    (C) bob will go upwards
    (D) bob will fall vertically downwards   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: At the extreme position of the oscillation, the speed of the bob is zero. So the bob is momentarily at rest. If the string is cut, the bob will fall vertically downwards.

Q15. A bob of mass 0.1 kg hung from the ceiling of a room by a string 2 m long is set into oscillation. The speed of the bob at its mean position is 1 m s^‚àí1. What is the trajectory of the bob if the string is cut when the bob is at its mean position?
    (A) bob will fall vertically downwards
    (B) bob will go down in a parabolic path   <-- CORRECT
    (C) bob will fall vertically upwards
    (D) bob will go upwards
    Answer: B
    Explanation: At the mean position, the bob has a horizontal velocity. So when the string is cut, it will fall along a parabolic path under the effect of gravity.

Q1. A man of mass 70 kg stands on a weighing scale in a lift which is moving upwards with a uniform speed of 10 ms^‚àí1, what would be the reading on the scale?
    (A) 700 N   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1050 N
    (C) 350 N
    (D) 750 N
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Given that mass of the man, m is = 70 kg
Acceleration, a = 0 
Using Newton‚Äôs second law of motion, 
we can write the equation of motion as:
R ‚Äì mg = ma
Where ma is the net force acting on the man. 
As the lift is moving at a uniform speed, so the acceleration a = 0
$\therefore$ R = mg = 70 $\times$ 10 = 700 N

Q2. A man of mass 70 kg stands on a weighing scale in a lift which is moving downwards with a uniform acceleration of 5 ms^‚àí2. What would be the reading on the scale?
    (A) 350 N   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 450 N
    (C) 380 N
    (D) 530 N
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When the lift moves downward with acceleration = 5 ms^-2 the net force acting downward. hence,
mg - R = ma
R = mg - ma 
R = m(g - a)
R = 70(10 - 5)
R = 350 N
R = 350 N

Q3. A man of mass 70 kg stands on a weighing scale in a lift which is moving upwards with a uniform acceleration of 5 ms^‚àí2. What would be the reading on the scale?
    (A) 150 kg
    (B) 105 kg   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 120 kg
    (D) 130 kg
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When the lift moves upward with acceleration = 5 ms^-2 the net force acting upward
R - mg = ma
R = mg + ma
R = m(g + a)
R = 70(10 + 5)
R = 1050N
(We experience weight due to reaction)
therefore Apparent weight = $ {1050\over g} = {1050\over 10 } $ = 105 kg

Q4. A man of mass 70 kg stands on a weighing scale in a lift which is freely falling under gravity. What would be the reading on the scale?
    (A) 115 kg
    (B) 0 kg   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 125 kg
    (D) 95 kg
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When the lift fall freely under gravity, a = g
Therefore Apparent weight, (We experience weight due to reaction)
R = m(g - a) = m(g - g) = 0
This is the condition for weightlessness.

Q5. A man of mass 70 kg stands on a weighing scale in a lift which is moving upwards with a uniform speed of 10 ms^-1. What would be the reading if the lift mechanism failed and it hurtled down freely under gravity?
    (A) 105 kg
    (B) 35 kg
    (C) 70 kg
    (D) 0 kg   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When the lift falls freely under gravity, a = g
Therefore Apparent weight, 
R = m(g ‚àí a) = m(g ‚àí g) = 0
This is the condition of weightlessness.

Q6. The figure shows the position-time graph of a particle of mass 4 kg. What is the force on the particle for t < 0, t > 4 s, 0 < t < 4 s?
    (A) 0, 2, 1
    (B) 0, 2, 0
    (C) 0, 1, 2
    (D) 0, 0, 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When t < 0. As this part is horizontal, thus it can be concluded that distance covered by the particle is zero and hence the force acting on the particle is zero.
When 0 < t < 4 s. As OA has a constant slope, hence in this interval, the particle moves with constant velocity (acceleration = 0). Hence the force acting on the particle is equal to zero.
When t > 4s. This portion shows that the particle always remains at a distance of 3 m from the origin i.e., the particle is at rest. Hence the force acting on the particle is zero.

Q7. The figure shows the position-time graph of a particle of mass 4 kg. What is the impulse at t = 0 and t = 4 s? (Consider one-dimensional motion only)
    (A) 5 kg m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ at t = 0 and -3 kg m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ at t = 4 s
    (B) 4 kg m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ at t = 0 and -4 kg m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ at t = 4 s
    (C) 3 kg ms^‚àí1 at t = 0 and -3 kg ms^‚àí1 at t = 4 s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2 kg m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ at t = 0 and -2 kg m ${{\rm{s}}^{ - {\rm{1}}}}$ at t = 4 s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Initial velocity $u=0$, between t = 0s and t = 4s, the particle has a constant velocity,
therefore slope of OA is $v=\frac{3}{4}\,\,m/s$ 
At t = 0,Impulse = Change in momentum = $m(v-u) = 4(\frac{3}{4}-0)=3\,\,kg\,\,m/s$ 
At t = 4s, initial velocity is $\frac{3}{4}$ m/s,
So, the Impulse = m(v - u) = $4(0-\frac{3}{4})$ = ‚àí3kgm/s

Q8. Two bodies of masses 10 kg and 20 kg respectively kept on a smooth, horizontal surface are tied to the ends of a light string. a horizontal force F = 600 N is applied to the 20 kg mass so as to pull it. What is the tension in the string?
    (A) 300 N
    (B) 250 N
    (C) 200 N   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 150 N
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let,
T = tension in the string, a = acceleration in the direction of force F. 
 Given that , m_1 = 10 kg and m_2 = 20 kg
Therefore, common acceleration is $a=\frac{F}{m_1+m_2}=\frac{600}{10+20}$ = 20ms^‚àí2 
Now the tension T in the string is T given by = m_1a = 10 $\times$ 20 = 200N

Q9. Two bodies of masses 10 kg and 20 kg respectively kept on a smooth, horizontal surface are tied to the ends of a light string, a horizontal force F = 600 N is applied to the 10 kg mass so as to pull it. What is the tension in the string?
    (A) 450 N
    (B) 300 N
    (C) 400 N   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 370 N
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let, T= tension on the string
a = acceleration, Given that , m_1 = mass of light body is = 10 kg and m_2 = mass of heavy body is = 20 kg
$a=\frac{F}{m_1+m_2}=\frac{600}{30}$ = 20ms^-2
Now the tension in the string will be,
T = m_2a = 20 $\times$ 20 = 400N

Q10. A nucleus is at rest in the laboratory frame of reference. If it disintegrates into two smaller nuclei ______ .
    (A) the products must move in opposite directions   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the products must move at an angle in same direction
    (C) the products must move in same direction
    (D) the products must move at an angle in opposite directions
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let, M = mass of nucleus at rest. m_1 and m_2 are masses of two smaller nuclei. v_1_ and v_2 are the velocities of respective masses
Now, According to the law of conservation of momentum,
Initial momentum before disintegration = final momentum after disintegration
m_1v_1 + m_2v_2 = 0
$v_2=-\frac{m_2}{m_1}\cdot{v_1}$
As masses, m_1 and m_2 cannot be negative, v_1, and v_2 having opposite signs and so the two smaller nuclei move in opposite directions.

Q11. Two billiard balls each of mass 0.05 kg moving in opposite directions with speed 6 ms^-1 collide and rebound at the same speed. What is the impulse imparted to each ball due to the other?
    (A) 0.5 kg ms^-1
    (B) 0.3 kg ms^-1
    (C) 0.6 kg ms^‚àí1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.4 kg ms^-1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Impulse imparted to one ball by the other = change in momentum
= momentum after collision - momentum before collision
= {0.05 $\times$ 6} - {0.05 $\times$ (-6)} 
= 0.6 kg ms^-1

Q12. A shell of mass 0.020 kg is fired by a gun of mass 100 kg. If the muzzle speed of the shell is 80 ms^-1, what is the recoil speed of the gun?
    (A) 1.9 cm/s
    (B) 1.7 cm/s
    (C) 1.8 cm/s
    (D) 1.6 cm/s   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mass of shell, m = 0.02kg 
Mass of gun, M = 100kg
Speed of shell, v = 80ms^‚àí1
Let V be the recoil speed of the gun. According to the law of conservation of momentum,
Initial momentum = Final momentum
0 = mv + MV
V = $-\frac{mv}{M}=-\frac{0.02\times80}{100}$
 recoil speed of the gun is ,V = ‚àí0.016ms^‚àí1 = ‚àí1.6cms^‚àí1
A negative sign indicates that the gun moves backward as the bullet moves forward.

Q13. A batsman deflects a ball by an angle of 45^o without changing its initial speed which is equal to 54 km/h. What is the impulse imparted to the ball? (Mass of the ball is 0.15 kg.)
    (A) 4.2 kg ms^‚àí1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 4.6 kg ms^‚àí1
    (C) 4.8 kg ms^‚àí1
    (D) 4.4 kg ms^‚àí1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let $\vec {v_1}$ and $\vec {v_2}$ be the velocities of the ball before and after deflection, which is equal to 54 km h^‚àí1 = 15ms^‚àí1 as the speed of the ball does not change after a deflection.
$v=\sqrt{v_{1}^{2}+v_{2}^{2}+2 v_{1} v_{2} \cos 45^{\circ}}$
$=\sqrt{15^{2}+15^{2}+2 \times 15 \times 15 \times({1 \over \sqrt{2}}}$
= 27.72 ms^-1
Impulse imparted to the ball = Mass $\times$ change in velocity of the ball
0.15 $\times$ 27.72 = 4.2kgms^‚àí1

Q14. A stone of mass 0.25 kg tied to the end of a string is whirled round in a circle of radius 1.5 m with a speed of 40 rev./min in a horizontal plane. What is the tension in the string?
    (A) 6.9 N
    (B) 6.6 N   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6.3 N
    (D) 6.1 N
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let, m = 0.25 kg, r = 1.5m and f = 40 rv/min = 40 rev /60 s = 2/3 rps
$\omega=2\pi f =2\pi \times\frac{2}{3}=\frac{4\pi}{3} \,rad\, s^{-1}$ 
Tension in the string = Centripetal force
so, $T=mr\omega^2=0.25\times1.5\times(\frac{4\pi}{3})^2$
6.6 N

Q15. A stone of mass 0.25 kg tied to the end of a string is whirled round in a circle of radius 1.5 m with a speed of 40 rev./min in a horizontal plane. What is the maximum speed with which the stone can be whirled around if the string can withstand a maximum tension of 200 N?
    (A) 37 ms^‚àí1
    (B) 35 ms^‚àí1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 33 ms^‚àí1
    (D) 38 ms^‚àí1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given that T_max = 200 N
$\frac{m v^{2}}{r}=T_{\max }$
$v_{\max }=\sqrt{\frac{T_{\max } \times r}{m}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{200 \times 1.5}{0.25}}$
= 34.6 m s^-1
= 35 m s^-1

Q1. A stone of mass 0.25 kg tied to the end of a string is whirled round in a circle of radius 1.5 m with a speed of 40 rev./min in a horizontal plane. The speed is then increased beyond the maximum permissible value, and the string breaks suddenly, which of the following correctly describes the trajectory of the stone after the string breaks.
    (A) the stone moves radially inwards
    (B) the stone flies off at an angle with the tangent whose magnitude depends on the speed of the particle
    (C) the stone flies off tangentially from the instant the string breaks   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the stone moves radially outwards
    Answer: C
    Explanation: it is because the velocity at any point is directed along the tangent at that point.

Q2. The figure shows a man standing stationary with respect to a horizontal conveyor belt that is accelerating with 1 ms^‚àí2. What is the net force on the man? Mass of the man = 65 kg
    (A) 70 N
    (B) 55 N
    (C) 60 N
    (D) 65 N   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Net force on the man = ma = 65 $\times$ 1 = 65 N

Q3. The figure shows a man standing stationary with respect to a horizontal conveyor belt that is accelerating with 1 ms^‚àí2. If the coefficient of static friction between the man‚Äôs shoes and the belt is 0.2, up to what acceleration of the belt can the man continue to be stationary relative to the belt? (g = 10 ms^-2)
    (A) 2 ms^‚àí2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2.8 ms^‚àí2
    (C) 2.5 ms^‚àí2
    (D) 3.1 ms^‚àí2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: For the maximum acceleration of the belt (for which man continue to be stationary relative to the belt) force by the belt is balanced by maximum static friction
F = f
ma = $\mu$R, here $\mu$ is coefficient of static friction
ma = $\mu$mg
here R = mg
a = $\mu$g = 0.2 $\times$ 10 = 2ms^‚àí2

Q4. A stone of mass m tied to the end of a string revolves in a vertical circle of radius R. if T_1 and v_1 denote the tension and speed at the lowest point. T_2 and v_2 denote corresponding values at the highest point. The net forces at the lowest and highest points of the circle directed vertically downwards at the Lowest Point and Highest Point are
    (A) T_1 ‚àí mg, mg + T_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) mg + T_1, mg - T_2
    (C) mg - T_1 -( $m\frac{v_1^2} {R}$), mg + T_2 +( $m\frac{v_1^2} {R}$)
    (D) mg + T_1 - ($m\frac{{v_1^2}}{R}$), mg - T_2 + ($m\frac{{v_1^2}}{R}$)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: At the lowest point 
${F_{net}} = {T_1} - mg = \frac{{m{v_1}^2} }{ R}$ 
at the highest point 
${F_{net}} = {T_2} + mg = \frac{{m{v_2}^2}}{ R}$

Q5. A helicopter of mass 1000 kg rises with a vertical acceleration of 15 ms^-2. The crew and the passengers weigh 300 kg. Give the magnitude and direction of the force on the floor by the crew and passengers. (g = 10ms^-2)
    (A) 7500 N vertically downwards   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1500 N vertically downwards
    (C) 4500 N upward
    (D) 3000 N upward
    Answer: A
    Explanation: m = 300Kg
a = 15ms^‚àí2
Reaction on the floor by the system
R = m(g + a)
= 300(10 + 15)
= 7500 N
The helicopter is accelerating vertically upward, therefore reaction force will also be directed upward. Hence according to newton's third law of motion force on the floor by the crew and passengers is 7500N and directed downward.

Q6. A helicopter of mass 1000 kg rises with a vertical acceleration of 15 ms^-2. The crew and the passengers weigh 300 kg. Give the magnitude and direction of the action of the rotor of the helicopter on the surrounding air.
    (A) 3.50 $ \times $ 10^4 N downwards
    (B) 3.25 $ \times $ 10^4 N downwards   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3.70 $ \times $ 10^4 N upwards
    (D) 3.95 $ \times $ 10^4 N upwards
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The reaction of the rotor on the surrounding air will be due to the mass of the helicopter as well as the passengers.
Let, the mass of helicopter, M = 1000 kg
Mass of crew and passengers, m = 300 kg
acceleration in upward direction a = 15 m s^-2
Action of the rotor of the helicopter on the surrounding air is
= (M + m)(g + a)
= (1000 + 300)(10 + 15)
= 32500N downward direction
Thus, the reaction force of the rotor on the surrounding air will be 32500 N

Q7. A helicopter of mass 1000 kg rises with a vertical acceleration of 15 ms^-2. The crew and the passengers weigh 300 kg. Give the magnitude and direction of the force on the helicopter due to the surrounding air.
    (A) 3.50 $ \times $ 10^4 N downwards
    (B) 3.25 $ \times $ 10^4 N upwards   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3.70 $ \times $ 10^4 N upwards
    (D) 3.95 $ \times $ 10^4 N upwards
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Force on the helicopter due to the surrounding air is equal and opposite to the action of the rotor of the helicopter on the surrounding air.
R‚Ä≤‚àím_tg = m_ta
= m_t(g + a)
= 1300 $\times$ (10 + 15) = 32500N
Therefore Force on the surrounding air is = 32500 N in an upward direction.

Q8. A stream of water flowing horizontally with a speed of 15 ms^‚àí1 gushes out of a tube of cross-sectional area 10^‚àí2 m^2 and hits a vertical wall nearby. What is the force exerted on the wall by the impact of water, assuming it does not rebound?
    (A) 2.75 $ \times $ 10^3 N
    (B) 2.55 $ \times $ 10^3 N
    (C) 2.45 $ \times $ 10^3 N
    (D) 2.25 $ \times $ 10^3 N   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Here, u = 15ms^‚àí1, v = 0, t = 1 s, A = 10^‚àí2m^‚àí2
m = mass of water gushed out per second
$=\frac{\text {Volumexdensity}}{\text {Time}}$
$=\frac{\text {Area} \times \text {distance} \times \text {density}}{\text {Time}}$
=Area $\times$ velocity $\times$ density
= Au$\rho$
= 10^‚àí2 $\times$ 15 $\times$ 1000 = 150kg
Force exerted by the wall on water,
F = ma = $m\frac{v-u}{t}=150\times \frac{0-15}{1}$ = -2250 N
So the force exerted on the wall by the impact of water,
F_1 = -F = 2250 N

Q9. An aircraft executes a horizontal loop at a speed of 720 km/h with its wings banked at 15^o. What is the radius of the loop?
    (A) 11 km
    (B) 15.24 km   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 14 km
    (D) 17.24 km
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Here, we have 
$\theta$ = 15^o, g = 9.8ms^‚àí2, v = 720kmh^‚àí1 = 200ms^‚àí1
Now we have, $\tan \theta=\frac{v^{2}}{r g}$
 $\therefore$$\,\,r=\frac{200\times 200}{9.8\times tan15^o}$ 
radius of loop is ,r = 15.24km

Q10. A train runs along an unbanked circular track of radius 30 m at a speed of 54 km/h. The mass of the train is 106 kg. What is the angle of banking required to prevent wearing out of the rail? (g =10m/s^2)
    (A) 37^o   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 27^o
    (C) 42^o
    (D) 32^o
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Here, we have:
r = 30m and v = 54 km/h = 15 m/s
Let angle of banking = $\theta$
For safe turn $\tan \theta = {{{v^2}} \over {rg}}{\mkern 1mu} {\mkern 1mu} $
$\tan \theta = {{{v^2}} \over {rg}} $ = $ {{{{(15)}^2}} \over {30 \times 10}} = {{15 \times 15} \over {30 \times 10}} = {3 \over 4} $
Hence, angle of banking is:-
$\theta $ = $ {\tan ^{ - 1}}\left( {{3 \over 4}} \right) $ = 37^o

Q11. You may have seen in a circus a motorcyclist driving in vertical loops inside a death well‚Äô (a hollow spherical chamber with holes, so the spectators can watch from outside). What is the minimum speed required at the uppermost position to perform a vertical loop if the radius of the chamber is 25 m?
    (A) 14.5 m/s
    (B) 18 m/s
    (C) 15.65 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 26 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As the centripetal force is equal to weight (mg) and normal reaction (R), we have
$\frac{mv^2}{r}$ = R + mg
At a minimum speed, R= 0, Therefore, we have
$\frac{mv^2}{r}$ = mg
v = $\sqrt{rg}=\sqrt{25\times 9.8}$ = 15.65ms^‚àí1

Q12. A monkey of mass 40 kg climbs on a rope which can stand a maximum tension of 600 N. What is the tension in the rope if the monkey climbs up with an acceleration of 6 ms^‚àí2?
    (A) 600 N
    (B) 640 N   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 740 N
    (D) 760 N
    Answer: B
    Explanation: When the monkey climbs up with an acceleration of 6 ms^-2, we have
T ‚àí mg = ma
T = mg + ma
T = m(g + a) = 40(10 + 6) = 640N

Q13. A monkey of mass 40 kg climbs on a rope which can stand a maximum tension of 600 N. What is the tension in the rope if the monkey climbs down with an acceleration of 4 ms^-2?
    (A) 300 N
    (B) 200 N
    (C) 280 N
    (D) 240 N   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When the monkey climbs down with an acceleration of 4 ms^-2, we have
mg ‚àí T = ma
tension in rope is given by , T = m(g ‚àí a) = 40(10 ‚àí 4) = 240N

Q14. A monkey of mass 40 kg climbs on a rope which can stand a maximum tension of 600 N. What is the tension in the rope if the monkey climbs up with a uniform speed of 5 ms^-1?
    (A) 400 N   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 206 N
    (C) 275 N
    (D) 315 N
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When monkey climbs with the uniform speed, the acceleration is zero and we have:
T = mg = 40 $\times$ 10 = 400N

Q15. A monkey of mass 40 kg climbs on a rope which can stand a maximum tension of 600 N. What is the tension in the rope if the monkey falls down the rope nearly freely under gravity?
    (A) 0 N   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 400 N
    (C) 600 N
    (D) 200 N
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When the monkey fall down down the rope nearly free under the gravity, then a = g and we have
T = m(g ‚àí a) = m(g ‚àí g) = 0N

Q1. The scalar product of two vectors A and B is
    (A) vector
    (B) a scalar   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a complex number
    (D) a tensor
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Scalar product means dot product and the dot product of 2 vectors gives a scalar. For example dot product of force and displacement gives work which is scalar.

Q2. The scalar product of two vectors A and B in terms of the magnitudes and angle $\theta $ is
    (A) $\left| {\bf{A}} \right|\left| {\bf{B}} \right|{\rm{cot}}\theta $
    (B) $\left| {\bf{A}} \right|\left| {\bf{B}} \right|{\rm{cos}}\theta $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\left| {\bf{A}} \right|\left| {\bf{B}} \right|{\rm{tan}}\theta $
    (D) $\left| {\bf{A}} \right|\left| {\bf{B}} \right|{\rm{sin}}\theta $
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The scalar product of two vectors can be constructed by taking the component of one vector in the direction of the other and multiplying it times the magnitude of the other vector. This can be expressed in the form $\vec A.\vec B = |A||B|\cos \theta $

Q3. The scalar product of two vectors $\overrightarrow A$ and $\overrightarrow B$ in terms of the projections of the vectors on the x, y and z axis is
    (A) $\overrightarrow A$.$\overrightarrow B$ = $A_x B_x-A_y B_y-A_z B_z$
    (B) $\overrightarrow A$.$\overrightarrow B$ = $A_x B_x+A_y B_y-A_z B_z$
    (C) $\overrightarrow A$.$\overrightarrow B$ = $A_x B_x-A_y B_y+A_z B_z$
    (D) $\overrightarrow A$.$\overrightarrow B$ = $A_x B_x+A_y B_y+A_z B_z$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\overrightarrow A$ = A_x i + A_y j+ A_zk
$\overrightarrow B$ = B_x i + B_y j+ B_zk
$\overrightarrow A$.$\overrightarrow B$ = (A_x i + A_y j+ A_zk). (B_x i+ B_y j+ B_zk) 
$\overrightarrow A$.$\overrightarrow B$ = A_xB_x + A_yB_y + A_zB_z , this is required result.

Q4. The scalar product of vectors is
    (A) non commutative and not distributive
    (B) commutative and not distributive
    (C) non commutative and distributive
    (D) commutative and distributive   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The scalar product is:
 Commutative:
 $\vec A.\vec B = \vec B.\vec A$ 
 |A||B| cos $\theta$ = |B||A| cos $\theta$
 Distributive 
 $\vec A.(\vec B + \vec C) = \vec A.\vec B + \vec A.\vec C$

Q5. The change in kinetic energy of a particle is equal to the
    (A) work done on it by some force.
    (B) work done on it by the net force.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) loss in ambient kinetic energy.
    (D) work done on it by the aerodynamic force.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If a body of mass m moving with velocity u under the action of force F. Its velocity become v after displaced by s, then by using equation of motion :-
$\eqalign{ & {v^2} = {u^2} + 2as \cr & {v^2} - {u^2} = 2as \cr & m{v^2} - m{u^2} = 2mas \cr & {1 \over 2}m{v^2} - {1 \over 2}m{u^2} = Fs \cr & {K_f} - {K_i} = W \cr & \Delta K = W \cr} $

Q6. The work done by the force is defined to be
    (A) the product of component of the force in the direction of the displacement and the magnitude of the displacement   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the product of component of the force in the direction perpendicular to displacement and the magnitude of the displacement
    (C) the negative product of component of the force in the direction of the displacement and the magnitude of this displacement
    (D) the product of force and the magnitude of the displacement
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Work done is given by 
W = (Fcos$\theta$)d
here Fcos$\theta$ is the component of applied force in direction of displacement and d is magnitude of displacement.

Q7. If F is a force and d is the displacement in the direction of force then the work done by the force is given by
    (A) - F.d
    (B) F.d   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -2F.d
    (D) 2F.d
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Work done is equal to force in the direction of displacement multiplied by displacement i.e., 
$W = \vec F.\vec d$

Q8. In which case is the work done zero?
    (A) Force and displacement are in the same direction
    (B) Force and displacement are at an angle of 45$^\circ $
    (C) Force and displacement are at an angle of 75$^\circ $
    (D) Force and displacement are perpendicular to each other   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Work done, W = Fdcos$\theta$
where $\theta$ is the angle between F and d. If both are perpendicular then $\theta$ = 90 degrees, so cos$\theta$ = 0 and thus work done is zero.

Q9. The S.I unit of force is
    (A) erg
    (B) dyne
    (C) Newton   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Joule
    Answer: C
    Explanation: In the International System of Units (SI) the newton is the unit for force. It is equal to the amount of net force required to accelerate a mass of one kilogram at a rate of 1 m/sec^2 in direction of the applied force. It is named after Isaac Newton in recognition of his work on classical mechanics, specifically Newton's second law of motion.

Q10. In a graph of F(x) vs x, the area under the curve represents the
    (A) work done by F(x).   <-- CORRECT
    (B) energy of F(x)
    (C) momentum of F(x)
    (D) impulse of F(x)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Work done by a variable force is given by 
W = ${\int F(x)dx } $
The above integration gives us the area under the curve F(x) Vs x.

Q11. Work-energy theorem does not give information on
    (A) difference of kinetic energies
    (B) time dependence   <-- CORRECT
    (C) change in kinetic energy
    (D) work done
    Answer: B
    Explanation: According to the work-energy theorem, the net work done on a body equals the change in its kinetic energy. So it does not give any information about time dependence.

Q12. Physically, the notion of potential energy is applicable only to:
    (A) The class of forces where work is done against the force gets converted to kinetic energy
    (B) The class of forces where work done against the force gets converted to thermal energy
    (C) The class of forces where work is done against the force gets stored up as energy.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) The class of forces where work is done against the force gets dissipated
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Potential energy is the , stored energy of an object. It is the energy by virtue of an object's position relative to other objects. Potential energy is often associated with restoring forces such as a spring . It is applicable only for the conservative forces.

Q13. The work done by a conservative forces depends
    (A) depends on the path
    (B) only on the end points   <-- CORRECT
    (C) on both the end points as well as the path
    (D) on the position of the forces
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A force is said to be conservative if work done by this force is independent of path and is dependent only on end points.

Q14. The total mechanical energy of a system is conserved if the forces, doing work on it, are
    (A) conservative   <-- CORRECT
    (B) viscous
    (C) damped
    (D) not conservative
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mechanical energy is the sum of kinetic energy and potential energy in an object that is used to do a particular work. In other words, it describes the energy of an object because of its motion or position, or both.

Q15. For a ball dropped from a tower of height h, the total mechanical energy is
    (A) the difference of potential and kinetic energies
    (B) the sum of potential and kinetic energies   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the kinetic energy
    (D) the potential energy
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Mechanical energy = K.E + P.E
 A falling ball will have both these energies in between topmost and bottomost points of its motion so, mechanical energy is the sum of potential and kinetic energies.

Work, Energy and Power Test 02  (id 553) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Physics > Work Energy and Power
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The potential energy of a spring whose spring constant is k and is compressed by x is
    (A) $2k{x^2}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{2}k{x^2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{1}{4}k{x^2}$
    (D) $k{x^2}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If a spring is stretched or compressed by a distance x from its natural length under the action of restoring force then
 F = -kx
Therefore, $d U=-F . d x$
$U=\int_\limits{0}^{x}-F . d x=\int_\limits{0}^{x} k x . d x=k\left[\frac{x^{2}}{2}\right]_{0}^{x}$
$U=\frac{1}{2} k x^{2}$

Q2. Mass and energy are equivalent and are related by
    (A) $E = m{c^2}/2$
    (B) $E = m{c^3}$
    (C) $E = m{c^2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $E = 2m{c^2}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mass-energy equivalence states that anything having mass has an equivalent amount of energy and vice versa. With these fundamental quantities directly relating to one another by Einstein's theory of special relativity, it shows that matter (as mass) and energy can be converted into each other according to the famous equation $E = m{c^2}$.

Q3. Power is defined as
    (A) ability to do work.
    (B) the time rate at which work is done.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) stored energy.
    (D) energy due to motion.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Power is the rate of doing work. It is the amount of energy consumed per unit time. Having no direction, it is a scalar quantity. In the SI system, the unit of power is the joule per second (J/s), known as the watt. The integral of power over time defines the work performed.
$P = {{dW} \over {dt}} = {{d(\vec F.\vec s)} \over {dt}}$

Q4. S.I unit of power is
    (A) Newton
    (B) Joule
    (C) Watt   <-- CORRECT
    (D) Angstrom
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The SI unit of power is Watt(equivalent to one joule per second).

Q5. Which of the following laws used to solve problems in collisions?
    (A) Laws of conservation of linear momentum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Newton‚Äôs laws
    (C) Kepler‚Äôs laws
    (D) Kirchhoff‚Äôs laws
    Answer: A
    Explanation: If an external force is absent then the linear momentum of the system remains conserved.

Q6. In an elastic collision the total kinetic energy of the system is
    (A) the same after the collision as before.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) greater than the total kinetic energy before.
    (C) is less than the total kinetic energy before.
    (D) zero after the collision.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Kinetic energy is transferred to other forms of energy‚Äîsuch as thermal energy, potential energy, and sound‚Äîduring the collision process. After the collision, if recovery of kinetic energy is 100% then it is called an elastic collision. So that in an elastic collision the total kinetic energy of the system is the same after the collision as before.

Q7. In an inelastic collision, the total kinetic energy of the system is
    (A) less than before the collision.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) greater than the total kinetic energy before.
    (C) same after the collision as before.
    (D) zero after the collision.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Kinetic energy is transferred to other forms of energy‚Äîsuch as thermal energy, potential energy, and sound‚Äîduring the collision process. After collision if recovery of kinetic energy is less than 100% then it is called inelastic collision i.e., some part of kinetic energy is not recovered. So that in an inelastic collision the total kinetic energy after the collision is less than before the collision.

Q8. In a completely inelastic collision the colliding bodies move
    (A) in opposite directions after the collision.
    (B) as one body after the collision.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) at an angle after the collision.
    (D) in same direction after the collision.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For a perfectly inelastic collision coefficient of restitution is zero. i.e, e = 0 so that relative velocity of separation will be zero means the colliding bodies stick together and move as one body after the collision.

Q9. Considering a completely inelastic collision of a particle of mass m_1 moving with initial velocity v_1 and a stationary particle of mass m_2, the final velocity is given by
    (A) $\frac{m_1}{2 m_1+m_2} v_1$
    (B) $\frac{m_1}{m_1+m_2} v_1$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{m_1}{m_1+2 m_2} v_1$
    (D) $\frac{m_2}{m_1+m_2} v_1$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For a completely inelastic collision momentum remains conserved i.e,
p_i = p_f
m_1v_1 + 0 = (m_1 + m_2)v
$v=\frac{m_1}{\left(m_1+m_2\right)} v_1$

Q10. Considering a completely inelastic collision of a particle of mass ${{\text{m}}_{\text{1}}}$moving with initial velocity ${{\text{v}}_{\text{1}}}$ and a stationary particle of mass ${{\text{m}}_{\text{2}}}$. The ratio of final to initial kinetic energy is
    (A) $\frac{{m_1}} {{2{m_1} + {m_2}}}$
    (B) $\frac{{m_1}}{{{m_1} + 2{m_2}}}$
    (C) $\frac{{m_2}}{{{m_1} + {m_2}}}$
    (D) $\frac{{m_1}}{{{m_1} + {m_2}}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: p_i = p_f
m_1v_1 + 0 = (m_1 + m_2)v
$v=\frac{m_1}{\left(m_1+m_2\right)} v_1$
$K_i=\frac{1}{2} m_1 v_1^2$
$K_f=\frac{1}{2}\left(m_1+m_2\right)\left(\frac{m_1}{\left(m_1+m_2\right)} v_1\right)^2$
$\frac{K_f}{K_i}=\frac{\frac{1}{2}\left(m_1+m_2\right)\left(\frac{m_1}{\left(m_1+m_2\right)} v_1\right)^2}{\frac{1}{2} m_1 v_1{ }^2}=\frac{m_1}{\left(m_1+m_2\right)}$

Q11. A dog weighing 25 kg, while chasing a cat, jumps over a fence of height 1.6 m. What is the potential energy of dog at the top of fence?
(Take gravity due to earth 'g'=10 m s^-2)
    (A) 160 Joules
    (B) 320 Joules
    (C) 480 Joules
    (D) 400 Joules   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Mass of the dog = m = 25 kg
Height of fence = h = 1.6 m
Acceleration due to gravity = g = 10 m/s¬≤
$\therefore$ Potential energy of dog = m.g.h = 25√ó10√ó1.6 = 25√ó16 = 400 kgm¬≤/s = 400 J

Q12. A body of mass 2 kg initially at rest moves under the action of an applied horizontal force of 7 N on a table with coefficient of kinetic friction = 0.1. Compute the work done by the applied force in 10 s.
    (A) 842 J
    (B) 800 J
    (C) 882 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 822 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\eqalign{ & f = {\mu _k}R = {\mu _k}mg = 0.1 \times 2 \times 9.8 = 1.96N \cr & F = 7N \cr & {F_{net}} = F - f = 7 - 1.96 = 5.04N \cr & a = {{{F_{net}}} \over m} = {{5.04} \over 2} = 2.52m/{\sec ^2} \cr} $
Displacement in 10 second
$s = ut + {1 \over 2}a{t^2} = 0 + {1 \over 2} \times 2.52 \times 10 \times 10 = 126m$
Work done by applied force 
${W_F} = Fs\cos 0^\circ = 7 \times 126 \times 1 = 882J$

Q13. A body of mass 2 kg initially at rest moves under the action of an applied horizontal force of 7 N on a table with a coefficient of kinetic friction = 0.1. Compute the (a) work done by the net force on the body in 10 s,(b) change in kinetic energy of the body in 10 s?
    (A) 600 J, 600 J
    (B) 555 J, 555 J
    (C) 635 J, 635 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 655 J, 655 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: f = $\mu_k$R = $\mu_k$mg = 0.1 $\times$ 2 $\times$ 9.8 = 1.96N
F = 7N
Fnet = F ‚àí f = 7 ‚àí 1.96 = 5.04N
$a=\frac{F_{n e t}}{m}=\frac{5.04}{2}$ = 2.52 m/sec^2
displacement in 10 second
$s = ut + {1 \over 2}a{t^2} = 0 + {1 \over 2} $ $\times$ 2.52 $\times$ 10 $\times$ 10 = 126m
work done by net force 
W_ = F_net s cos0^o = 5.04 $\times$ 126 $\times$ 1 = 635
change in kinetic energy = work done by a net force
$\Delta K$ = W = 635J

Q14. The casing of a rocket in flight burns up due to friction. At whose expense is the heat energy required for burning obtained?
    (A) Reaction force energy
    (B) Earth‚Äôs gravitational energy
    (C) Atmosphere
    (D) Rocket   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The heat energy required for the burning of the casing of the rocket comes from the rocket itself. As a result of work done against friction the kinetic energy of the rocket continuously decreases and this work against friction reappears as heat energy. This results in a reduction of the mass of the rocket.

Q15. A body constrained to move along the z-axis of a coordinate system is subject to a constant force F given by ${\bf{F}} = - {\bf{\hat i}} + 2{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}{\rm{N}}$, where $\hat i,{\rm{\hat j}}$ and $\hat k$ are unit vectors along the x-, y- and z-axis of the system respectively. What is the work done by this force in moving the body a distance of 4 m along the z-axis?
    (A) 9 J
    (B) 12 J   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 15 J
    (D) 7 J
    Answer: B
    Explanation: given that 
$\overrightarrow{\mathbf{F}}=-\hat{\mathbf{i}}+2 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}}$
$\vec{s}=4 \hat{\mathbf{k}}$
$W=\vec{F} \cdot \vec{s}=(-\hat{\mathbf{i}}+2 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}}) \cdot 4 \hat{\mathbf{k}}$ = 12 J

Q1. Find the angle between the force ${\bf{F}} = 3{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} - 5{\bf{\hat k}}$ and displacement ${\bf{d}} = 5{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}$.
    (A) $\theta=\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{11}{25}\right)$
    (B) $\theta=\sin ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{25}\right)$
    (C) $\theta=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{11}{25}\right)$
    (D) $\theta=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{25}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $W=\vec{F} \cdot \vec{d}$
$\vec{F} \cdot \vec{d}$ = Fd cos$ \theta$
$\cos \theta$ = $\frac{\vec{F} \cdot \vec{d}}{F d}$ = $\frac{(3 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}-5 \hat{\mathbf{k}}) \cdot(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{3^{2}+4^{2}+(-5)^{2}} \times \sqrt{5^{2}+4^{2}+3^{2}}}$ $=\frac{15+16-15}{\sqrt{50} \times \sqrt{50}}=\frac{16}{50}=\frac{8}{25}$
$\theta=\cos ^{-1}\left(\frac{8}{25}\right)$ = 71^o

Q2. Find the projection of F on d, if force ${\bf{F}} = 3{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} - 5{\bf{\hat k}}$ and displacement ${\bf{d}} = 5{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}$
    (A) $\frac{8}{{25}}\left( {5{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}} \right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{3}{{25}}\left( {5{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}} \right)$
    (C) $\frac{17}{{25}}\left( {5{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}} \right)$
    (D) $\frac{11}{{25}}\left( {5{\bf{\hat i}} + 4{\bf{\hat j}} + 3{\bf{\hat k}}} \right)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The vector projection of a vector $\vec A$ on a nonzero vector $\vec B$ is also known as the vector component $\vec A$ in the direction of $\vec B$ and is equal to $\left( {\vec A.\hat B} \right).\hat B$ 
Here projection of $\vec F$ on vector $\vec d$ = $\left( {\vec F.\hat d} \right).\hat d $ = $(\vec{F} \cdot \hat{d}) \cdot \hat{d}=\left[(3 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}-5 \hat{\mathbf{k}}) \cdot \frac{(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{5^2+4^2+3^2}}\right] \cdot\left[\frac{(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{5^2+4^2+3^2}}\right]$
$=\left[(3 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}-5 \hat{\mathbf{k}}) \cdot \frac{(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{50}}\right] \cdot\left[\frac{(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{50}}\right]$
$=\left[\frac{1}{\sqrt{50}}(15+16-15)\right] \cdot\left[\frac{(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{50}}\right]$
$=\frac{16}{\sqrt{50}} \cdot\left[\frac{(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})}{\sqrt{50}}\right]=\frac{8}{25}(5 \hat{\mathbf{i}}+4 \hat{\mathbf{j}}+3 \hat{\mathbf{k}})$

Q3. Balram exerts a steady force of magnitude 150 N on the stalled car as shown in the figure below; he pushes it a distance of 20 m. The car also has a flat tyre, so to make the car move straight. He pushes at an angle of 30^o to the direction of motion. How much work does he do?
    (A) 2299 J
    (B) 2323 J
    (C) 2654 J
    (D) 2598 J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: W = Fs cos$ \theta$ = $ 150 \times 20 \times {{\sqrt 3 } \over 2} $ = 2598J

Q4. Balram exerts a steady force of magnitude F = 200${\bf{\hat i}}$+ 2.0$\hat j$ on the stalled car as shown in the figure above, he pushes it a distance s = 10${\bf{\hat i}}$ + 10$\hat j$ m. How much work does he do?
    (A) 2020 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2320 J
    (C) 2220 J
    (D) 2120 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\vec{F}=200 \hat{i}+2 \hat{j}$
$\vec{s}=10 \hat{i}+10 \hat{j}$
$W=\vec{F} \cdot \vec{s}=(200 \hat{i}+2 \hat{j}) \cdot(10 \hat{i}+10 \hat{j})$
W = 2000 + 20 = 2020 J

Q5. A railway porter is holding a weight of 100 kgs on his head and is standing still. What is the work done by him?
    (A) 200 J
    (B) 1000 J
    (C) 100 J
    (D) 0 J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: W = Force $\times$ displacement in the direction of the force
Work done will be zero because porter is stationary (i.e. displacement is zero)

Q6. Balram pushes 500kg weight on a horizontal frictionless surface a distance of 10 m. The work done by the gravitational force is:
    (A) 100 J
    (B) 5000 J
    (C) 0 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 200 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: the angle between force and displacement is 90^o
W = Fscos90^o = 0

Q7. Weight of 20kg falls from a height of 10 m. The work done by the gravitational force is (Take g = 10 ms^‚àí2)
    (A) 2000 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1500 J
    (C) 3000 J
    (D) 2500 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: W = Fscos$\theta$ = mghcos0^o
W = 20 $\times$ 10 $\times$ 10 $\times$ 1 = 2000 J

Q8. A raindrop of mass 2.00 g falls from a height of 1.00 km. It hits the ground with a speed of 50.0 m/s. What is the work done by the gravitational force? (Take g = 10 ms^‚àí2)
    (A) 20 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 26 J
    (C) 22 J
    (D) 24 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: W = Fscos$\theta$ = mghcos0^o
W = 2 $\times$ 10^ ‚àí 3 $\times$ 10 $\times$ 1000 $\times$ 1 = 20J

Q9. A raindrop of mass 2.00 g falls from a height of 1.00 km. It hits the ground with a speed of 50.0 m/s. What is the work done by the resistive forces if any? (Take g = 10 ms^‚àí2)
    (A) ‚Äì 19.5 J
    (B) ‚Äì 22.5 J
    (C) - 17.5 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ‚Äì 27.5 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: From work kinetic energy theorem
$\Delta$K = W_mg + W_air
W_mg = Fscos$\theta$ = mghcos0^o
W_mg = 2 $\times$ 10 ^- 3 $\times$ 10 $\times$ 1000 $\times$ 1 = 20J
$1\over2$ $\times$2 $\times$ 10^ - 3(50^2 ‚àí 0) = 20 + W_air
2.5 = 20 + W_air
W_air = ‚àí 17.5J

Q10. A 6.0-kg block initially at rest is pulled to the right along a horizontal frictionless surface by a constant horizontal force of 12 N. Find the speed of the block after it has moved 3.0 m?
    (A) 4.5 m/s
    (B) 5.5 m/s
    (C) 2.5 m/s
    (D) 3.5 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: From work kinetic energy theorem
K.E. = $\frac{1}{2}$m v^2
$\Delta$K = W
$\frac{1}{2}$mv^2 - $\frac{1}{2}$mu^2 = Fs
$\left(\frac{1}{2} \times 6 \times v^{2}\right)$ ‚àí 0 = 12 $\times$ 3
3 v^2 = 36
v^2 = 12
v = 3.5m/sec

Q11. A 6.0-kg block initially at rest is pulled to the right along a horizontal, surface having a coefficient of kinetic friction of 0.15, by a constant horizontal force of 12 N. Find the speed of the block after it has moved 3.0 m?
    (A) 1.8 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.8 m/s
    (C) 3.8 m/s
    (D) 2.8 m/s
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\Delta$K = W
F = 12N
f = $\mu$R = $\mu$mg = 0.15 $\times$ 6 $\times$ 9.8 = 8.82N
F_net = F - f = 12 - 8.82 = 3.18N
1/2mv^2 - 1/2mu^2 = W
1/2mv^2-0 = F_net x $x$
$\left(\frac{1}{2} \times 6 \times v^{2}\right)$ = 3.18 $\times$ 3
3v^2 = 3.18 $\times$ 3
v^2 = 3.18v = 1.8m/sec

Q12. A pump on the ground floor of a building can pump up water to fill a tank of volume 30m^3 in 15 min. If the tank is 40 m above the ground, and the efficiency of the pump is 30%, how much electric power is consumed by the pump?
    (A) 43.3 kW   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 33.6 kW
    (C) 38.3 kW
    (D) 45.2 kW
    Answer: A
    Explanation: P = $W\over t$
W = mgh
30m^3 = 30000 = 3 $\times$ 10^4 lit
mass of 30000 lit water = 30000 Kg
$P = {{mgh} \over t} = {{3 \times {{10}^4} \times 9.8 \times 40} \over {15 \times 60}} = 1.30 \times {10^4}W$ 
efficiency = power output / power consumption
$\eta=\frac{P}{P_{\mathrm{c}}}$
$P_{c}=\frac{P}{\eta}=\frac{1.30 \times 10^{4}}{0.3}$ = 4.33 √ó 10^4 = 43.3KW.

Q13. The bob of a pendulum is released from a horizontal position. If the length of the pendulum is 1.5 m, what is the speed with which the bob arrives at the lowermost point, given that it dissipated 5$\% $ of its initial energy against air resistance?
    (A) 4.9 m/s
    (B) 5.5 m/s
    (C) 4.7 m/s
    (D) 5.3 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: 95% of potential energy is converted into kinetic energy.
applying conservation of mechanical energy between horizontal and lowermost points
$mgl \times {{95} \over {100}} = {1 \over 2}m{v^2}$
$gl \times {{95} \over {100}} = {1 \over 2}{v^2}$
v = $\sqrt {{{2 \times gl \times 95} \over {100}}}$ = $\sqrt {{{2 \times 9.8 \times 1.5 \times 95} \over {100}}}$ = 5.3m/s

Q14. Consider a collision between two pool balls. Ball 1 is at rest and ball 2 is moving towards it with a speed of 2 ms^-1. The mass of each ball is 0.3 kg. After the balls collide elastically, ball 2 comes to an immediate stop and ball 1 move off. What is the final velocity of ball 1?
    (A) 2 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2.2 m/s
    (C) 2.4 m/s
    (D) 1.87 m/s
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Inelastic collision (e = 1) if the mass of colliding bodies is the same then their velocities after collision interchanged.
m_1 = m_2 = m
u_1 = 0
u_2 = 2m/s
${v_1} = \left( {{{{m_1} - {m_2}} \over {{m_1} + {m_2}}}} \right){u_1} + \left( {{{2{m_2}} \over {{m_1} + {m_2}}}} \right){u_2} $ = 2m/s
${v_2} = \left( {{{2{m_1}} \over {{m_1} + {m_2}}}} \right){u_1} + \left( {{{{m_2} - {m_1}} \over {{m_1} - {m_2}}}} \right){u_2} $ = 0

Q15. Consider two 2 marbles. Marble 1 has mass 100 g and marble 2 has mass 50 g. Edward rolls marble 1 along the ground towards marble 2 in the positive x-direction. Marble 2 is initially at rest and marble 1 has a velocity of 3 m /s in the positive x-direction. After they collide elastically, both marbles are moving. What is the final velocity of each marble?
    (A) ball 1 moves to the right at 2 m /s and ball 2 moves to the left with a velocity of 2m /s
    (B) ball 1 moves to the right at 5 m /s and ball 2 moves to the left with a velocity of 3m /s
    (C) ball 1 moves to the right with a velocity of 1m/s and ball 2 also moves to the right at 4 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ball 1 moves to the right at 3 m /s and ball 2 moves to the left with a velocity of 2m /s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: m_1 = 100gm
m_2 = 50gm
u_1 = 3m/s
u_2 = 0
$v_{1}=$$\left(\frac{m_{1}-m_{2}}{m_{1}+m_{2}}\right) u_{1}+\left(\frac{2 m_{2}}{m_{1}+m_{2}}\right) u_{2}$ = $\left(\frac{50}{150} \times 3\right)$ + 0 = 1 m/s
$v_{2}$ = $\left(\frac{2 m_{1}}{m_{1}+m_{2}}\right) u_{1}+\left(\frac{m_{2}-m_{1}}{m_{1}-m_{2}}\right) u_{2}$ = $\left(\frac{200}{150} \times 3\right)+0$ = 4m/s
