Q1. Two billiard balls each with a mass of 150g collide head-on in an elastic collision. Ball 1 was travelling at a speed of 2 m /s and ball 2 at a speed of 1.5 m /s. After the collision, ball 1 travels away from ball 2 at a velocity of 1.5 m /s .What is the velocity of ball 2?
    (A) ball 2 moves with a velocity of 2.5 m /s
    (B) ball 2 moves with a velocity of 2 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ball 2 moves with a velocity of 3.5 m/s
    (D) ball 2 moves with a velocity of 3.7 m/s
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the elastic collision (e = 1) if the mass of colliding bodies is the same then their velocities after collision interchanged.
m_1 = 150gm
m_2 = 150gm
u_1 = 2m/s
u_2 = ‚àí1.5m/s
$v_{1}=\left(\frac{m_{1}-m_{2}}{m_{1}+m_{2}}\right) u_{1}+\left(\frac{2 m_{2}}{m_{1}+m_{2}}\right) u_{2}$ = ‚àíu_2 = ‚àí1.5m/s
v_2 = $\left(\frac{2 m_{1}}{m_{1}+m_{2}}\right) u_{1}+\left(\frac{m_{2}-m_{1}}{m_{1}-m_{2}}\right) u_{2}$ = u_1 = 2 m/s
so that ball 2 moves with a velocity of 2 m/s

Q2. Consider the collision of two cars. Car 1 is at rest and Car 2 is moving at a speed of 2 m /s in the negative x-direction. Both cars each have a mass of 500 kg. The cars collide inelastically and stick together. What is the resulting velocity of the resulting mass of metal?
    (A) 1 m/s to the left   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1.5 m /s to the left
    (C) 1.2 m /s to the left
    (D) 1.4 m /s to the left
    Answer: A
    Explanation: from conservation of linear momentum initial momentum = final momentum
$\vec{p}_{i}=\vec{p}_{f}$
(500 $\times$ 0) + [500 $\times$ (‚àí2)] = (500 + 500)v
- 1000 = 1000v
v = ‚àí1m/s negative sign indicates that cars move to the left.

Q3. A body of mass 0.5 kg travels in a straight line with velocity v = $a x^{\frac 3 2}$ where a = $5 m^{\frac {‚àí1}{2}}s^{‚àí1}$. What is the work done by the net force during its displacement from x = 0 to x = 2 m is:
    (A) 10 J
    (B) 100 J
    (C) 50 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1.5 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mass of the body, m = 0.5 kg
The velocity of the body v = $ax^{\frac 3 2}$
a = 5 $m^{\frac {-1}{2}}$s^-1
Initial velocity at x = 0 is u = 0
Final velocity at x = 2 m is v = 10$\sqrt2$ m/s
work done = Change in kinetic energy
W = K_f - K_i
W =$\frac 12$mv^2 - 0
W = $\frac 12 \times$ 0.5 $\times$ (10$\sqrt 2$)^2 = $\frac 12 \times$0.5 $\times$ 200 = 50J

Q4. A person trying to lose weight (dieter) lifts a 10 kg mass, one thousand times, to a height of 0.5 m each time. Assume that the potential energy lost each time she lowers the mass is dissipated. How much work does she do against the gravitational force?
    (A) 49000 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 45000 J
    (C) 59000 J
    (D) 55000 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Work done by force applied against gravity for one lift will be
W = Fs = mgh = 10 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$ 0.5 = 49J
So work done for 1000 lifts = 49 $\times$ 1000 = 49000 J

Q5. A person trying to lose weight (dieter) lifts a 10 kg mass, one thousand times, to a height of 0.5 m each time. Assume that the potential energy lost each time she lowers the mass is dissipated. Fat supplies 3.8 ${\times }$ 10^7 J of energy per kilogram which is converted to mechanical energy with a 20% efficiency rate. How much fat will the dieter use up?
    (A) 7.45 $ \times $ 10^-3 kg
    (B) 6.45$ \times $ 10^-3 kg   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8.85 $ \times $ 10^-3 kg
    (D) 8.45 $ \times $ 10^-3 kg
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Work done by force applied against gravity for one lift will be
W = Fs = mgh = 10 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$ 0.5 = 49J
So work done for 1000 lifts = 49 $\times$ 1000 = 49000 J
efficiency = $Work \ done \over energy \ from \ fat$
energy from fat used = $Work \ done \over efficiency$
E = $ {W \over \eta } = {{49000} \over {0.2}} $ = 245000J
Energy from per kilogram fat = 3.8 ${\times }$ 10^7 J
Fat used $ = {{245000} \over {3.8 \times {{10}^7}}} $ = 64473 $\times$ 10^-7 = 6.45 $\times$ 10^-3 Kg

Q6. The Sun converts an enormous amount of matter to energy. Each second, 4.19 ${\times }$ 10^9 kg-approximately the capacity of 400 average-sized cargo ships-is changed to energy. What is the power output of the Sun?
    (A) 0.72 $ \times $ 10^26 W
    (B) 3.77 $ \times $ 10^26 W   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.57 $ \times $ 10^26 W
    (D) 2.62 $ \times $ 10^26 W
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The energy liberated per second 
E = mc^2 = 4.19 $\times$ 10^9 $\times$ 3 $\times$ 10^8 $\times$3 $\times$ 10^8 = 37.71 $\times$ 10^25 J
power output of the sun is equal to energy output per second 
P = ${W \over t} = {{37.71 \times {{10}^{25}}} \over 1} $ = 3.77 $\times$ 10^26 W

Q7. A block having a mass of 0.80 kg is given an initial velocity of 1.2 m/s to the right and collides with a spring of negligible mass and force constant k = 50 N/m. Assuming the surface to be frictionless, calculate the maximum compression of the spring after the collision.
    (A) 0.25 m
    (B) 0.10 m
    (C) 0.20 m
    (D) 0.15 m   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: for maximum compression 
${1 \over 2}k{x^2} = {1 \over 2}m{v^2}$
x = $ \sqrt {{{m{v^2}} \over k}} = \sqrt {{{0.8 \times 1.2 \times 1.2} \over {50}}} $ = 0.15m
the maximum compression of the spring after the collision = 0.15m.

Q8. The launching mechanism of a toy gun consists of a spring of unknown spring constant. When the spring is compressed 0.120 m, the gun, when fired vertically, is able to launch a 35.0-g projectile to a maximum height of 20.0 m above the position of the projectile before firing. Neglecting all resistive forces, determine the spring constant.
    (A) 953 N/m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 993 N/m
    (C) 903 N/m
    (D) 873 N/m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The potential energy of spring converted into potential energy
${1 \over 2}k{x^2} $ = mgh
k = ${{2mgh} \over {{x^2}}}$ =$ {{2 \times 35 \times {{10}^{ - 3}} \times 9.8 \times 20} \over {0.12 \times 0.12}} $ = 953N/m

Q9. A 3.00-kg crate slides down a ramp. The ramp is 1.00 m in length and inclined at an angle of 30.0^o. The crate starts from rest at the top, experiences a constant frictional force of magnitude 5.00 N, and continues to move a short distance on the flat floor after it leaves the ramp. Use energy methods to determine the speed of the crate at the bottom of the ramp?
    (A) 1.76 m/s
    (B) 2.25 m/s
    (C) 2.54 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2.78 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Height of ramp 
h = lsin30^o = 1 $\times$ 1/2 = 0.5m
from work kinetic energy theorem
K_f - K_i = W_mg + W_f
$1\over 2$mv^2 - 0 = mgh + fd
$1\over 2$ $\times$ 3v^2 = (3 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$0.5) + [5 $\times$ ( - 1)]
$\frac{3}{2}$v^2 = 14.7 - 5
v^2 = 9.7 $\times$ $\frac{2}{3}$
v = $\sqrt{\frac{9.7 \times 2}{3}}$ = 2.54m/s

Q10. A bullet of mass 0.012 kg and horizontal speed 70 m ${\rm{s}}{-^{\rm{1}}}$ strikes a block of wood of mass 0.4 kg and instantly comes to rest with respect to the block. The block is suspended from the ceiling by means of thin wires. Calculate the height to which the block rises. Also, estimate the amount of heat produced in the bloc?.
    (A) 23.2 cm, 38.5 J
    (B) 21.2 cm, 28.5 J   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 29.2 cm, 29.5 J
    (D) 72.2 cm, 28.5 J
    Answer: B
    Explanation: mass of bullet m = 0.012 kg
mass of block = 0.4 kg
The initial speed of a bullet, u =70m/s
Let the final speed of block and bullet which move together = v m/s
According to the law of conservation of momentum,
$v\sqrt{\frac{9.7 \times 2}{3}}$
v =$ {{mu} \over {M + m}} = {{0.012 \times 70} \over {0.412}} $ = 2.04m/s
Let block rises to a height h after the collision, then
Loss in K.E. of block and bullet = Gain in P.E. after the collision.
${1 \over 2}\left( {m + M} \right){v^2} $ = (m + M)gh
h = $ {{{v^2}} \over {2g}} = {{2.04 \times 2.04} \over {2 \times 9.8}} $ = 0.212m = 21.2 cm
Heat produced in the block = loss of K.E. = K.E. of bullet - K.E. of block and bullet
Heat produced in the block = ${1 \over 2}m{u^2} - {1 \over 2}\left( {m + M} \right){v^2}$ = $ \left( {{1 \over 2} \times 0.012 \times 70 \times 70} \right) - \left( {{1 \over 2} \times 0.412 \times 2.04 \times 2.04} \right) $ = 28.5J

Q11. A 1 kg block situated on a rough incline is connected to a spring of spring constant 100 Nm^-1 as shown in Figure. The block is released from rest with the spring in the unstretched position. The block moves 10 cm down the incline before coming to rest. Find the coefficient of friction between the block and the incline. Assume that the spring has a negligible mass and the pulley is frictionless.
    (A) 0.112   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.25
    (C) 0.3
    (D) 0.07
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The weight of the block can be resolved in two components.
the component parallel to incline plane (mgsin37^o)and a component perpendicular to the plane (mgcos37^o) 
at equilibrium
R = mg cos 37^o 
f = $\mu$R = $\mu$mg cos 37
The net force acting on the block = mgsin37^o - f 
= mgsin37^o ‚àí $\mu $mgcos37^o 
At equilibrium, the work done by the block is equal to the potential energy of the spring, i.e.,
= (mg sin 37^o - $\mu$mg cos 37^o) $x$ = $\frac{1}{2}$kx^2 
$(1 \times 9.8 \times 0.6)-(\mu \times 1 \times 9.8 \times 0.8)$ $=\frac{1}{2} \times 100 \times 0.1$
5.88 - 7.84$\mu$ = 5
$\mu=\frac{0.88}{0.784}$ = 0.112

Q12. A bolt of mass 0.3 kg falls from the ceiling of an elevator moving down with a uniform speed of 7 m/s. It hits the floor of the elevator (length of the elevator = 3 m) and does not rebound. What is the heat produced by the impact?
    (A) 8.42 J
    (B) 9.22 J
    (C) 8.82 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 8.11 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The whole of the potential energy of bolt converted into heat energy 
heat produced by the impact = mgh = 0.3 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$ 3 = 8.82J

Q13. A trolley of mass 200 kg moves with a uniform speed of 36 km/h on a frictionless track. A child of mass 20 kg runs on the trolley from one end to the other (10 m away) with a speed of 4 ms^-1 relatives to the trolley in a direction opposite to its motion, and jumps out of the trolley. What is the final speed of the trolley?
    (A) 9.36 m/s
    (B) 8.13 m/s
    (C) 10.36 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 11.36 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Mass of trolley M = 200Kg
mass of child m = 20Kg
speed of trolley v = 36Km/hr = 36 $\times$ $5\over 18$ = 10m/s
Let v' be the final velocity of the trolley with respect to the ground.
The final velocity of the boy with respect to the ground = v' - 4
from conservation of linear momentum
p_i = p_f
(M + m)v = Mv' +m(v' ‚àí 4)
(200 + 20) $\times$ 10 = 200v' + 20(v' ‚àí 4)
2200 = 220v' - 80
= $2280\over 220$ = 10.36m/s

Q14. A trolley of mass 200 kg moves with a uniform speed of 36 km/h on a frictionless track. A child of mass 20 kg runs on the trolley from one end to the other (10 m away) with a speed of 4 ms^‚àí1 relatives to the trolley in a direction opposite to its motion, and jumps out of the trolley. How much has the trolley moved from the time the child begins to run?
    (A) 25.9 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 23.3 m
    (C) 24.1 m
    (D) 27.8 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Mass of trolly M = 200Kg
mass of child m = 20Kg
speed of trolley v = 36Km/hr = 36 $\times$ $5\over 18$ = 10m/s
Let v' be the final velocity of the trolley with respect to the ground.
The final velocity of the boy with respect to the ground = v' - 4 
from conservation of linear momentum
p_i = p_f
(M + m)v = Mv' + m(v' ‚àí 4)
(200 + 20) $\times$ 10 = 200v' + 20(v' ‚àí 4)
2200 = 220v' - 80
v' = $2280\over 220$ = 10.36m/s
Time taken by the boy to run, t = $10\over 4$ = 2.5 sec
Distance moved by the trolley = v't = 10.36 $\times$ 2.5 = 25.9 m

Q15. A 50.0-kg marathon runner runs up the stairs to the top of a 443-m-tall Tower. To lift herself to the top in 15.0 minutes, what must be her average power output?
    (A) 241 W   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 221 W
    (C) 261 W
    (D) 201 W
    Answer: A
    Explanation: P = $ {W \over t}$
W = mgh = 50 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$ 443
t = 15 $\times$ 60sec
P = ${{50 \times 9.8 \times 443} \over {15 \times 60}} $ = 241 W.

Q1. A 75.0-kg painter climbs a ladder that is 2.75 m long leaning against a vertical wall. The ladder makes an angle of $30^\circ $ with the wall. How much work does gravity do on the painter?
    (A) -1750 J   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -1850 J
    (C) -1950 J
    (D) -2050 J
    Answer: A
    Explanation: W = ‚àímgh
h = $ x\cos 30^\circ = 2.75 \times {{\sqrt 3 } \over 2}$
$W = - 75 \times 9.8 \times 2.75 \times {{\sqrt 3 } \over 2} $ = - 1750J

Q2. A 0.800-kg ball is tied to the end of a string 1.60 m long and swung in a vertical circle. (a) During one complete circle, starting anywhere, calculate the total work done on the ball by
 the tension in the string and
 gravity
    (A) 10 J, 10 J
    (B) 30 J, 30 J
    (C) 0, 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 25 J, -25 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Work done by the conservative force in round trip will be zero (displacement = 0).
So that work done by tension and gravity will be zero.

Q3. A 0.800-kg ball is tied to the end of a string 1.60 m long and swung in a vertical circle. Calculate the total work done on the ball by
 the tension in the string and
 gravity for motion along the semicircle from the lowest to the highest point on the path.
    (A) 0, -281 J
    (B) 0, -2.51 J
    (C) 0, -25.1 J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0, -251 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: work done by tension will be zero because tension is perpendicular to the displacement.
W = Tscos90^o = 0
work is done by gravity in a semicircle from the lowest to the highest point on the path
W = mghcos180^o = 0.8 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$ 3.2 $\times$ (‚àí1) = ‚àí25.1J

Q4. Adult cheetahs, the fastest of the great cats, have a mass of about 70 kg and have been clocked running at up to 72 mph (32 m/s). How many joules of kinetic energy does such a swift cheetah have?
    (A) 34,000 J
    (B) 29,000 J
    (C) 32,000 J
    (D) 35840 J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The kinetic energy of a cheetah 
K = $ {1 \over 2}m{v^2}$
m = 70Kg
v = 32m/s
K = $\frac{1}{2}$ $\times$ 70 $\times$ 32 $\times$ 32 = 35840J

Q5. A sled with mass 8.00 kg moves in a straight line on a frictionless horizontal surface. At one point in its path, its speed is 4.00 m/s; after it has traveled 2.50 m beyond this point, its speed is 6.00 m/s. Use the work-energy theorem to find the force acting on the sled, assuming that this force is constant and that it acts in the direction of the sled‚Äôs motion.
    (A) 30.0 N
    (B) 28.0 N
    (C) 32.0 N   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 34.0 N
    Answer: C
    Explanation: from work-energy theorem
change in kinetic energy = work done
$\Delta K$ = W
K_f ‚àí K_i = F_s
${1 \over 2}m{v_f}^2 - {1 \over 2}m{v_i}^2 = Fs $
${1 \over 2}m\left( {{v_f}^2 - {v_i}^2} \right) = Fs$ 
m = 8Kg, s = 2.5m
v_f = 6m/s, v_i = 4m/s
$1 \over 2$ $\times$ 8(6^2 ‚àí 4^2) = F $\times$ 2.5
4 $\times$20 = F $\times$ 2.5
F = ${{80} \over {2.5}}$ = 32N

Q6. A 12-pack of Omni-Cola (mass 4.30 kg) is initially at rest on a horizontal floor. It is then pushed in a straight line for 1.20 m by a trained dog that exerts a horizontal force with magnitude 36.0 N. Use the work-energy theorem to find the final speed of the 12-pack if there is no friction between the 12-pack and the floor.
    (A) 4.38 m/s
    (B) 4.68 m/s
    (C) 4.48 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4.58 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: from work-energy theorem
change in kinetic energy = work done
$\Delta K$ = W
K_f - K_i = Fs
${1 \over 2}m{v^2} - 0 $ = Fs 
m = 4.30Kg, s = 1.2m, F = 36N
v_f = vm/s, v_i = 0
${1 \over 2}m{v^2} = Fs$
$1\over 2$ $\times$ 4.3 $\times$ v^2 = 36 $\times$ 1.2
$v = \sqrt {{{36 \times 1.2 \times 2} \over {4.3}}} $ = 4.48m/s

Q7. A12-pack of Omni-Cola (mass 4.30 kg) is initially at rest on a horizontal floor. It is then pushed in a straight line for 1.20 m by a trained dog that exerts a horizontal force with magnitude 36.0 N. Use the work-energy theorem to find the final speed of the 12-pack if the coefficient of kinetic friction between the 12-pack and the floor is 0.30?
    (A) 3.81 m/s
    (B) 4.01 m/s
    (C) 3.61 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4.22 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\Delta$K = W
F = 36N
f = $\mu$R = $\mu$mg = 0.3 $\times$ 4.3 $\times$ 9.8 = 12.642N
F_net = F - f = 36 - 12.642 = 23.358N
s = 1.2 m
$\frac{1}{2} m v^{2}$ - 0 = F_net $\times$ s
$\frac{1}{2}$$ \times$ 4.3 $ \times$ v^2 = 23.358 $ \times$ 1.2
${v^2} = {{23.358 \times 1.2 \times 2} \over {4.3}} $ = 13.03
v = $ \sqrt {13.03} $ = 3.61m/s

Q8. A 6.0-kg box moving at 3.0 m/s on a horizontal, frictionless surface runs into a light spring of force constant 75 N/cm Use the work‚Äìenergy theorem to find the maximum compression of the spring.
    (A) 8.5 cm   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 9.5 cm
    (C) 7.5 cm
    (D) 6.5 cm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: For maximum compression of spring, kinetic energy will be converted into the potential energy of spring.
${1 \over 2}k{x^2} = {1 \over 2}m{v^2}$
${x^2} = {{m{v^2}} \over k} = {{6 \times 3 \times 3} \over {75 \times {{10}^2}}}$
$x = \sqrt {{{6 \times 3 \times 3} \over {75 \times {{10}^2}}}} $ = 0.085m = 8.5cm

Q9. How many joules of energy does a 100-watt light bulb use per hour? How fast would a 70-kg person have to run to have that amount of kinetic energy?
    (A) 360000 J, 101 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 380000 J, 120 m/s
    (C) 320000 J, 130 m/s
    (D) 340000 J, 140 m/s
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Energy = P $\times$ Time = 100 $\times$ 1Hr
Energy = 100 $\times$ 1 $\times$ 60 $\times$ 60 = 360000 J
for a 70 Kg man $K = {1 \over 2}m{v^2}$ 
speed of man v = $ \sqrt {{{2K} \over m}} = \sqrt {{{2 \times 360000} \over {70}}} $ = 101m/s

Q10. A tandem (two-person) bicycle team must overcome a force of 165 N to maintain a speed of 9.00 m/s. Find the power required per rider, assuming that each contributes equally?
    (A) 798 W
    (B) 742.5 W   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 702 W
    (D) 765 W
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Total power required to overcome a force of 165 N and to maintain a speed of 9.00 m/s
F = 165N
v = 9m/s
P = Fv = 165 $\times$ 9 = 1485W
if each rider contribute equal power, then the power required per rider will be $P\over 2$ = $1485\over 2$ = 742.5W

Q11. You are asked to design spring bumpers for the walls of a parking garage. A freely rolling 1200-kg car moving at 0.65 m/s is to compress the spring no more than 0.090 m before stopping. What should be the force constant of the spring? Assume that the spring has negligible mass.
    (A) 5.3 $ \times $ 10^4 N/m
    (B) 6.25 $ \times $ 10^4 N/m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 5.8 $ \times $ 10^4 N/m
    (D) 6.6 $ \times $10^4 N/m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The kinetic energy of the car will be converted into the potential energy of spring.
${1 \over 2}k{x^2} = {1 \over 2}m{v^2}$
$k = {{m{v^2}} \over {{x^2}}}$
m = 1200Kg
v = 0.65m/s
x = 0.09m
$k = {{1200 \times 0.65 \times 0.65} \over {0.09 \times 0.09}} $ = 6.25 $\times$ 10^4N/m

Q12. On an essentially frictionless, horizontal ice rink, a skater moving at 3.0 m/s encounters a rough patch that reduces her speed to 1.65 m/s due to a friction force that is 25$\% $ of her weight. Use the work-energy theorem to find the length of this rough patch?
    (A) 1.1 m
    (B) 1.3 m   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.9 m
    (D) 1.5 m
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Using the work-energy theorem, change in kinetic energy = work done by the friction force
$\Delta K$ =W_f
$\frac{1}{2} m\left(v_{f}^{2}-v_{i}^{2}\right)$ = -fd
$\frac{1}{2} m\left(v_{f}^{2}-v_{i}^{2}\right)$ = $-m g \times \frac{25}{100} \times d$
$\frac{1}{2} m\left[(1.65)^{2}-(3)^{2}\right]$ = $-m \times 9.8 \times \frac{25}{100} \times d$
$\frac{1}{2} \times(2.7225-9)=-9.8 \times \frac{25}{100} \times d$
$-\frac{6.2775}{2}=-9.8 \times \frac{25}{100} \times d$
d = $\frac{6.2775 \times 100}{2 \times 9.8 \times 25}$ = 1.3 m

Q13. A pump is required to lift 800 kg of water per minute from a well 14.0 m deep and eject it with a speed of 18.0 m/s. How much work is done per minute in lifting the water?
    (A) 1.40 $ \times $ 10^5 J
    (B) 1.30 $ \times $ 10^5 J
    (C) 1.20 $ \times $ 10^5 J
    (D) 1.10 $ \times $ 10^5 J   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: mass is given by ,m = 800Kg per minute
h = 14m
work done per minute in lifting the water is given by :-
W = mgh = 800 $\times$ 9.8 $\times$ 14 = 109760J = 1.1 $\times$ 10^5J

Q14. A pump is required to lift 800 kg of water (about 210 gallons) per minute from a well 14.0 m deep and eject it with a speed of 18.0 m/s. How much work is done in giving the water the kinetic energy it has when ejected?
    (A) 1.10 $ \times $ 10^5J
    (B) 1.30 $ \times $ 10^5J   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.40 $ \times $ 10^5J
    (D) 1.20 $ \times $ 10^5J
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Work is done in giving kinetic energy is equal to change in kinetic energy
W = $ \Delta K$
$W = {1 \over 2}m{v^2} - 0$
W = $\frac{1}{2}$ $\times$ 800 $\times$ 18 $\times$ 18 = 129600J = 1.3 $\times$ 10^5J

Q15. In which of the following cases is the work done positively?
    (A) Work is done by friction on a body sliding down an inclined plane.
    (B) Work is done by gravitational force while a man in lifts a bucket out of a well by means of a rope tied to the bucket.
    (C) Work is done by the resistive force of air on a vibrating pendulum in bringing it to rest.
    (D) Work is done by an applied force on a body moving on a rough horizontal plane with uniform velocity.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When a body is moving on a rough horizontal surface then there will be 2 forces acting on the body 
 Applied force ( in the direction of motion)
 friction ( opposite to the direction of motion)
As applied force is in the same direction as displacement so work is done will be positive.

Particles & Rotational Motion Test 01  (id 557) [FREE]

Q1. A rigid body is a body which:
    (A) deforms on the application of force.
    (B) becomes longer or shorter if force is applied.
    (C) does not deform on the application of force.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) does not maintain the same distance between any two points on it if force is applied.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A rigid body is an idealization of a solid body in which deformation or change in shape is neglected on the application of deforming force.

Q2. In the pure translational motion of a rigid body:
    (A) at different instants of time, every particle of the body has the same velocity.
    (B) at any instant of time different particles of the body have different velocities.
    (C) at any instant of time velocity is dependent on the position vector of a point on the body.
    (D) at any instant of time, every particle of the body has the same velocity.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In translational motion when the body moves along a straight line or more exactly when every point of the body travels on parallel lines, thus at any instant of time every particle of the body has the same velocity.

Q3. In rotation of a rigid body about a fixed axis is that in which:
    (A) every particle of the body moves in a circle, which lies in a plane perpendicular to the axis and has its centre on the axis.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) every particle of the body moves in an ellipse, which lies in a plane perpendicular to the axis and has its focii on the axis.
    (C) every particle of the body moves at the same speed.
    (D) particles close to the axis have larger velocities.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When a rigid body rotates about a fixed axis, all particles of the body except those which lies on the axis of rotation, move along circular paths in a plane perpendicular to the axis.

Q4. In precession such as that of a top:
    (A) the axis of rotation is fixed
    (B) the axis of rotation moves   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the axis of rotation oscillates vertically
    (D) the axis of rotation oscillates horizontally
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Precession is a change in the orientation of the rotational axis of a rotating body, so the orientation of the axis of rotation of Top change.

Q5. In general motion of a rigid body:
    (A) particles on the body always move around an axis in circles
    (B) both translation and rotation can be present   <-- CORRECT
    (C) only rotation is present
    (D) only translation is present
    Answer: B
    Explanation: In the general motion of the body can be seen as the combination of pure translation of the center of mass and pure rotation of the body about the center of mass like the motion of a wheel.

Q6. Let r_i be the position vector of the i^th particle having mass m_i and R be the position vector of the centre of mass. The formula for R is:
    (A) $\mathbf{R}=\frac{\sum^{m_1} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{i}}}{\sum^{m_3}}$
    (B) $\mathbf{R}=\frac{\sum^{m_1} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{i}}}{\sum^{m_1}}$
    (C) $R=\frac{\sum m_1 \cdot r_i}{\sum m_1}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\mathbf{R}=\frac{\sum^{m_1} \mathbf{r}_{\mathbf{i}}}{\sum^{m_2}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let us consider a system consisting of N ‚Äì particles of masses m_1, m_2,‚Ä¶.. m_N having position vectors ${\vec r_1},{\vec r_2}$,...... $ {\vec r_N} $ respectively.
The total mass M of the system is given by 
M = m¬≠_1 +m_2 +‚Ä¶‚Ä¶.+ m_N 
We can generalize the definition of the position of centre of mass consisting of N particles, hence the position vector of centre of mass is given below:-
$\vec{R}=\frac{m_1 \vec{r}_1+m_2 \vec{r}_2+\ldots \ldots \ldots+m_N \vec{r}_N}{m_1+m_2+\ldots \ldots+m_N}=\frac{\sum_\limits{i=1}^N m_i \vec{r}_i}{\sum_\limits{i=1}^N m_i}=\frac{\sum_\limits{i=1}^N m_i \vec{r}_i}{M}$

Q7. the centre of mass of a system of particles moves
    (A) as if all the mass of the system was concentrated at the axis of rotation and all the external forces were absent
    (B) as if all the mass of the system was concentrated at the centre of mass and all the external forces were zero
    (C) as if all the mass of the system was concentrated at the centre of mass and all the external forces were applied at that point   <-- CORRECT
    (D) as if all the mass of the system was concentrated in a sphere around the centre of mass and all the external forces were zero
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The centre of mass of a system of particles moves as if all the mass of the system is concentrated at the centre and all the external forces were applied at that point. In order to ease the calculations involved in the dynamics of an extended body, we treat any extended body as the system of particles, and the motion of centre of mass of the system is calculated by taking the mass of the whole system to be concentrated at the centre of mass and the external forces acting on system are said to be acting on the centre of mass.

Q8. The total momentum of a system of particles is equal to:
    (A) the product of half the total mass of the system and the velocity of its centre of mass
    (B) the product of the total mass of the system and the speed of its centre of mass
    (C) the product of the total mass of the system and the velocity of its centre of mass   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the product of the total mass of the system and the average velocity of its centre of mass
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let us consider a system of n particles of masses m_1, m_2, ‚Ä¶.m_N. If M is the total mass of the system.
M = m_1 + m_2 +‚Ä¶‚Ä¶..+ m_N
If ${\vec R}$ is the position vector of the centre of mass and ${\vec r_1},{\vec r_2},{\vec r_3} . ..... {\vec r_n}$those of constituent particles then
$\mathop R\limits^ \to = {{{m_1}{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_1} + {m_2}{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_2} + .... + {m_N}{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_N}} \over {{m_1} + {m_2} + ..... + {m_N}}} $ = $ {{{m_1}{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_1} + {m_2}{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_2} + {m_N}{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_N}} \over M}$ 
Differentiating both sides w.r.t. time t, we get
${{d\mathop R\limits^ \to } \over {dt}} $ = $ {1 \over M}\left[ {{m_1}{{d{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_1}} \over {dt}} + {m_2}{{d{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_2}} \over {dt}} + .......... + {m_N}{{d{{\mathop r\limits^ \to }_N}} \over {dt}}} \right]$ 
Let the velocity of centre of mass is ${{d\mathop R\limits^ \to } \over {dt}} = \mathop {{V_{CM}}}\limits^ \to $
${{d\mathop {{r_1}}\limits^ \to } \over {dt}} = {\mathop v\limits^ \to _1},{{d\mathop {{r_2}}\limits^ \to } \over {dt}} = {\mathop v\limits^ \to _{2,}}.....{{d\mathop {{r_n}}\limits^ \to } \over {dt}} = \mathop {{v_n}}\limits^ \to $ 
$M\mathop {{V_{CM}}}\limits^ \to $ = $ {m_1}{\mathop v\limits^ \to _1} + {m_2}{\mathop v\limits^ \to _2} + .... + {m_N}{\mathop v\limits^ \to _N} = \sum\limits_{i = 1}^N {{m_i}\,\,\,{{\mathop v\limits^ \to }_i}} $ 
Hence the total momentum of a system of particles is equal to the product of the total mass of the system and the velocity of its centre of mass.

Q9. Considering binary (double) stars in our frame of reference, the trajectories of the stars are a combination of
    (A) uniform motion in a straight line and
 elliptical orbits of the stars
    (B) uniform motion in a straight line and
 circular orbits of the stars   <-- CORRECT
    (C) uniform motion in a straight line and
 straight line motion of the stars
    (D) uniform motion in a circle and
 circular orbits of the stars
    Answer: B
    Explanation: A double star or visual double is a pair of stars that appear close to each other in the sky as seen from Earth when viewed through an optical telescope.
In absence of external force Centre of mass of double star moves like a free particle. In Centre of mass frame both stars moving in a circle about the Centre of mass which is at rest and both star are diametrically opposite to each other.
Thus in our frame of reference, the trajectories of the stars are a combination of
uniform motion in a straight line of the Centre of mass and 
circular orbits of the stars about the Centre of mass. 
Trajectories of two stars, S_1 (dotted line) and S_2 (solid line) forming a binary system with their centre of mass C in uniform motion.
The same binary system, with the centre of mass C at rest.

Q10. The vector product of two vectors a and b is a vector c such that the magnitude of c is given by:
    (A) $\left| {\mathbf{a}} \right|\left| {\mathbf{b}} \right|$cot$\theta $
    (B) $\left| {\mathbf{a}} \right|\left| {\mathbf{b}} \right|$cos$\theta $
    (C) $\left| {\mathbf{a}} \right|\left| {\mathbf{b}} \right|$sin$\theta $   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\left| {\mathbf{a}} \right|\left| {\mathbf{b}} \right|$tan$\theta $
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As per the definition of vector product:-
$\vec c = \vec a \times \vec b = \left| {\vec a} \right|\left| {\vec b} \right|\sin \theta \hat n$
$\left| {\vec c} \right| = \left| {\vec a} \right|\left| {\vec b} \right|\sin \theta $

Q11. The vector product of two vectors a and b is a vector c such that c is perpendicular to the plane containing a and b and the direction is given by:
    (A) index finger rule
    (B) left-handed screw rule
    (C) right-handed screw rule   <-- CORRECT
    (D) left hand rule
    Answer: C
    Explanation: If vectors A and B lie in the plane of this page, the vector C will be perpendicular to this plane. 
The sense (upward or downward) of the direction of the vector product is given by the direction of the advance of the tip of a right-handed screw when rotated from A to B through angle $\theta$ between them, the screw being placed with its axis perpendicular to the plane containing the two vectors.

Q12. If $\overrightarrow{\mathbf{a}}=a_x \hat{\mathbf{i}}+a_y \hat{\mathbf{j}}+a_z \hat{\mathbf{k}}$ and $\overrightarrow{\mathbf{b}}=b_x \hat{\mathbf{i}}+b_y \hat{\mathbf{j}}+b_z \hat{\mathbf{k}}$ then the cross product $\overrightarrow{\mathbf{a}} \times \overrightarrow{\mathbf{b}}$ is given by:
    (A) $\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {{\mathbf{\hat i}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat j}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat k}}} \\ {{{\text{a}}_{\text{x}}}}&{{a_x}}&{{a_z}} \\ {{b_x}}&{{b_x}}&{{b_z}} \end{array}} \right|$
    (B) $\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {{\mathbf{\hat i}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat j}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat k}}} \\ {{{\text{a}}_{\text{x}}}}&{{a_y}}&{{a_z}} \\ {{b_x}}&{{b_x}}&{{b_z}} \end{array}} \right|$
    (C) $\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {{\mathbf{\hat i}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat j}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat k}}} \\ {{{\text{a}}_{\text{x}}}}&{{a_y}}&{{a_z}} \\ {{b_x}}&{{b_y}}&{{b_x}} \end{array}} \right|$
    (D) $\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {{\mathbf{\hat i}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat j}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat k}}} \\ {{{\text{a}}_{\text{x}}}}&{{a_y}}&{{a_z}} \\ {{b_x}}&{{b_y}}&{{b_z}} \end{array}} \right|$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: ${\bf{\vec a}} \times {\bf{\vec b}}$ = $ \left( {{a_y}{b_z} - {a_z}{b_y}} \right){\bf{\hat i}} $ - $\left( {{a_x}{b_z} - {a_z}{b_x}} \right){\bf{\hat j}}$ + $ \left( {{a_x}{b_y} - {a_y}{b_x}} \right){\bf{\hat k}}$ 
As the cross product is the determinant of a 3x3 matrix.
$\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {{\mathbf{\hat i}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat j}}}&{{\mathbf{\hat k}}} \\ {{{\text{a}}_{\text{x}}}}&{{a_y}}&{{a_z}} \\ {{b_x}}&{{b_y}}&{{b_z}} \end{array}} \right|$

Q13. If a body is rotating about z-axis with a speed $\omega $ and a point is at a distance of r in the x-y plane then the velocity of the point is:
    (A) $2r\omega $
    (B) $r\omega $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $r\omega /2$
    (D) $3r\omega $
    Answer: B
    Explanation: the angular displacement of a particle about the z-axis
$d\theta = {{ds} \over r}$ 
differentiate with respect to time
${{d\theta } \over {dt}} = {1 \over r}{{ds} \over {dt}}$
${{d\theta } \over {dt}} = \omega$
${{ds} \over {dt}} $ = v
$\omega = {v \over r}$
v = $ r\omega$

Q14. The moment of inertia of a body about any axis is
    (A) equal to the sum of the moment of inertia of the body about any axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
    (B) equal to the sum of the moment of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) equal to the difference of the moment of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
    (D) equal to the average of the moments of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: according to parallel axis theorem the moment of inertia of a body about any axis is equal to the sum of the moment of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its Centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
$I = {I_{cm}} + M{a^2}$

Q15. The angular acceleration vector is defined as:
    (A) $\alpha=\frac{d \omega}{d t}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\alpha=\frac{d^3 \omega}{d t^3}$
    (C) $\alpha=2 \frac{d \omega}{d t}$
    (D) $\alpha=\frac{d^2 w}{d t^2}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As per the definition of angular acceleration that " it is the time rate of change of angular velocity" , therefore $\alpha=\frac{d \omega}{d t}$

Particles & Rotational Motion Test 02  (id 558) [PAID]

Q1. Torque $\tau $ is defined in terms of the position vector $r$ and the force acting F as:
    (A) $\tau = r \times F.r$
    (B) $\tau = F + r$
    (C) $\tau = r.r \times F$
    (D) $\tau = r \times F$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Torque = Force $\times$ Perpendicular distance of the line of action of the force from the axis of rotation. It is also called the moment of force.
Torque is defined as the cross product of the vector by which the force's application point is offset relative to the fixed suspension point (distance vector) and the force vector, which tends to produce rotational motion.
$\vec \tau = \vec r \times \vec F$

Q2. The angular momentum L of the particle having a position vector $r$ and linear momentum $p$, with respect to the origin O is defined to be
    (A) $\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p.\vec \omega $
    (B) $L = \vec r \times \vec p \times \vec r$
    (C) $\vec L = \vec r \times \vec r \times \vec p$
    (D) $\vec L =\vec r \times\vec p$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Angular momentum is also referred to as a moment of linear momentum
The angular momentum L of a particle of mass m with respect to a chosen origin is given by
$\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p$ 
The direction of angular momentum is according to the right-hand rule.

Q3. Torque $\tau $ and angular momentum L are related by:
    (A) $\tau=\frac{d L}{d t}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\tau=\frac{d^2 L}{d t^2}$
    (C) $\tau=2 \frac{d L}{d t}$
    (D) $\tau=\frac{d^3 L}{d t^3}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p$ 
on differentiation with respect to time 
$\frac{d \vec{L}}{d t}=\frac{d}{d t}(\vec{r} \times \vec{p})$ 
Applying the product rule for differentiation to the right-hand side,
$\frac{d}{d t}(\vec{r} \times \vec{p})=\left(\frac{d \vec{r}}{d t} \times \vec{p}\right)+\left(\vec{r} \times \frac{d \vec{p}}{d t}\right)$
$\frac{d \vec{r}}{d t}=\vec{v}, \vec{p}=m \vec{v}$
$\left(\frac{d \vec{r}}{d t} \times \vec{p}\right)=\vec{v} \times m \vec{v}=0$
$\frac{d \vec{p}}{d t}=\vec{F}$
$\left(\vec{r} \times \frac{d \vec{p}}{d t}\right)=\vec{r} \times \vec{F}=\vec{\tau}$
Hence $\vec{\tau}=\frac{d \vec{L}}{d t}$

Q4. A rigid body is in mechanical equilibrium if:
    (A) $\sum F \ne 0$ and $\sum \tau \ne 0$
    (B) $\sum F = 0$ and $\sum \tau = 0$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\sum F \ne 0$ and $\sum \tau = 0$
    (D) $\sum F = 0$ and $\sum \tau \ne 0$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: For the mechanical equilibrium of a rigid body, it must be in translational as well as in rotational equilibrium. Linear acceleration and angular acceleration must be zero. Hence net force and net torque will be zero that is $\sum F = 0$ and $\sum \tau = 0$

Q5. Centre of gravity can be defined:
    (A) as that point where the total gravitational torque on the body is zero   <-- CORRECT
    (B) as that point where the total gravitational torque on the body is greater than zero
    (C) as the center of mass
    (D) as that point where the total gravitational force on the body is zero
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The point at which the entire weight of a body may be thought of as centered so that if supported at this point the body would balance perfectly, so it can also be defined as that point where the total gravitational torque on the body is zero.

Q6. Analogue of mass in rotational motion is:
    (A) rotary mass
    (B) angular acceleration
    (C) torque
    (D) moment of inertia   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The moment of inertia is a physical quantity that tells how easily a body can be rotated about a given axis. It is a rotational analog of mass. It plays the same role in rotational motion as 'inertia' does in translational motion. A large moment of inertia also helps in keeping the rotation motion uniform.

Q7. The radius of gyration of a body about an axis may be defined as the
    (A) distance from the center of gravity to the axis of rotation
    (B) distance from the center of gravity to the center of mass
    (C) distance from the center of mass to the axis of rotation
    (D) distance from the axis of a mass point whose mass is equal to the mass of the whole body and whose moment of inertia is equal to the moment of inertia of the body about the axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It is the perpendicular distance from the axis of rotation to a point mass of mass m that gives an equivalent inertia to the original object (of mass, m)
if radius of gyration is k then 
$\eqalign{ & I = m{k^2} \cr & k = \sqrt {{I \over m}} \cr} $

Q8. The moment of inertia of a planar body (lamina) about an axis perpendicular to its plane is.
    (A) equal to the its moments of inertia about an axis perpendicular to the axis of rotation axis and lying in the plane of the body
    (B) equal to the difference of its moments of inertia about two perpendicular axes concurrent with perpendicular axis and lying in the plane of the body
    (C) equal to the average of its moments of inertia about three perpendicular axes concurrent with perpendicular axis and lying in the plane of the body
    (D) equal to the sum of its moments of inertia about two perpendicular axes concurrent with perpendicular axis and lying in the plane of the body   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: According to perpendicular axis theorem "For a planar object, the moment of inertia about an axis perpendicular to the plane is the sum of the moments of inertia of two perpendicular axes through the same point in the plane of the object".
${I_z} = {I_x} + {I_y}$

Q9. The moment of inertia of a body about any axis is
    (A) equal to the sum of the moment of inertia of the body about any axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
    (B) equal to the average of the moments of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
    (C) equal to the difference of the moment of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
    (D) equal to the sum of the moment of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: according to parallel axis theorem the moment of inertia of a body about any axis is equal to the sum of the moment of inertia of the body about a parallel axis passing through its Centre of mass and the product of its mass and the square of the distance between the two parallel axes.
$I = {I_{cm}} + M{a^2}$

Q10. The angular acceleration of a rigid body ${\bf{\alpha }}$ rotating about a fixed axis is given by (I is the moment of inertia and ${\bf{\tau }}$ is the torque):
    (A) ${\rm{I}}\alpha $ = ${\rm{2}}\tau $
    (B) ${\rm{I}}\alpha $ = $\frac{\tau}{\rm{3}}$
    (C) ${\rm{I}}\alpha $ = ${\bf{\tau }}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\rm{I}}\alpha $ = $\frac{\tau}{\rm{2}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $L = I\omega $ 
differentiate with respect to time
$\frac{d L}{d t}=I \frac{d \omega}{d t}$
$\frac{d L}{d t}=\tau$ 
$\frac{d \omega}{d t}=\alpha$
$\tau $ = $ I\alpha$

Q11. For rolling motion without slipping the kinetic energy of the body is:
    (A) equal to the difference of kinetic energies of translation and rotation
    (B) equal to the sum of kinetic energies of translation and rotation   <-- CORRECT
    (C) equal to the kinetic energy of translation
    (D) equal to the kinetic energy of rotation
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Rolling motion without slipping involves both translation motion and rotation motion. Hence kinetic energy of the body in rolling motion is the sum of both translation kinetic energy and rotational kinetic energy.
K = K_trans + K_rot
 K = $ {1 \over 2}I{\omega ^2} + {1 \over 2}m{v^2} $

Q12. A solid sphere of mass M and radius R spins about an axis passing through its centre making 600 rpm. Its kinetic energy of rotation is:
    (A) 80$\pi$MR
    (B) $\frac{2}{5} {\pi^2}$MR
    (C) 80$\pi$^2MR^2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{2}{5} \pi \mathrm{M}^2 \mathrm{R}^2$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The kinetic energy of rotation
K =$\frac{1}{2} I \omega^2$ 
$n = \frac{600} {60} = 10$ revolution per second
angular velocity $\omega = 2\pi n $ = 2$\pi$ $\times$ 10 = 20 rad/sec
moment of inertia about an axis passing through centre of a solid sphere
$I =\frac {2}{ 5}M{R^2}$ 
The kinetic energy of rotation
$K=\frac{1}{2} I \omega^2=\frac{1}{2} \times \frac{2}{5} M R^2 \times(20 \pi)^2$ = 80$\pi$^2MR^2

Q13. A child swinging on a swing in a sitting position stands up. Then, the time period of the swing will:
    (A) Decrease   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Increase if the child is tall and decreases if the child is short
    (C) Remains the same
    (D) Increase
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As the child stand up then Centre of mass is shifted in upwards direction from the sitting position of the child, thus decreasing the effective length of the swing, so as the time period is proportional to the square root of length, thus time period decreases.
time period 
$T = 2\pi \sqrt {{l \over g}} $
$T \propto \sqrt l $
The time period of swing decreases as effective length decreases.

Q14. Angular momentum is:
    (A) A scalar
    (B) A plain
    (C) An axial-vector   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A polar vector
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The axial vector represents the rotational effect and is always along the axis of rotation. The direction of angular momentum always along the axis of rotation in accordance with the right-hand screw rule. Hence angular momentum is an axial vector.
$\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p$

Q15. Angular momentum of a body is defined as the product of:
    (A) Linear velocity and angular velocity
    (B) Moment of inertia and angular velocity   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Mass and angular velocity
    (D) Centripetal force and radius
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p$ 
if r is the perpendicular to P (in case of circular motion)
L = mvr
L = $ m\left( {r\omega } \right)r = m{r^2}\omega$
 L = $ I\omega$

Q1. The radius of gyration of a circular loop of radius r and mass m rotating about its diameter as the axis is:
    (A) $\frac{R}{2}$
    (B) $\frac{\sqrt2}{R}$
    (C) R
    (D) $\frac{R}{\sqrt2}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Moment of inertia of ring or circular loop about an axis passing through centre of mass and perpendicular to the plane is MR^2,
Applying perpendicular axis theorem 
I_z = I_x + I_y
MR^2 = I + I
I = $\frac {1}{2}M{R^2}$
Here I = Moment of inertia about an axis passing through diameter
A moment of inertia in terms of the radius of gyration (k) is Mk^2
I = Mk^2
$\frac{1}{2}$MR^2 = Mk^2
k = $\frac{R}{\sqrt2}$

Q2. In an orbital motion, the angular momentum vector is:
    (A) perpendicular to the orbital plane   <-- CORRECT
    (B) parallel to the linear momentum
    (C) along the radius vector
    (D) in the orbital plane
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p = m\left( {\vec r \times \vec v} \right)$ 
Hence the direction of angular momentum $\vec L$ is perpendicular to both $\vec r$ and $\vec v$ that is perpendicular to the orbital plane.

Q3. The moment of inertia of a circular disc of mass M and radius R rotating about an axis passing through its edge and perpendicular to the plane of the disc is:
    (A) MR^2
    (B) 2MR^2
    (C) $\frac{\mathrm{MR}^2}{2}$
    (D) $\frac{3 \mathrm{MR}^2}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Moment of inertia of a disc about an axis passing through Centre of mass and perpendicular to the plane
${I_{cm}} = \frac{1}{2}M{R^2}$}
if I = Moment of inertia of a disc about an axis passing through its edge and perpendicular to the plane
applying parallel axis theorem
I = I_cm + MR^2
I = $\frac{1}{2}$MR^2 + MR^2
I = $\frac{3}{2}$MR^2

Q4. A constant torque acting on a uniform circular wheel changes its angular momentum from A_0 to 4A_0 in 4 seconds. The magnitude of the torque is:
    (A) $\frac{4{\rm{A}}_0}{3}$
    (B) $\frac{3{\rm{A}}_0} {4}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 12 A_0
    (D) A_0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\tau=\frac{\Delta L}{\Delta t}=\frac{L_f-L_i}{\Delta t}$
L_f = 4A_0
L_i = A_0
$\Delta t $ = 4 sec
$\tau=\frac{4 A_0-A_0}{4}=\frac{3 A_0}{4}$

Q5. The moment of inertia of a circular ring about an axis passing through its centre and normal to its plane is 200 gm cm^2. Then its moment of inertia about diameter is:
    (A) 200 gm cm^2
    (B) 100 gm cm^2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 400 gm cm^2
    (D) 300 gm cm^2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: applying perpendicular axis theorem
I_z = I_x + Iy
I_z = 200
200 = I + I
2I = 200
I = 100
I = moment of inertia about an axis passing through diameter
I = 100 gm cm^2

Q6. A dancer on ice spins faster when she folds her hands. This is due to:
    (A) constant angular momentum and an increase in kinetic energy   <-- CORRECT
    (B) increase in energy and decrease in angular momentum
    (C) increase in energy and an increase in angular momentum
    (D) the decrease in friction at the skates
    Answer: A
    Explanation: L =$ I\omega $ 
if L = const.
then $I\omega $ = const.
When a dancer is spinning, she has a certain angular momentum. When the dancer folds her arms, the distance of all the points of her body decreases with respect to axis of rotation so that her moment of inertia decreases. Thus, in order to conserve angular momentum, the speed of rotation has to increase and hence the dancer spins faster.
$K = {{{L^2}} \over {2I}}$
$
 K \propto {1 \over I} $ 
Hence if the moment of inertia decrease then kinetic energy will increase.

Q7. A uniform rod of mass 2 kg is 1 meter long. Its radius of gyration about an axis through its one end and perpendicular to its length in SI units is:
    (A) $\frac{2}{3}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{\sqrt 3}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{1}{2\sqrt 3}$
    (D) $\frac{2}{ \sqrt 3}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Moment of inertia of the rod about an axis through its one end and perpendicular to its length
$I = \frac{M{L^2}}{3}$ 
M = 2 Kg
L = 1 m
Moment of inertia of rod in terms of the radius of gyration
I = Mk^2
$\frac{M{L^2}}{3} = M{k^2}$
$k=\sqrt{\frac{L^2}{3}}=\frac{L}{\sqrt{3}}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}$

Q8. Two discs of the same mass and same thickness t are made from two different materials of densities d_1 and d_2 respectively. The ratio of the moments of inertia of the two about an axis passing through the centre and perpendicular to the plane of the lamina is:
    (A) 1: d_1d_2
    (B) d_1 : d_2
    (C) d_2 : d_1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{\mathrm{d}_1}{\mathrm{~d}_2}$: 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: if V = volume of disc (At), A = area of disc = $\pi$r^2, t = thickness of disc, M = mass of disc, d = density of material of disc
$V = \frac{M}{d}$
At = $\frac{M}{d}$
$\pi r^{2} t=\frac{M}{d}$
$r^{2}=\frac{M}{\pi d_{1} t}$
r^2 $ \propto \frac{1}{d}$
$\left(\frac{r_{1}}{r_{2}}\right)^{2}=\frac{d_{2}}{d_{1}}$
$\frac{I_{1}}{I_{2}}=\frac{\frac{1}{2} M r_{1}^{2}}{\frac{1}{2} M r_{2}^{2}}=\left(\frac{r_{1}}{r_{2}}\right)^{2}=\frac{d_{2}}{d_{1}}$
I_1:I_2 = d_2:d_1

Q9. Four spheres each of mass M and radius R are placed with their centers on the four corners of a square of side 'b'. The moment of inertia of the system about any side of the square is:
    (A) $\frac{8}{5}{\rm{M}}{{\rm{R}}^{\rm{2}}}$ + Mb^2
    (B) $\frac{8}{5}{\rm{M}}{{\rm{R}}^{\rm{2}}}$ + 4Mb^2
    (C) $\frac{4}{3}{\rm{M}}{{\rm{R}}^{\rm{2}}}$ + 2Mb^2
    (D) $\frac{8}{5} $${\rm{M}}{{\rm{R}}^{\rm{2}}}$ + 2Mb^2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The moment of inertia of the system about any side of the square is
I = I_1 + I_2 + I_3 + I_4
I = $\frac {2}{5}M{R^2} + \frac{2}{5}M{R^2}$ + $\left(\frac{2}{5} M R^2+M b^2\right)$ + $\left(\frac{2}{5} M R^2+M b^2\right)$
I = $\frac{8}{5}$MR^2 + 2Mb^2

Q10. When a mass is rotating in a plane about a fixed point, its angular momentum is directed along:
    (A) the axis of rotation   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the radius
    (C) a line at an angle of 45^o to the plane of rotation
    (D) the tangent to the orbit
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\vec L = \vec r \times \vec p = m\left( {\vec r \times \vec v} \right)$ 
Hence the direction of the angular vector $\vec L$ is perpendicular to both $\vec r$ and $\vec v$ that is along the axis of rotation according to the right-hand screw rule.

Q11. A mass is revolving in a circle, which is in the plane of the paper. The direction of angular acceleration if any, is:
    (A) Towards the radius
    (B) Tangential
    (C) Upward from the plane of the paper
    (D) At right angles to the plane of the paper   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Angular acceleration is an axial vector. It is always directed along the axis of rotation according to the right-hand screw rule. Hence the direction of the angular acceleration vector is perpendicular to the plane in which the rotation takes place.

Q12. Which of the following has the largest moment of inertia?
    (A) Disc of mass M and radius R about an axis perpendicular to its plane
    (B) Ring of mass M and radius R about an axis perpendicular to its plane   <-- CORRECT
    (C) A solid sphere of mass M and radius R about an axis passing through its centre of mass
    (D) Bar magnet of mass M and length R about an axis passing through its centre of mass
    Answer: B
    Explanation: I_Ring = MR^2
I_disc = $1\over 2$MR^2
I_sphere = $2\over 5$MR^2
I_rod=$MR^2\over 12$
Hence the ring has the largest moment of inertia.

Q13. A spherical solid ball of 1 kg. mass and radius 3 cm is rotating about an axis passing through its centre with an angular velocity of 50 radians/s. The kinetic energy of rotation is
    (A) 920 J
    (B) 910 J
    (C) $9\over20$ J   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 45000 J
    Answer: C
    Explanation: M = 1Kg
R = 3cm = 3 $\times$ 10^-2m
$\omega$ = 50rad/s
K = $\frac{1}{2} I \omega^{2}=\frac{1}{2} \times \frac{2}{5} M R^{2} \times \omega^{2}$
K = $\frac12 \times\frac25$ $\times$1 $\times$(3 $\times$10^‚àí2)^2 $\times$50 $\times$50 = $9 \over {20}$J

Q14. A jet airplane travelling at the speed of 500 kmh^‚Äì1 ejects its products of combustion at the speed of 1500 km h^‚Äì1 relative to the jet plane. What is the speed of the combustion with respect to an observer on ground?
    (A) -1000 km/h   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -2550 km/h
    (C) -1250 km/h
    (D) -2000 km/h
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Speed of the jet airplane, v_jet = 500 km/h
Relative speed of its products of combustion with respect to the plane, v_smoke = ‚Äì 1500 km/h
Speed of its products of combustion with respect to the ground = v‚Ä≤_smoke
Relative speed of its products of combustion with respect to the airplane, v_smoke = v‚Ä≤_smoke ‚Äì v_jet
$\Rightarrow$ ‚Äì 1500 = v‚Ä≤_smoke ‚Äì 500
$\Rightarrow$ v‚Ä≤_smoke = ‚Äì 1000 km/h
The negative sign indicates that the direction of its products of combustion is opposite to the direction of motion of the jet airplane.

Q15. If a gymnast sitting on a rotating stool with his arms outstretched, suddenly lowers his hands:
    (A) His moment of inertia decreases   <-- CORRECT
    (B) The angular velocity decreases
    (C) The angular velocity stays constant
    (D) The angular momentum increases
    Answer: A
    Explanation: When gymnast lowers his hand the distance of the mass from rotational axis decrease. Hence his moment of inertia decreases and angular velocity increases to conserve angular momentum.

Q1. A planet is revolving around the sun in an elliptical orbit. The maximum and the minimum distances of the planet from the sun are 3 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{{\rm{12}}}}$ m and 2 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{{\rm{10}}}}$ m respectively. The speed of the planet when it is nearest to sun is 2 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{{\rm{7}}}}$ m/sec. What is the speed of the planet when it is farthest from the sun?
    (A) 2.66 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{{\rm{5}}}}$ m/sec
    (B) 1.33 $ \times $ 10^5 m/sec   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1.5 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{{\rm{7}}}}$ m/sec
    (D) 3 $ \times $ ${\rm{1}}{0^{{\rm{5}}}}$ m/sec
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Perihelion is the nearest distance of planet from focus.
aphelion is the farthest distance of planet from focus.
v_p = 2 $\times$ 10^7m/s
v_a = ?
r_p = 2 $\times$ 10^10m
r_a= 3 $\times$ 10^12m
$\frac{v_{p}}{v_{a}}=\frac{r_{a}}{r_{p}}$
$\frac{2 \times 10^{7}}{v_{a}}=\frac{3 \times 10^{12}}{2 \times 10^{10}}$
v_a = 1.33 $\times$ 10^5m/s

Q2. The angular velocity of the body changes from ${\omega _{\rm{1}}}$ to ${\omega _{\rm{2}}}$ without applying torque but by changing moment of inertia. The ratio of the initial radius of gyration to the final radius of gyration is:
    (A) ${\omega _{\rm{2}}}$: ${\omega _{\rm{1}}}$
    (B) ${\omega _{\rm{2}}}^{\rm{2}}$: ${\omega _{\rm{1}}}^2$
    (C) ($\sqrt{\omega _{\rm{2}}}$) : ($\sqrt{\omega _{\rm{1}}}$)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (${1 \over\omega _{\rm{2}}}$): ($1 \over{\omega _{\rm{1}}}$)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $I_{1} \omega_{1}$ = $I_{2} \omega_{2}$
$\frac{I_{1}}{I_{2}}=\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}$
$\frac{m k_{1}^{2}}{m k_{2}^{2}}=\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}$
$\frac{k_{1}}{k_{2}}=\sqrt{\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}}$
k_1:k_2 = $\sqrt{\omega _{\rm{2}}}$ : $\sqrt{\omega _{\rm{1}}}$

Q3. Two bodies with moments of inertia I_1 and I_2 (I_1$ > $ I_2) have equal angular momenta. If K.E. of rotation is E_1 and E_2 then:
    (A) E_1 < E_2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) E_1 = E_2
    (C) E_1 $\ge$ E_2
    (D) E_1 > E_2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: K.E. of rotation 
E = ${{{L^2}} \over {2I}}$
E $\propto$ $ {1 \over I}$
I_1 > I_2
E_1 < E_2

Q4. The moment of inertia of a thin uniform ring of mass 1 Kg about an axis passing through the centre and perpendicular to the plane of the ring is 0.25 Kg m^2. Then the diameter of the ring is:
    (A) 1 m   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.5 m
    (C) 0.25 m
    (D) 0.75 m
    Answer: A
    Explanation: I = MR^2
I = 0.25Kgm^2
M = 1Kg
$R=\sqrt{\frac{I}{M}}=\sqrt{\frac{0.25}{1}}$ = 0.5 m
Diameter d = 2R
d = 2 $\times$ 0.5 = 1 m

Q5. We have two spheres, one is a hollow shell and the other a solid. They have identical masses and moments of inertia about their respective diameters. The ratio of their radii is given by
    (A) $\sqrt3$ : $\sqrt5$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3: 5
    (C) $\sqrt3$ : $\sqrt7$
    (D) 5:7
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Moment of inertia of a hollow sphere about an axis passing through its diameter 
${I_{1}} = {2 \over 3}M{R_1}^2$ 
Moment of inertia of hollow shell about an axis passing through its diameter 
${I_{2}} = {2 \over 5}M{R_2}^2$
Given that 
I_1 = I_2
$\frac{2}{3} M R_{1}^{2}=\frac{2}{5} M R_{2}^{2}$
$\frac{R_{1}}{R_{2}}=\sqrt{\frac{3}{5}}$
R_1:R_2 = $\sqrt3$:$\sqrt5$

Q6. A particle performs uniform circular motion with an angular momentum L. If the frequency of particle's motion is doubled and its K.E. is halved, the angular momentum becomes:
    (A) 4L
    (B) $L\over2$
    (C) $L\over4$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2L
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $K=\frac{1}{2} I \omega^{2}=\frac{1}{2} \times I \omega \times \omega$
$K=\frac{1}{2} L \omega$
$\frac{K_{1}}{K_{2}}=\frac{L_{1} \omega_{1}}{L_{2} \omega_{2}}$ 
K_1 = K, K_2 = $K\over2$ 
n_1 = n, ${\omega _1} = 2\pi n = \omega $ 
n_2 = 2n, ${\omega _2} = 2\pi \times 2n = 2\omega $ 
L_1 = L, L_2 = ?
${{2K} \over K} = {{L\omega } \over {{L_2} \times 2\omega }}$
$L_{2}=\frac{L}{4}$

Q7. A flywheel at rest is to reach an angular velocity of 36 rad/sec, in 6 sec, with a constant angular acceleration. The total angle turned during this interval is:
    (A) 72 rad
    (B) 108 rad   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 216 rad
    (D) 144 rad
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\omega = {\omega _o} + \alpha t$
36 = 0 + 6$\alpha$ 
$\alpha = {{36} \over 6} = 6rad/{s^2}$
$\theta = {\omega _o}t + {1 \over 2}\alpha {t^2}$
$\theta$ = 0 + ${1 \over 2}$ $\times$ 6 $\times$ 6 $\times$ 6 
$\theta$ = 108rad

Q8. The radius of gyration of a rod of mass 100 gm and length 100 cm about an axis passing through its edge and perpendicular to its length is given by:
    (A) $\frac{50} {{3\sqrt 2 }}$
    (B) $\frac{50}{ {2\sqrt 3 }}$
    (C) $\frac{100} {{3\sqrt 3 }}$
    (D) $\frac{100} {{\sqrt 3 }}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Moment of inertia of the rod about an axis passing through its centre of gravity and perpendicular to its length
$I = \frac{M{l^2}} {{3}}$ 
Moment of inertia of rod in terms of the radius of gyration 
I = Mk^2
M = 100 gm
l = 100 cm
Mk^2 = $\frac{Ml^2}{3}$
$k=\sqrt{\frac{l^{2}}{3}}=\sqrt{\frac{100 \times 100}{3}}$
$k=\frac{100}{\sqrt{3}} \mathrm{cm}$

Q9. The M.I. of a body about a given axis is 1.2 kg m^2. Initially, the body is at rest. In order to produce rotational kinetic energy of 1500 joule, the angular acceleration of 25 rad/sec^2 must be applied about that axis for the duration of
    (A) 4 sec
    (B) 8 sec
    (C) 10 sec
    (D) 2 sec   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: K = 1500 J
I = 1.2 Kgm^2
$\alpha $ = 25rad/s^2
$\Delta$t = ?
$K=\frac{1}{2} I \omega^{2}$
$\omega=\sqrt{\frac{2 K}{I}}=\sqrt{\frac{2 \times 1500}{1.2}}$ = 50rad/s
$\alpha = {{\Delta \omega } \over {\Delta t}} = {{\omega - {\omega _o}} \over {\Delta t}} = {{50 - 0} \over {\Delta t}}$
25 = $ {{50 - 0} \over {\Delta t}}$ 
$ \Delta t = {{50} \over {25}} $ = 2 sec

Q10. A fan of the moment of inertia 0.3 kg m^2 is to run up to working speed of 0.5 revolutions per second. Indicate the correct value of the angular momentum of the fan:
    (A) 3 kg $ \times $ m^2/sec
    (B) 6 kg $ \times $ m^2/sec
    (C) 0.3$\pi $kg $ \times $ m^2/sec   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{\pi}{6}$ kg $ \times $ m^2/sec
    Answer: C
    Explanation: n = 0.5 revolution per second
angular velocity $\omega = 2\pi n = 2\pi \times 0.5 $ = $\pi $ rad/s
moment of inertia I = 0.3Kgm^2
angular momentum L= I$\omega$ = 0.3 $\times$ $\pi$ = 0.3$\pi$Kgm^2/s

Q11. Three thin uniform rods each of mass M and length L are placed along the three-axis of a Cartesian coordinate system with one end of each rod at the origin. The Moment of inertia of the system about the z-axis is:
    (A) $\frac{\mathrm{ML}^2}{3}$
    (B) ML^2
    (C) $\frac{2 \mathrm{ML}^2}{3}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{\mathrm{ML}^2}{6}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Moment of inertia about an axis passing through the edge
$I =\frac{M{L^2}} {3}$ 
Moment of inertia of the system about z-axis
I = I_x + I_y + I_z
$I=\frac{M L^{2}}{3}+\frac{M L^{2}}{3}+0$
$I=\frac{2}{3} M L^{2}$

Q12. Two circular rings have their masses in the ratio 1:2 and their diameters in the ratio 2: 1. The ratio of their moments of inertia about their axes is:
    (A) 1: 4
    (B) 1:2
    (C) 4:1
    (D) 2:1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\frac{M_{1}}{M_{2}}=\frac{1}{2}$
$\frac{R_{1}}{R_{2}}=\frac{2}{1}$
$\frac{I_{1}}{I_{2}}=\frac{M_{1} R_{1}^{2}}{M_{2} R_{2}^{2}}$
$\frac{I_{1}}{I_{2}}=\left(\frac{M_{1}}{M_{2}}\right)\left(\frac{R_{1}}{R_{2}}\right)^{2}$ = $\frac{1}{2} \times\left(\frac{2}{1}\right)^{2}$ = $\frac{1}{2} \times \frac{4}{1}=\frac{2}{1}$
I_1:I_2 = 2:1

Q13. Four masses are fixed on a massless rod as shown in the figure. The moment of inertia about the axis P is about
    (A) 2 kg metre^2
    (B) 1.04 kg metre^2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0.5 kg metre^2
    (D) 0.3 kg ${\rm{metr}}{{\rm{e}}^{\rm{2}}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: I = I_1 + I_2 + I_3 + I_4
I = $m_{1} r_{1}^{2}+m_{2} r_{2}^{2}+m_{3} r_{3}^{2}+m_{4} r_{4}^{2}$
I = (2 $\times$ 0.4 $\times$ 0.4)+(5 $\times$0.2 $\times$0.2)+(5 $\times$0.2 $\times$ 0.2)+(2 $\times$ 0.4 $\times$ 0.4)
I = 0.32 + 0.20 + 0.20 + 0.32
I = 1.04 K gm^2

Q14. A wheel is rotating about an axis through its centre at 720 r.p.m. When acted upon by a constant torque opposing its motion for 8 seconds it stops rotating. The value of this torque in Nm is (given I = $\frac {24} {\pi }$ kg ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$)
    (A) 48
    (B) 96
    (C) 120
    (D) 72   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $n = \frac {720} {60} = 12$ rev/s
angular velocity $\omega = 2\pi n $ = $ 2\pi \times 12 = 24\pi $ rad/s
moment of inertia 
I =$\frac {24}{ \pi }$kg ${{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$
torque
$T = I\alpha $
T = $ I\frac{{\Delta \omega }}{{\Delta t}} = \frac{{24}}{\pi } \times \left( {\frac{{24 \pi- 0}}{8}} \right)$ = $ \frac{{24}}{\pi } \times \frac{{24\pi }}{8}$ = 72.0Nm

Q15. A flywheel rotating about a fixed axis has a kinetic energy of 360 joules when its angular speed is 30 radians per second. The moment of inertia of the flywheel about the axis of rotation is:
    (A) 0.8 kg m^2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0.75 kg m^2
    (C) 0.6 kg m^2
    (D) 0.15 kg m^2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: K = ${1\over 2}I \omega^2$
K = 360J
$\omega $ = 30rad/s
I = $ {{2K} \over {{\omega ^2}}} = {{2 \times 360} \over {30 \times 30}} $0 = 0.8Kgm^2

Q1. A body of mass 2.0 kg and radius of gyration 0.5 m is rotating about an axis. If its angular speed is 2.0 rad/s, the angular momentum of the body (in kg - m^2/s) is:
    (A) 0.5
    (B) 1.5
    (C) 1.0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2.0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Moment of inertia
I = mk^2
m = 2 Kg
k = 0.5 m
I = 2 $\times$ 0.5 $\times$ 0.5 = 0.5Kgm^2
angular momentum
L = I$\omega$
$\omega$ = 2rad/s
L = 0.5 $\times$ 2 = 1.0Kgm^2/s

Q2. The angular velocity of a body changes from 1 rev/sec to 25 rev/sec. without applying any external torque. The ratio of the radii of gyration in the two cases is:
    (A) 5:1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1: 5
    (C) 1: 25
    (D) 25:1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: I_1$\omega$_1 = I_2$\omega$_2
$\frac{I_{1}}{I_{2}}=\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}$ 
$\omega$_1 = 1rev/s
$\omega$_2 = 25rev/s
if the radius of gyration is k_1 and k_2 then 
$\frac{M k_{1}^{2}}{M k_{2}^{2}}=\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}$
$\frac{k_{1}}{k_{2}}=\sqrt{\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}}=\sqrt{\frac{25}{1}}=\frac{5}{1}$
k_1:k_2 = 5:1

Q3. The angular velocity of a body changes forms 1 rev/sec to 16 rev/sec. Without applying any external torque. The ratio of its radius of gyration in the two cases is:
    (A) 1:16
    (B) 1:4
    (C) 4: 1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 16:1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: I_1$\omega$_1 = I_2$\omega$_2
$\frac{I_{1}}{I_{2}}=\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}$ 
$\omega$_1 = 1rev/s
$\omega$_2 = 16rev/s
if the radius of gyration is k_1 and k_2 then 
$\frac{M k_{1}^{2}}{M k_{2}^{2}}=\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}$
$\frac{k_{1}}{k_{2}}=\sqrt{\frac{\omega_{2}}{\omega_{1}}}=\sqrt{\frac{16}{1}}=\frac{4}{1}$
k_1:k_2 = 4:1

Q4. A body having a moment of inertia about its axis equal to 3 kg m^2 is rotating with an angular velocity equal to 3 rad/s. The kinetic energy of this rotating body is the same as that of a body of mass 27 kg moving with a speed of
    (A) 2.0 m/s
    (B) 1.5 m/s
    (C) 1.0 m/s   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0.5 m/s
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $K_{r o t}=\frac{1}{2} I \omega^{2}$
$K_{t r a n s}=\frac{1}{2} m v^{2}$
given that
K_rot = K_trans
$\frac{1}{2} I \omega^{2}=\frac{1}{2} m v^{2}$
I = 3Kgm^2
$\omega$ = 3rad/s
m = 27Kg
v =?
$I \omega^{2}$ = mv^2
v =$ \sqrt {{{I{\omega ^2}} \over m}} = \sqrt {{{3 \times 3 \times 3} \over {27}}} $ = 1.0m/s

Q5. The moment of inertia of a solid sphere about a diameter is 8000 gms ${\rm{c}}{{\rm{m}}^{\rm{2}}}$ (mass of sphere = 50 gm, radius = 20 cm). The moment of inertia about a tangent will be
    (A) 2.8 $ \times $ 10^4 gm cm^2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 8400 gm cm^2
    (C) 280 gm cm^2
    (D) 2.8 10^3 gm
    Answer: A
    Explanation: I = $2\over 5$MR^2 = 8000 gm cm^2, using the parallel axis theorem the Moment of Inertia about a tangent to the sphere is = $2\over 5$ MR^2+ MR^2 = $7\over 5$ MR^2 = 2.8 $ \times $ 10^4 gm cm^2

Q6. A particle moves with a constant velocity parallel to the x-axis. Its angular momentum with respect to the origin:
    (A) goes on increasing
    (B) is zero
    (C) remains constant   <-- CORRECT
    (D) goes on decreasing
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As angular momentum is $\vec L = \vec p \times \vec r $ = mvrsin$\theta$, Now rsinŒ∏ = perpendicular distance from x-axis which is constant, so angular momentum remains constant.

Q7. If the radius of earth contracts to half of its present value, the mass remaining unchanged, the duration of the day will be:
    (A) 6 Hrs   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 12 Hrs
    (C) 24 Hrs
    (D) 48 Hrs
    Answer: A
    Explanation: As the Moment of inertia of earth considered as the sphere is I = $2\over 5$ MR^2, thus according to the law of conservation of angular momentum as the radius contracts to half, thus a new moment of inertia of earth will be $I\over 4$, thus the angular velocity will increase 4 times and making the length of the day to 6 hrs.

Q8. A boy comes running and sits on a merry-go-round. What is conserved?
    (A) Angular momentum   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Linear momentum
    (C) The kinetic energy of function
    (D) The kinetic energy of rotation
    Answer: A
    Explanation: According to the law of conservation of angular momentum if no external torque is applied on a body in rotation than its angular momentum remains conserved.

Q9. A ring of radius r and mass m rotates about its central axis. The kinetic energy is:
    (A) $\frac{\mathrm{mr}^2 \omega^2}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{mr{\omega ^2}}{2}$
    (C) mr ${\omega ^2}$
    (D) mr^2 ${\omega ^2}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The kinetic energy of the body in rotational motion is $KE = \frac{1}{2}I{\omega ^2} = \frac{1}{ 2}m{r^2}{\omega ^2}$ as a moment of inertia of ring about its central axis is I = mr^2.

Q10. A thin circular ring of mass M and radius R is rotating about its central axis with angular velocity. Four-point objects each of mass m are attached gently to the opposite ends of two perpendicular diameters, the angular velocity of the ring is given by:
    (A) $\frac{M}{{M + 4m}} \cdot \omega $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{M}{{M + m}} \cdot \omega $
    (C) $\frac{M-4 m}{M+4 m} \cdot \omega$
    (D) $\frac{{M + 4m}} {M} \cdot \omega $
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let $\omega$ be the angular velocity of the Ring of Mass M, thus the moment of inertia about a given axis is I_1 = $MR^2$ and the four-point objects are gently placed at perpendicular diameters at the opposite end, so, the distance of each object from the axis of rotation is R, so total moment of inertia of the ring and four objects is I_2 = $MR^2 + 4mR^2$. 
According to the law of conservation of angular momentum I_1 $\omega$ = I_2$\omega$_2 , So on solving $\omega_2=\left(\frac{M R^2}{M R^2+4 m R^2}\right) \omega=\frac{M}{M+4 m} \cdot \omega$

Q11. What is the moment of inertia of a thin rod of length L and mass M about an axis passing through one end and perpendicular to its length?
    (A) $\frac{1}{12}$ ML^2
    (B) $\frac{1}{2}$ML^2
    (C) $\frac{1}{3}$ ML^2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ML^2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Using theorem of the parallel axis, the axis is shifted by $\frac{L}{2}$ distance from the centre of Mass where the Moment of Inertia is $\frac{M L^2}{12}$, thus the moment of inertia of a thin rod about an axis passing through one end and perpendicular to its length is $\frac{M L^2}{12}+\frac{M L^2}{4}=\frac{1}{3} M L^2$

Q12. The radius of gyration of a solid disc about one of its diameter is given by:
    (A) $\frac{R}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2R
    (C) $\sqrt {2} $R
    (D) $\frac{R}{{\sqrt 2 }}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Moment of inertia of an axis passing through its center and perpendicular to its plane:
I = $\frac{1}{2}$ MR^2
Using perpendicular axis theorem Ix +Iy = Iz, so 2I_d = $\frac{1}{2}$ MR^2
Moment of inertia of along its diameter I_d = $\frac{1}{4}$MR^2
And the radius of gyration MK^2 = $\frac{1}{4}$MR^2 
K = $\frac{R}{2}$

Q13. The moment of inertia of a solid sphere of density $\rho $ and radius R is given by:
    (A) $\frac{176} {{105}}\rho {R^2}$
    (B) $\frac{176}{{105}}\rho {R^5}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{176}{{105}}\rho {R^3}$
    (D) $\frac{105}{{176}}\rho {R^2}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $I=\frac{2}{5}\left(M R^{2}\right)$
$=\frac{2}{5}\left[\left(\frac{4}{3} \pi R^{3}\right) \cdot \rho . R^{2}\right]$
$=\frac{2}{5}\left[\left(\frac{4}{3} \frac{22}{7} R^{3}\right) \cdot \rho . R^{2}\right]$ 
As Mass = Density $\times $ Volume of Sphere 
$=\frac{176}{{105}}\rho {R^5}$

Q14. A thin uniform rod of length 2l and mass M is acted upon a constant torque. The angular velocity changes from zero to $\omega $ in time t. The value of torque is:
    (A) $\frac{M{l^2}\omega } {t}$
    (B) $\frac{M{l^2}\omega }{{12t}}$
    (C) $\frac{2M{l^2}\omega } {{3t}}$
    (D) $\frac{M{l^2}\omega }{{3t}}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As Torque($\tau $) is equal to the product of Moment of Inertia (I) and Angular acceleration $\left( \alpha \right)$
$\tau=I \alpha$
 $\tau=I \frac{\Delta \omega}{\Delta t}$
$\tau=\left[\frac{M(2 l)^{2}}{12}\right]\left[\frac{\omega}{t}\right]$
$\tau=\frac{M l^{2} \omega}{3 t}$

Q15. A particle is orbiting in a vertical plane. Its linear momentum will be directed:
    (A) Horizontally
    (B) Vertically
    (C) Tangential to the orbit   <-- CORRECT
    (D) At 45$^\circ $ to the vertical
    Answer: C
    Explanation: As the direction of velocity at any point moving in a circular orbit is tangent at that point, thus momentum would be tangential to the orbit.

Gravitation Test 01  (id 562) [FREE]
